Interpolation in Classical Texts: Historical Precedents
Responding to objection about interpolation by citing historical precedents

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify instances of interpolation (idrāj) in Islamic scholarly texts and evaluate the evidence for such claims using historical precedents from Hanafi tradition.

Core Idea
Interpolation in authoritative texts is historically attested; even respected Hanafi works have undergone additions.

In this passage, the commentator defends the possibility that an example in Mukhtasar al-Ma'ani is interpolated. He anticipates the objection that such insertion could not occur and counters with multiple precedents from Islamic history, including hadith collections and works of major scholars. Understanding this argument strengthens your ability to critically assess textual authenticity in usul al-fiqh.

Guided Path
1
Identify the objection
The author responds to an implicit objection: how could interpolation occur in a respected work like Mukhtasar al-Ma'ani?
2
Note the textual evidence
The author points out that the disputed example is absent in the longer work al-Mutawwal but present in Mukhtasar al-Ma'ani, indicating insertion.
3
Examine the supporting precedents
The author lists historical cases of interpolation: hadith books when not preserved, books of Shaykh Abd al-Qadir al-Jilani, and Shah Ismail Shahid's Siraat-e-Mustaqim.
4
Evaluate the rational argument
Assess the strength of using historical precedent to prove the possibility of interpolation in a specific text.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
الترويج لحل التَّوْضِيح والتنويج نہیں کہ وہ مختصر المعانی میں بھی ہو بخلا اس مقام کے یہاں معاملہ برعکس ہے مطول میں تو یہ مثال موجود نہیں مختصر میں موجود ہے معلوم ہوا کہ یہ مثال مدرج ہے۔ باقی رہا یہ سوال کہ اوراج کیسے ہو گیا تو اس کی کئی نظائر اور مثالیں موجود ہیں جب کتب احادیث محفوظ نہ رہیں پیران پیر شیخ عبد القادر جیلانی کی کتب میں ادراج والحاق ہوا قریب زمانہ میں شاہ اسماعیل شہید رحمہ اللہ کی کتاب صراط مستقیم میں غالیوں کی طرف سے عبارتوں کے اضافے کئے گئے تو مختصر المعانی میں ادراج کیوں نہیں ہو سکتا۔
Al-Tarwīḥ li-Ḥall al-Tawḍīḥ wa al-Talwīḥ: It is not that it is also in Mukhtasar al-Ma'ani; contrary to this place, the matter is reversed. In al-Muṭawwal, this example is not present; in al-Mukhtaṣar, it is present. It became known that this example is interpolated. Remaining is this question: how did interpolation occur? So many precedents and examples exist for this: when the hadith books were not preserved, in the books of Pirān Pīr Shaykh ‘Abd al-Qādir al-Jīlānī, interpolation and addition occurred; recently, in Shāh Ismā‘īl Shahīd’s book Ṣirāṭ-e Mustaqīm, additions were made by extremists. So why can interpolation not occur in Mukhtasar al-Ma‘ānī?
Source pages p. 58

Commentary
This passage addresses an objection regarding the presence of a particular example in Mukhtasar al-Ma‘ānī. The author argues that the example is indeed interpolated (mudraj) and not original. He supports this by noting that in al-Muṭawwal (a longer work) the example is absent, while it appears in Mukhtasar al-Ma‘ānī, indicating insertion. He then anticipates the question of how interpolation could occur, and provides historical precedents: the books of Shaykh ‘Abd al-Qādir al-Jīlānī were subject to interpolation, and even the recent work Ṣirāṭ-e Mustaqīm by Shāh Ismā‘īl Shahīd had additions by extremists. Therefore, interpolation in Mukhtasar al-Ma‘ānī is plausible.

Key Terms
ادراج (idrāj): Interpolation or insertion of foreign material into a text.
الحاق (ilḥāq): Addition or annexation, often used synonymously with idrāj in this context.
نظائر (naẓā'ir): Precedents or analogous cases used as evidence.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What example does the author give to show that interpolation has occurred in Islamic books?
A) The books of Imam Bukhari
B) The books of Shaykh Abd al-Qadir al-Jilani
C) The Qur'an
D) The works of Imam Abu Hanifa

Key Takeaway
Interpolation in classical texts is not only possible but historically documented, requiring scholars to critically verify attributions.

Grammatical Analysis of 'Muʿāwinan Ẓahīran'
Analyzing the grammatical structure of a phrase in a Hanafi usul text.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify the two possible grammatical analyses of the phrase 'muʿāwinan ẓahīran' and explain the use of taḍmīn to justify a second object.

Core Idea
A verb's transitivity can shift through taḍmīn — a key tool for parsing legal texts.

In this passage, the commentator explores the grammar of a two-word phrase from a key Hanafi usul text. The analysis reveals two possibilities: a circumstantial accusative or a second object. Resolving the tension requires understanding taḍmīn, a device where a verb carries another's meaning.

Guided Path
1
Identify the phrase and its context
Locate the phrase 'muʿāwinan ẓahīran' in the original text and note the verb 'arsala' it relates to.
2
Recognize the two grammatical possibilities
The phrase can be parsed as a circumstantial accusative (ḥāl) from the pronoun of 'arsalahu', or as a second object (mafʿūl thānī) for 'arsalahu'.
Each parsing changes the grammatical relationship.
3
Analyze the transitivity question
The verb 'arsala' normally takes only one object, so how can it take a second? This leads to the invocation of taḍmīn.
4
Understand taḍmīn as a solution
'Arsala' is used in the sense of 'jaʿala' (to make), which is transitive with two objects. This allows the second object parsing.
Taḍmīn is a common grammatical device in classical Arabic.
5
Evaluate the rhetorical order
The passage also questions why 'muʿāwinan' (greater hyperbole) appears after 'ẓahīran' (lesser hyperbole) when eloquence suggests the opposite. This shows the author's attention to stylistic precision.
This discussion reinforces the grammatical analysis.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ترکیبی تحقیق : معوانا ظهيرا اس کی ترکیب میں دو احتمال ہیں اول ارسلہ کی ضمیر سے حال ہوں ثانی ارسلہ کے لئے مفعول ثانی ہوں ۔ سوال: دوسرے احتمال پر سوال ہو گا کہ ارسلہ میں فعل ارسل متعدی بیک مفعول ہوتا ہے تو یہ مفعول ثانی کیسے بن گیا؟ جواب: یہاں تضمین ہوتی ہے کہ ارسل جعل کے معنی میں ہے اور جعل متعدی بدو مفعول ہے اور اس اعتبار سے یہ مفعول ثانی بن سکتے ہیں۔ سوال : معو انا کا معنی ہے کثیر المعومیہ اور ظہیر کا معنی ہے غالب تو معوانا میں مبالغہ زیادہ ہے بنسبت ظہیر ا کے تو فصاحت کا تقاضا یہ تھا کہ پہلے اس لفظ کو ذکر کرتے جس میں کم درجہ کا مبالغہ پایا جاتا ہے پھر اس لفظ کو ذکر کرتے جس میں مبالغہ زیادہ پایا
Grammatical analysis: 'Muʿāwinan Ẓahīran'. There are two possibilities in its parsing: first, it could be a circumstantial accusative (ḥāl) from the pronoun of 'arsalahu'; second, it could be a second object (mafʿūl thānī) for 'arsalahu'. Question: In the second probability, there is a question: since the verb 'arsala' is transitive with one object, how can it take a second object? Answer: Here there is inclusion (taḍmīn) that 'arsala' has the meaning of 'jaʿala' (to make), and 'jaʿala' is transitive with two objects, so based on that it can be a second object. Question: 'Muʿāwinan' means 'one who provides great help' and 'Ẓahīran' means 'dominant', so 'muʿāwinan' has a higher degree of hyperbole compared to 'ẓahīran'. The requirement of eloquence would be to mention the word with lesser hyperbole first, then the word with greater hyperbole.
Source pages p. 68

Commentary
This passage engages in detailed grammatical analysis (tarkībī taḥqīq) of the phrase 'muʿāwinan ẓahīran' found in the text. Two parsing options are presented: as a circumstantial adverb (ḥāl) or as a second object (mafʿūl thānī). The question about the second object is answered by noting that the verb 'arsala' is used here in the sense of 'jaʿala' (to make), which takes two objects—a common technique in Arabic grammar called taḍmīn (inclusion). Finally, a question about the order of the two words in terms of eloquence is raised: since 'muʿāwinan' has a higher degree of hyperbole (mubālagha) than 'ẓahīran', the expected order would place the lesser first. This shows the text's careful attention to rhetorical and grammatical precision.

Key Terms
ترکیبی تحقیق (tarkībī taḥqīq): Grammatical analysis; examining the syntactic composition of a phrase.
مفعول ثانی (mafʿūl thānī): Second object of a transitive verb that takes two objects.
تضمین (taḍmīn): Inclusion; using a verb in a sense that incorporates the meaning of another verb to change its transitivity.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What is the condition for 'muʿāwinan' to be parsed as a second object?
A) If 'arsala' is used in its literal meaning
B) If 'arsala' is used in the sense of 'jaʿala'
C) If it is a circumstantial accusative
D) If 'muʿāwinan' is a direct object

Key Takeaway
The grammatical analysis of legal texts often requires understanding taḍmīn to correctly parse phrases that otherwise defy standard transitivity rules.

Commentary on the Word 'Zahir' and the Companions: A Hanafi Textual Analysis
Explains the hyperbolic form 'ظہیر' and the reference to Muhajirun and Ansar

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to analyze the linguistic and rhetorical features of a classical usul text and apply the Hanafi method of resolving apparent contradictions using analogy and contextual interpretation.

Core Idea
The word 'zahir' is more emphatic than 'mu'in' due to its hyperbolic form and continuous meaning, as shown by three scholarly answers.

In this lesson, we examine a passage from a Hanafi commentary on a usul matn. The commentator faces a potential objection: why is the word 'ظہیر' (zahir) placed after 'معوان' (mu'in) if it appears weaker? He provides three answers, demonstrating how Hanafi scholars use linguistic analysis, analogy, and contextual reasoning to resolve such issues. We will also explore the treatment of the Companions and the use of metaphors in the text.

Guided Path
1
Identify the objection
State the apparent problem: 'ظہیر' (zahir) seems to be placed after 'معوان' (mu'in) in the text, implying a descent from higher to lower, which contradicts the expected progression. The commentator must justify this.
The objection is based on the assumption that later words should be stronger than earlier ones.
2
Analyze the first answer
The commentator claims that 'ظہیر' is a hyperbolic adjective (صفت مشبہ) implying continuous support, thus stronger. Note the objection that صفت مشبہ is usually intransitive, but it is analogized to 'نصیر' (nasir). Consider the counter-critique that 'نصیر' is actually an active participle, not a descriptive adjective.
This answer relies on the classification of 'ظہیر' as صفت مشبہ to derive the meaning of continuity.
3
Consider the second answer
The arrangement is not for progression but for completion (تمیم). First, a meaning is mentioned with exaggeration, then the leftover meaning is expressed. This addresses the progression issue.
This answer focuses on rhetorical structure rather than linguistic form.
4
Consider the third answer
'ظہیر' may derive from 'ظہیر القوم' (one completely relied upon), making it even more emphatic. Evaluate which answer is most convincing.
This answer provides a separate etymological origin.
5
Understand the Companions and metaphors
The text says 'من المهاجرين والأنصار' refers to all Companions, with special mention for honor. 'والذين اتبعوهم' refers to the Tabi'un, not connected to the earlier groups. Then the metaphors (sciences as sea, waves, roaring) enhance the description.
The separation of Tabi'un from Companions is important for usul: the three methods (ijtihad, istishab, istihsan) are specific to the Companions.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
جاتا ہے۔ تا کہ ادنی سے اعلی کی طرف ترقی ہو حالانکہ یہاں پر اعلی سے ادنی کی طرف تنزلی ہے جو صحیح نہیں ہے۔ جواب (۱):۔ کہ ظہیر صفت مشبہ کا صیغہ ہے اور اس میں دوام والا معنی پایا جاتا ہے اس کا معنی ہوگا دائم المعونہ یعنی ہمیشہ مدد کرنے والا تو اس میں معوان سے زیادہ مبالغہ ہے فلا اشکال عالیہ لیکن اس پر سوال:۔ سوال ہوگا کہ صفت مشبہ تو لازم ہوتا ہے اور اس صورت میں اس کا متعدی ہونا لازم آئے گا۔ جواب:۔ اس کو لفظ نصیر پر قیاس کیا گیا ہے جس طرح وہ صفت مشبہ ہے لیکن اس کے باوجو د متعدی ہے کیونکہ اس کا معنی ہے مدد کرنے والا ، اسی طرح یہ صفت مشبہ ہونے کے باوجود متعدی ہے لیکن یہ درست نہیں کیونکہ محققین حضرات کے نزدیک نصیر اسم فاعل ہے صفت مشبہ نہیں ۔ جواب (۲):۔ ٹھیک ہے کہ ظہیر میں مبالغہ کم ہے لیکن مصنف نے مجمع کی رعایت کرتے ہوئے ظہیر کو موخر کیا ہے خلاصہ ہے ہے کہ یہ ترقی کے قبیل سے نہیں ہے بلکہ تمیم کے قبیل سے ہے کہ پہلے ایک معنی کو مبالغہ کے ساتھ ذکر کر دیا پھر بچے کھچے مفہوم کو دوسرے لفظ سے بیان کر دیا۔ جواب (۳):۔ یہ بھی تو ہو سکتا ہے کہ یہ ظہیر القوم سے لیا گیا ہو اور ظہیر القوم اس کو کہتے ہیں کہ جو قوم کا کلی طور پر معتمد علیہ ہو تو اس صورت میں ظہیر میں مبالغہ معوان سے زیادہ ہوگا۔ قوله من المهاجرين والانصار : يا اتم کا بیان ہے اس سے مراد سب صحابہ کرام ہیں لیکن زیادہ شرافت کیوجہ سے ذکر صرف مہاجرین اور انصار کا کیا۔ والذین اتبعو ہم اس کا عطف وانتم پر ہے اس سے مراد تا بعین ہیں مہاجرین والا نصار پر اس کا عطف نہیں ہوسکتا کیونکہ پیچھے تین چیزین ذکر ہوئیں (۱) اغتنام (۲) استصحاب (۳) استحسان یہ تین چیزیں صحابہ کرام کو حاصل ہیں باقیوں کو حاصل نہیں ۔ مرادی تحقیق : حتی صادفت حتی غایت کے لئے ہے اور صادفت نتیجہ ہے اوقد کا اور رایت الناس نتیجہ ہے اوضح کا، خلاصہ یہ ہے کہ جب علوم نظریہ اور علوم عملیہ کو حاصل کرنے کے لئے کامل النور چراغ (محمد ہے ) پایا گیا تو علوم اتنے کثیر ہو گئے کہ گویا ٹھاٹھیں مارتے سمندر ہیں اور جب لوگوں کو واضح راستہ مل گیا اور اس پر چلنے سے کسی قسم کی رکاوٹ نہ رہی تو لوگ فوج در فوج اس پر چلنے لگے۔ استعارات :- شاری نے علوم کو تشبیہ دی ہے دریا سے ذکر مشبہ کا اور مراد بھی مشبہ ہے تو علوم میں استعارہ مکیہ ہے اور دریا کے لوازمات میں سے موجوں کا ہونا ہے تو امواج میں استعارہ تخیلیہ ہے اور دریا کے مناسبات میں سے ٹھاٹھیں مارتا ہے تو تتلاطم میں استعارہ ترشیجیہ ہے۔ لساطع الحجہ : یہ جار مجرور مل کر معوانا کے متعلق ہیں ساطع الحجۂ اضافت المصفت الى الموصوف کی قبیل سے ہے دراصل تھا الحجہ الساطعة فائدہ:۔ مصنف نے خطبہ کے ابتدائی حصہ میں براعت استملال کی طرف اشارہ کیا کہ میری کتاب میں ادلہ اربعہ یعنی کتاب اللہ، سنت رسول اللہ اللہ، اجماع اور قیاس اصول و فروع ، احکام ، خطاب مقتضی انص، اشارة النص ، دلالة النص ، تواتر ، ظاہر، استحسان و استصحاب وغیرہ سے بحث ہوگی جو کہ اصول فقہ کی اصطلاحات ہیں۔
It goes. So that there is progression from lower to higher, whereas here it is descent from higher to lower, which is not correct. Answer (1): That 'zahir' is the form of a descriptive adjective, and it contains the meaning of continuity. Its meaning will be 'always helping', so it has more exaggeration than 'mu'in', so no problem. But there is a question: The descriptive adjective is transitive? So it would require being transitive. Answer: It is analogized to the word 'nasir'; just as that is a descriptive adjective but nevertheless transitive because it means 'helper', similarly this is a descriptive adjective but transitive. But this is not correct because according to the verifying scholars, 'nasir' is a noun of agent, not a descriptive adjective. Answer (2): It is correct that 'zahir' has less exaggeration, but the author, observing the context, placed 'zahir' later. The summary is that this is not of the type of progression but of the type of completion, that first one meaning is mentioned with exaggeration, then the leftover meaning is expressed with another word. Answer (3): It could also be that this is taken from 'zahir al-qawm', and 'zahir al-qawm' is called one who is completely relied upon by the people. In that case, 'zahir' has more exaggeration than 'mu'in'. His saying: 'from the Muhajirun and the Ansar' is a statement of completion; by this he means all the Companions, but due to greater honor, he mentioned only the Muhajirun and Ansar. 'And those who follow them' is connected to 'you' (؟); by this he means the Tabi'un. It cannot be connected to 'Muhajirun and Ansar' because three things were mentioned earlier: (1) ijtihad, (2) istishab, (3) istihsan. These three things are possessed by the Companions, not by others. Research of meaning: 'hatta' is for limit, 'sadafat' is the result of 'awqada', and 'ra'aytu al-nas' is the result of 'awdaha'. The summary is that when the lamp of complete light (Muhammad) was found for acquiring theoretical and practical sciences, the sciences became so abundant that they are like roaring seas. And when people found a clear path and no obstacle remained in following it, people began to follow it in throngs. Metaphors: The commentator likened sciences to a sea; the mention of the compared is and the intended is also the compared, so in 'sciences' there is a primary metaphor, and among the sea's accessories is the existence of waves, so in 'waves' there is a imaginary metaphor, and among the sea's correspondences is that it roars, so in 'roaring' there is a secondary metaphor. 'Li-sati' al-hujja': This prepositional phrase is connected to 'mu'inan'; 'sati' al-hujja' is of the type of adding the described to the description; originally it was 'al-hujja al-sati'a'. Benefit: The author indicated in the initial part of the sermon a good opening, that my book will discuss the four proofs: the Book of Allah, the Sunnah of the Messenger of Allah, consensus, and analogy, as well as principles and branches, rulings, explicit meaning, implied meaning, textual indication, tawatur, zahir, istihsan, istishab, etc., which are the terminologies of Usul al-Fiqh.
Source pages p. 69

Commentary
This passage is a commentary on the matn's khutba, specifically on the praise of the Companions and the author's use of the word 'ظہیر' (zahir) meaning 'helper'. The commentator addresses a potential criticism: why is 'ظہیر' placed after 'معوان' (helper) when it appears to be a weaker form? He provides three answers. First, 'ظہیر' is a hyperbolic adjective implying continuous support, thus more emphatic. The objection that it should be intransitive is refuted by analogy to 'نصیر', though noted that scholars consider 'نصیر' as an active participle. Second, the arrangement is for rhetorical completion, not progression. Third, 'ظہیر' may derive from 'ظہیر القوم' meaning one completely relied upon, giving it even greater emphasis. He then explains that 'من المهاجرين والأنصار' refers to all Companions, with Muhajirun and Ansar mentioned for their special status. 'والذين اتبعوهم' refers to the Tabi'un, not the earlier groups. The commentary then turns to metaphors in the verse: sciences likened to a roaring sea, with waves and roaring as metaphorical extensions. Finally, a note that the author's sermon indicates the book will cover the four proofs and other usul topics.

Key Terms
ظہیر (zahir): A hyperbolic adjective meaning 'continuous helper' or 'one who provides ongoing support', derived from the form of descriptive adjectives.
صفت مشبہ (sifah mushabbahah): A descriptive adjective that implies a permanent quality, usually intransitive, but here considered transitive by analogy.
استعارہ (isti'arah): Metaphor, where a word is used in a sense other than its original, with different types: primary, imaginary, secondary.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the commentator, why is the word 'ظہیر' considered more emphatic than 'معوان'?
A) Because it is derived from a root meaning strength
B) Because it is a hyperbolic adjective implying continuous support
C) Because it is a plural form
D) Because it is a verbal noun

Key Takeaway
The commentator uses linguistic analysis (صفت مشبہ) and rhetorical context to demonstrate that 'ظہیر' is more emphatic than 'معوان', resolving a textual objection.

Lexical Roots of Hanafi Usul Terminology
Lexical definitions of key usul terms

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify the lexical root of key Hanafi usul terms and explain how their literal meanings inform technical usage.

Core Idea
Precise lexical meaning is the foundation of Usul al-Fiqh — a term's root determines its legal scope.

This passage from the commentary on Al-Tawdih wa al-Talwih provides a lexical investigation (lughawi tahqiq) of key terms that appear in the author's introduction. While these may seem like simple dictionary entries, understanding the literal meanings of words like madarik, mahsul, and alam is essential for grasping the technical framework of Hanafi usul. The commentator shows how each term's root connotation shapes its role in legal theory.

Guided Path
1
Identify the term and its Arabic root
Note the root letters and verbal noun of the term. For example, 'madarik' is from d-r-k, meaning 'to reach' or 'attain'.
Root analysis helps connect literal and technical meanings.
2
State the literal meaning
Determine the basic lexical definition from Arabic dictionaries. For 'madarik', it is 'places of occurrence'.
Often there are multiple literal meanings; note them all.
3
Translate to the technical usul sense
Explain how the term is used in the discipline of usul al-fiqh. For 'madarik', it refers to detailed proofs (adillah tafsiliyyah).
The technical sense is an extension of the literal meaning.
4
Explain why this lexical connection matters
Show how the literal root illuminates the technical usage. 'Madarik' as 'places of occurrence' suggests that proofs are the loci where rulings occur.
This method prevents confusion and deepens understanding.
5
Apply to a sample sentence from the commentary
Take a phrase like 'madarik al-ahkam' and see how the lexical meaning enriches the interpretation.
Practice reinforces the skill.

Lexical investigation: 'Madarik' is the plural of 'madrak' meaning 'places of occurrence,' and here it refers to detailed proofs. 'Mahsul' is everything that is appropriate to know, and here it means the qiyasi issues that are unknown. 'Yatanassamu' is from the form tafa'ala, meaning to smell a fragrance. The Arabs say 'tanassamtu ruh al-hayat' (I smelled the spirit of life). 'Qabul': with fatha on qaf has two meanings: (1) east wind, and (2) acceptance; if with damm on qaf, it means acceptance only. 'Uqul': with fatha on 'ayn means refuge; with damm on 'ayn is plural of 'aql' meaning intellectual faculty. 'Bahr' means a great scholar, derived from 'bahr' (sea). 'Alam' has two meanings: (1) flag—just as flags are made as signs for knowing the way, so the author is a sign for guidance in religion; (2) mountain—just as mountains are used as signs for knowing the way, the author is a sign for guidance. 'Alam' also means world. 'Dirayah' means understanding. 'Mu'addil' means straightener. 'Munaqqih' means cleaner. 'Aghsan' is plural of 'ghusn' meaning branch. 'Mabsut' means a large book. 'Mustasfa' means summary, essence. 'Madid' means long. 'Wajiz' means concise. 'Arkan' plural of 'rukn'. 'Waf' means complete, nothing left. 'Wasit' means intermediate. 'Mabani' plural of 'mabna' meaning foundation. 'Salaka yasluku sulukan' means to walk. 'Min hajan' means path. 'Badi'an' means wondrous. 'Asrar' plural of 'sirr' meaning secret. 'Istawla' from the form istif'al means to ascend. 'Al-amad' means goal. 'Al-aqsa' means extreme. 'Manar' in ancient times they built pillars for determining the path and lit fire on them at night so that no one would lose the way; now it means pillar in general. 'Musabbaha' from the form nasara means a small thing. 'Ratq' means veil. 'Afkar' plural of 'fikr'; 'fatq' means opening. 'Adhan' plural of 'udhun' meaning ear.

Commentary
This section provides lexical definitions of key terms occurring in the introductory praise of the author and the book. The commentator explains that these words, while common in Arabic, have specific connotations in the context of usul al-fiqh. For example, 'madarik' is defined as 'places of occurrence' but here refers to detailed proofs (adillah tafsiliyyah). 'Mahsul' refers to the unknown qiyasi issues that are the subject of legal reasoning. The commentary also clarifies nuanced meanings of 'qabul' depending on vowelization, and distinguishes between the two meanings of 'uqul' (with fatha vs. damm). These lexical clarifications are essential for a precise understanding of the author's claims about the book and the science of usul. The commentator then lists and defines various adjectives and nouns used to describe the book's comprehensiveness and the author's scholarly attributes.

Key Terms
مدارک (madarik): Plural of madrak, meaning 'places of occurrence'; in this context, it refers to detailed proofs (adillah tafsiliyyah).
محصول (mahsul): Everything that is appropriate to know; here it specifically denotes the unknown qiyasi issues that require deduction.

Resolving Grammatical Objections in Usul Texts: The Case of Waw
Resolves grammatical objection about waw joining different sentence types

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify a grammatical objection based on conjunction of different sentence types and apply the Hanafi resolution strategies (declarative reinterpretation, content conjunction, compensatory waw).

Core Idea
A grammatical objection about waw can be resolved by analyzing sentence types or by reinterpreting waw as compensatory.

When reading Hanafi usul texts, you may encounter grammatical objections that question the validity of a phrase. One such objection is the conjunction of a declarative sentence to an imperative, which Arabic grammar forbids. In this lesson, we examine a passage where three answers are given to defend the text's phrasing. Understanding these answers strengthens your ability to parse usul texts accurately and appreciate the linguistic precision of Hanafi scholars.

Guided Path
1
Identify the Grammatical Objection
Read the passage and locate the specific objection: the 'waw' in 'wa ba'd' joins a declarative clause (the content after it) to an imperative clause ('al-hamdu wa al-salawat'). Understand why this is forbidden in Arabic grammar.
The objection assumes that 'al-hamdu lillah' is imperative (a command to praise) rather than declarative.
2
Analyze the First Answer: Both Are Declarative
The first answer reclassifies 'al-hamdu lillah' and 'al-salawat' as declarative statements (khabar) because they inform that Allah deserves praise and the Prophet deserves blessings. This turns the conjunction into 'atf al-khabar 'ala al-khabar', which is allowed.
This resolution depends on interpreting the meaning of the phrases, not just their form.
3
Analyze the Second Answer: Conjunction of Content
The second answer states that the conjunction is not of the sentences themselves but of the overall stories or contents (atf al-qissah 'ala al-qissah). This avoids the grammatical issue by shifting focus to the broader narrative.
This is a pragmatic resolution that emphasizes the intended meaning over strict sentence-by-sentence parsing.
4
Analyze the Third Answer: Compensatory Waw
The third answer argues that the 'waw' is not a conjunctive particle but a compensatory waw (waw iwadiyyah) that replaces the conditional 'amma'. The presence of 'fa-inna' later supports this interpretation. If 'waw' is not conjunctive, no grammatical objection arises.
This is the most technical answer, drawing on the distinction between conjunctive and other uses of 'waw'.
5
Determine the Legal Significance
Reflect on why this textual analysis matters: it safeguards the integrity of the usul text against a superficial grammatical flaw, ensuring that the author's intended meaning remains clear and authoritative.
Hanafi usul scholars are meticulous about even particle-level usage.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
سوال:۔ و بعد میں واؤ عاطفہ ہے اور مابعد کا جملہ کے ماقبل یعنی الحمد و الصلوۃ پر عطف ہے اور یہ عطف درست نہیں کیونکہ وبعد کا مابعد جملہ خبریہ ہے اور الحمد والصلوۃ یہ جملہ انشائیہ ہے تو لازم آئے گا " عطف الخبر علی الانشاء " اور یہ جائز نہیں ہے۔ جواب (۱):۔ جس طرح واؤ کا مابعد جملہ خبریہ ہے اسی طرح واؤ کا ماقبل بھی جملہ خبریہ ہے کیونکہ الحمدللہ میں اللہ کے حمد کے مستحق ہونے کی خبر دی گئی ہے اور والصلوۃ میں حضور صلى الله عليه وسلم کے مستحق صلوۃ و سلام ہو نے کی خبر دی گئی ہے تو یہ عطف الخبر علی الخبر " ہے۔ فلا اعتراض ۔ جواب (۲) : ۔ یہ عطف القصہ علی القصہ کے قبیل سے ہے یعنی جملہ کا عطف جملہ پر نہیں بلکہ واؤ کے بعد کے مضمون کا (۲):۔ القصہ ماقبل کے مضمون پر عطف ہے۔ جواب : یہ سوال تب وارد ہوتا جب واو عاطفہ ہو حالانکہ ہم کہتے ہیں کہ یہ واؤ عوضیہ ہے اما شرطیہ کے عوض میں اس کو ذکر کیا گیا ہے یہی وجہ ہے کہ آگے فان میں فاجزا یہ ہے فلا اعتراض۔
Question: The 'waw' in 'wa ba'd' is a conjunction, and the clause after it is conjoined to what precedes it, i.e., 'al-hamdu wa al-salawat'. This conjunction is not correct because the clause after 'wa ba'd' is declarative (khabariyyah), while 'al-hamdu wa al-salawat' is imperative (insha'iyyah). This would require 'conjunction of a declarative to an imperative', which is not permissible. Answer (1): Just as the clause after 'waw' is declarative, similarly the clause before 'waw' is also declarative, because 'al-hamdu lillah' informs that Allah deserves praise, and 'al-salawat' informs that the Prophet (PBUH) deserves blessings and peace. So this is 'conjunction of declarative to declarative' – no objection. Answer (2): This is of the type 'conjunction of story to story', i.e., not conjunction of sentence to sentence, but conjunction of the content after 'waw' to the content before. Answer (3): This objection would apply if the 'waw' were conjunctive, but we say this 'waw' is compensatory, mentioned in place of 'amma' conditional. That is why later 'fa' appears in 'fa-inna' – no objection.
Source pages p. 73

Commentary
This passage addresses a grammatical objection about the use of 'waw' in the author's phrase 'wa ba'd'. The objection is that 'waw' is joining a declarative sentence (the content after 'wa ba'd') to an imperative sentence (the preceding 'al-hamdu wa al-salawat'), which is not allowed. Three responses are given: (1) Both sentences are actually declarative because 'al-hamdu lillah' is informing of Allah's worthiness of praise. (2) It is conjunction of the whole story, not just the sentence. (3) The 'waw' is not conjunctive but compensatory for 'amma' (the conditional particle), so the objection is void. This shows meticulous attention to Arabic syntax in usul texts.

Key Terms
عطف الخبر على الانشاء (atf al-khabar ala al-insha'): Conjoining a declarative sentence to an imperative/performative sentence, which is grammatically disallowed in Arabic.
واؤ عوضیہ (waw iwadiyyah): A compensatory waw used in place of another particle (here, 'amma' conditional) to indicate conditionality.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Key Takeaway
Grammatical objections to usul texts can be resolved by reinterpreting sentence types, shifting focus to content, or reclassifying particles like waw as compensatory.

Allama Radhi's Rule on Annexing Masdar to a Sentence
Explaining a grammatical rule for interpreting a phrase in the author's introduction

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to apply Allama Radhi's rule to interpret a masdar joined to a sentence by waw, and determine whether the waw is emphatic or circumstantial.

Core Idea
When a masdar is joined via waw, it emphasizes the preceding sentence; its verb is omitted and understood from context.

This lesson introduces a grammatical rule from Allama Radhi that clarifies the author's phrase 'ولا اشتهار في نصف النهار'. By understanding this rule, you will see how the author emphasizes that his book's fame surpasses the midday sun. This tool is essential for accurate textual interpretation in usul al-fiqh.

Guided Path
1
Identify the construction
Locate a masdar (verbal noun) joined by the conjunction waw to a preceding complete sentence. In our example, 'ولا اشتهار' is joined to the implied sentence 'طار' (meaning 'اشتهر' - became famous).
2
Determine the implied verb
The preceding sentence provides the verb that governs the masdar. Here, the verb 'طار' is understood from context, meaning 'became famous'.
3
Recognize emphasis
The masdar functions to emphasize the action, not to introduce new information. It confirms that the book's fame is different from the sun's fame – it is even greater.
4
Consider the alternative
Check if the waw could be circumstantial (حالية). In that case, the masdar would be accusative due to removal of the preposition (نزع الخافض), giving a similar but distinct meaning of comparison.
Both interpretations lead to the same practical meaning: the book is more famous than the sun.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
عطف المصدر علی الجملہ کے بارے میں علامہ رضی کا ضابطہ
قوله ولا اشتهار في نصف النهار : ضابطہ :۔ علامہ رضی نے ایک ضابطہ نقل کیا ہے کہ جب مصدرکا کسی جملہ پر عطف بواسطہ واؤ کے ہو تو وہ معطوف علیہ کی تاکید کے لئے آتا ہے اور اس کے فعل کو حذف کرنا واجب ہوتا ہے کیونکہ معطوف علیہ اس کے فعل مقدر پر دلالت کرتا ہے جیسے ” اعتديت ولا اعتداء الغراب “اى” لا اعتديت اعتداء الغراب بل اسرع منه تو اسی طرح یہاں ولا اشتہار الشمس کا عطف ہے طار" پر جو "اشتہر " کے معنی میں ہے تو تقدیر عبارت ہوگی لا اشتهر اشتهار الشمس بل اشهر منه ، مطلب یہ ہے کہ یہ کتاب نصف النہار کے سورج کی طرح مشہور نہیں ہوئی بلکہ اس سے بھی زیادہ مشہور ہوئی ہے۔ یا واؤ حالیہ ہے اور اشتہار منصوب بنزع الخافض ہے اصل میں تھا ولا کاشتھار الشمس في نصف النهار معنی ہوگا کہ یہ کتاب مشہور ہوئی ہے حال یہ ہے کہ نصف النہار میں سورج کے مشہور ہونے کی طرح نہیں بلکہ اس سے بھی زیادہ مشہور ہوئی۔
Rule regarding the annexation of the masdar to the sentence by Allama Radhi. His statement: 'And there is no fame like the sun at midday.' The rule: Allama Radhi has transmitted a rule that when a masdar is annexed to a sentence by means of waw, it comes for emphasis of the annexed-to and its verb must be deleted, because the annexed-to indicates its implied verb, like 'I transgressed, not the transgression of the crow' meaning 'I did not transgress the transgression of the crow, but faster than it.' So similarly here, 'Wa la ishtihar al-shams' is annexed to 'ṭāra' which is in the meaning of 'ishtahara', so the implied phrase would be 'la ishtahara ishtihara al-shams bal ashharu minhu'. The meaning is that this book did not become famous like the sun at midday, but rather more famous than it. Or the waw is circumstantial and 'ishtihar' is accusative by removal of the preposition; originally it was 'wa la ka-ishtihar al-shams fi nisf al-nahar', meaning: this book became famous while not being like the fame of the sun at midday, but rather more famous.
Source pages p. 75

Commentary
This passage is a grammatical analysis of the author's phrase 'wa la ishtihar fi nisf al-nahar'. The commentator invokes a rule from Allama Radhi concerning the construction where a masdar (verbal noun) is joined to a complete sentence by the conjunction waw. According to this rule, such a masdar serves to emphasize the sentence it is attached to, and its implicit verb must be omitted because the preceding sentence already indicates that verb. For example, in Arabic one might say 'اعتديت ولا اعتداء الغراب' meaning 'I transgressed, but not the transgression of the crow' – the omitted verb is 'اعتديت' understood from the first clause. Applying this here, 'لا اشتہار الشمس' is joined to the implied verb 'طار' (which means 'اشتہر', became famous), so the full meaning is 'لا اشتہر اشتهار الشمس بل اشهر منه' – the book did not become famous like the sun at midday, but even more famous. Alternatively, the waw could be circumstantial (حالية) and 'اشتہار' is accusative due to removal of the preposition (نزع الخافض), originally 'ولا كاشتہار الشمس' meaning 'and not like the fame of the sun', giving a similar meaning. This rule is a tool for proper understanding of the author's intent, not a legal ruling, but it is essential for accurate interpretation of texts.

Key Terms
عطف المصدر على الجملة (atf al-masdar ala al-jumla): The grammatical construction where a verbal noun (masdar) is joined to a preceding complete sentence by the conjunction waw, functioning as emphasis with an implied verb deleted.
واؤ حالية (waw haliyya): The waw that introduces a circumstantial clause (hal), here considered as an alternative interpretation.
نزع الخافض (naz al-khafid): A grammatical phenomenon where the preposition is omitted, causing the following noun to be accusative.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to Allama Radhi's rule, when a masdar is annexed to a sentence with waw, what is the function of the masdar?
A) It provides a new independent statement.
B) It emphasizes the sentence it is attached to, with its verb deleted.
C) It indicates past tense.
D) It is always a circumstantial clause.

Key Takeaway
Allama Radhi's rule: when a masdar is joined by waw to a sentence, it emphasizes that sentence; the verb is omitted and understood from context.

Linguistic Precision in Hanafi Usul: Analyzing Key Terms from the Matn's Introduction
Lexical and grammatical analysis of the matn's opening

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain the grammatical and lexical analysis of key terms from the matn's introduction as presented in Al-Tarweeh, and apply similar linguistic scrutiny to other usul texts.

Core Idea
Linguistic precision is the bedrock of Hanafi usul; every word is parsed to avoid ambiguity in legal derivation.

This passage from Al-Tarweeh demonstrates the meticulous lexicographical and grammatical work that underpins Hanafi usul al-fiqh. The commentator analyzes words from the matn's opening, explaining their roots, forms, and meanings, sometimes engaging with alternative interpretations. Understanding this level of detail is essential for grasping how Hanafi jurists derived rulings from texts.

Guided Path
1
Identify the word being explained
For each word noted in the commentary, locate its root and plural form as given by the author.
e.g., 'af'idah' is plural of 'fu'ad'
2
Determine grammatical function
Analyze whether the word is a noun of place, active participle, etc., and note any omitted elements (e.g., genitive construct).
The author rejects the noun-of-place interpretation for 'majazan' due to missing 'fi'.
3
Note any debate or alternative interpretation
Identify cases where the commentator discusses differing opinions, like 'ha'imah', and evaluate the reasoning given.
Al-Khattabi argues for 'thirsting' rather than 'perplexed' based on the liver's attribute.
4
Reflect on legal implications
Consider how precise lexical understanding prevents misinterpretation in legal texts.
A wrong meaning could alter the derivation of a hukm.

الترويج لحل التوضيح والتنويج
مجازی“ یہ مصدرمسیحی ہے مجاز ا اسم ظرف کے معنی میں ہے یا پھر مضاف محذوف ہے اور یا اپنے معنی مصدری میں مستعمل ہے تقدیر عبارت یوں ہوگی وقت اجتیازی یعنی میرے گزرنے کے وقت بعض حضرات کہتے ہیں کہ یہ ظرف مکان ہے اور بما وراء النہر اس سے بدل ہے لیکن یہ قول ضعیف ہے کیونکہ نحویوں نے یہ تصریح کی ہے کہ ظرف مکان سے پہلے حرف فی کو ذکر کرنا ضروری ہے اور وہ یہاں مذکور نہیں ہے أفئدة جمع ہے فواد کی بمعنی دل تہوی الیہ عمر ب سے بمعنی تحمیل الیہ" ا عباد جمع ہے کبد کی بمعنی جگر هائمه ای متحیرہ بمعنی حیران لیکن یہاں تہوی الیہ پر سوال ہوتا ہے۔
سوال:۔ یہ ہے کہ باقی صفات تو اسم فاعل کے ساتھ ذکر کی ہیں اس کو فعل کی صورت میں کیوں لائے؟ جواب:۔ یہی ہے ' فاجعل افئدة من الناس تہوی الیہم" کی طرف۔ ہائمہ کے بارے میں خطابی کہتے ہیں یہ مشتق ہے "ہام" بمعنی عطش سے کیونکہ جگر پیاس سے متصف ہوتا ہے تحیر سے متصف نہیں ہوتا یا پھر یہاں تضمین ہوتی ہے حرص کے معنی میں یا پھر کبد سے مراد اہل اکباد ہیں اور اہل اکباد تحیر وعطش دونوں سے متصف ہوتے ہیں ۔ " عقول " جمع ہے عقل کی مراد صاحب عقل ہے جائیہ باب نصر سے اس کا معنی ہے گھٹنے کے بل بیٹھنا رغبات" رغبة کی جمع ہے متوقفة مشتق ہے وقف سے بمعنی ٹھہر نے والی "السمطایا جمع ہے مطیہ کی دراصل مطیوۃ تھا یہاں ادغام ہوا ہے بمعنی سواری استار ستر کی جمع ہے بمعنی پردہ حواشی جمع ہے حاشیہ کی اطراف جمع ہے طرف کی دونوں کا معنی ہے کنارہ بحار جمع ہے بحر کی بمعنی سمندر لالی جمع ہے لؤلؤ کی بمعنی موتی اصداف جمع ہے صدف کی بمعنی سیپ انامل جمع ہے انملۃ کی بمعنی انگلیاں انظار جمع ہے نظر کی مراد اصحاب نظر ہیں "عقد جمع ہے عقدہ کی بمعنی گانٹھ گرہ بسنان انگلیوں کے پورے فلطائفہ بعد تقدیر عبارت ہے بعد ڈ لک الی الآن یعنی اس کی باریکیاں اس کے لکھے جانے کے بعد سے اب تک الفاظ کے پردوں کے نیچے چھپی ہوئی ہیں۔ خلاصہ یہ کہ اس کا مضاف الیہ محذوف منوی ہے اس لئے بعد مبنی بر ضم ہے۔
"حجب جمع ہے حجاب کی بمعنی پردہ " خرائد " جمع ہے خریدہ کی بمعنی نو جوان خوب رو محبوبہ " همم" جمع ہے ہمتہ کی مستشرفة باب استفعال سے ہے اس کا معنی ہے گردن اٹھانا اعناق جمع ہے علق کی بمعنی گردن احداق حدقة کی جمع ہے بمعنی آنکھ کی پتلی اخوض "باب نصر سے بمعنی داخل ہونا لجج " جمع ہے جہ کی بمعنی گہرا پانی اغوص"
The commentary on the solution of Al-Tawdih wa Al-Talwih. Metaphorically, this is a verbal noun [masdar]? It is used in the sense of a noun of place, or the genitive construct is omitted, or it is used in its original verbal noun meaning. The appreciation of the phrase would be 'time of my passing', i.e., at the time of my passing. Some scholars say it is a noun of place, and 'beyond the river' is a substitute for it, but this saying is weak because grammarians have explicitly stated that before a noun of place, the letter 'fi' must be mentioned, and it is not mentioned here. 'Af'idah' is the plural of 'fu'ad' meaning heart. 'Tahwi ilayhi' from 'amr'? meaning to incline towards. 'A'bad' is the plural of 'kabid' meaning liver. 'Ha'imah' meaning perplexed, i.e., confused. But here there is a question about 'tahwi ilayhi'. Question: The other attributes were mentioned with the active participle, why was it brought in the form of a verb? Answer: That is it, referring to 'faj'al af'idatan mina al-nasi tahwi ilayhim'. Regarding 'ha'imah', al-Khattabi says it is derived from 'ham' meaning thirst, because the liver is described with thirst, not with perplexity. Or here there is a guarantee of the meaning of greed, or by 'kabid' is meant the people of livers, and the people of livers are described with both perplexity and thirst. 'Uqul' is the plural of 'aql', meaning the possessor of intellect. 'Jai'ah' from the door of 'nasr' meaning to sit on the knees. 'Raghabat' is the plural of 'raghbah'. 'Mutawaqqifah' is derived from 'waqf' meaning stopping. 'Al-Samathaya' is the plural of 'matiyyah', originally 'matiywah', with idgham, meaning riding animal. 'Astar' is the plural of 'sitr' meaning veil. 'Hawashi' is the plural of 'hashiyah' meaning edges. 'Atraf' is the plural of 'taraf', both meaning side. 'Bihar' is the plural of 'bahr' meaning sea. 'La'ali' is the plural of 'lu'lu' meaning pearls. 'Asdaf' is the plural of 'sadaf' meaning shell. 'Anamil' is the plural of 'anmalah' meaning fingers. 'Anzar' is the plural of 'nazar', meaning people of insight. 'Uqad' is the plural of 'uqda' meaning knot, joint of fingers. 'Lata'if' after appreciation of the phrase is after writing until now, i.e., its subtleties since its writing until now are hidden under the veils of words. Summary: its genitive construct is omitted and implied, therefore 'ba'd' is based on the presumption of genitive. 'Hujub' is the plural of 'hijab' meaning veil. 'Khara'id' is the plural of 'kharidah' meaning young beautiful beloved. 'Humam' is the plural of 'himmah' meaning high aspiration. 'Mustashrifah' from the door of 'istif'al' meaning to raise the neck. 'A'naq' is the plural of 'unuq' meaning neck. 'Ahdaq' is the plural of 'hadaqah' meaning pupil of the eye. 'Akhawwad' from the door of 'nasr' meaning to enter. 'Lujaj' is the plural of 'lujjah' meaning deep water. 'Aghawwas'
Source pages p. 77

Commentary
This passage is a lexical and grammatical commentary by the author on the opening words of the matn (Al-Tawdih). The author explains that the word 'majazan' may be used as a noun of place, or with the genitive construct omitted, or in its original verbal meaning. He then clarifies the phrase 'waqta ijtiazi' (time of my passing) and refutes the opinion that it is a noun of place, citing the grammatical rule that the letter 'fi' is required before a noun of place, which is absent here. The commentary then proceeds to explain individual words from a Qur'anic phrase or from the matn: 'af'idah' (hearts), 'tahwi' (inclines), 'ha'imah' (perplexed or thirsting), 'uquul' (intellects), 'raghabat' (desires), etc. For each, the author provides the plural form, meaning, and sometimes a grammatical clarification. He also engages with a question about why a particular word is in verb form rather than as an active participle, and answers it by referencing the Qur'anic verse. The commentary is detailed, serving to enable students to understand the precise meanings and nuances of the text the author is explaining. This is typical of Hanafi usul commentaries, which prioritize linguistic precision as a foundation for legal reasoning.

Key Terms
مجاز (majaz): Used metaphorically or in a derived sense, as opposed to حقيقة (literal).
أفئدة (af'idah): Plural of fu'ad, meaning hearts; here in the context of the Qur'anic phrase 'faj'al af'idatan mina al-nasi tahwi ilayhim'.
هائمة (ha'imah): Derived from 'ham' (thirst) or 'haym' (perplexity); here debated whether it means thirsting or perplexed.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

B) To indicate continuous action
C) To maintain the rhyme of the verse

Key Takeaway
Linguistic analysis, including grammatical function and root derivation, is essential for accurately understanding usul texts and preventing misinterpretation.

Analyzing Multiple Interpretations (Ihtimalat) and Metaphors in Usul Text
Explores multiple meanings and a metaphor in the opening praise

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify multiple probabilities (ihtimalat) in a usul text and distinguish a manifest metaphor (isti'arah tasrihiyyah) from other rhetorical devices.

Core Idea
A single phrase can carry multiple valid meanings; the usul scholar explores them systematically.

This lesson examines the commentary (sharh) on the author's opening praise. The commentator carefully unpacks four possible interpretations of the words 'first' and 'second,' a classic usul exercise in exploring ihtimalat. Additionally, the metaphor of 'reins of praise' is dissected as a manifest metaphor, showing the rhetorical depth of the text. By understanding these analytical moves, you will strengthen your own ability to engage with dense usul texts.

Guided Path
1
Identify the object of analysis
What specific phrase is being analyzed? The author's praise containing the words 'first' and 'second'.
The commentator begins by asking about the intended meaning of these two terms.
2
List the four probabilities
What are the four possible meanings? Label them carefully: (1) praise at book's beginning vs. end; (2) praise in Tanqih vs. Tawdih; (3) praise at life's beginning vs. end; (4) praise for first creation (souls) vs. second creation (bodies).
Additional probabilities exist in Talwih, but these are the main ones.
3
Understand the classification
Why does the commentator present multiple interpretations? This is an usul method to explore the depth of meaning and show that a text can be understood in different ways.
Such analysis helps avoid hasty adoption of one meaning.
4
Analyze the metaphor
How does the commentator explain the phrase 'the reins of praise are turned to Him'? The intention of praise is likened to a rein that can be directed, forming a manifest metaphor (isti'ārah taṣrīḥiyyah).
The mention is of the rein (thing compared to), but the intention (thing compared) is meant.
5
Apply the method
What is the lesson for reading usul texts? Be open to multiple plausible readings and recognize rhetorical devices that add layers of meaning.
This skill helps in deriving accurate legal rulings from authoritative texts.

امر ثالث مرادی تحقیق:۔ اول و ثانیا کی مراد میں چار احتمال ہیں۔
احتمال اول:۔ اول سے مراد جو کتاب کے شروع میں تعریف کی اورثانی سے مراد جو کتاب کے آخر میں تعریف کی۔ ر احتمال ثانی: اولا سے مراد وہ تعریف ہے جو نقیح میں کی اور ثانیا سے مراد وہ تعریف ہے جو تو ضیح میں کی ہے۔ احتمال ثالث: اولا سے مراد اول عمر کی تعریف اور ثانیا سے مراد آخر عمر کی تعریف ۔ احتمال رابع: اولا سے مراد اللہ تعالی کی تعریف کرتا ہوں اس کی تخلیق اولیٰ پر ۔ (ارواح کے پیدا کرنے پر ) او د ثانیا سے مراد یہ ہے کہ اس کی تعریف کرتا ہوں تخلیق ثانوی پر ۔ (اجساد کے پیدا کرنے پر مزید احتمالات تلویح میں مذکور ہیں۔ امر رائع استعارات: ولعنان الثناء الیہ ثانیا۔ اسمیں بعض استعارے تو صاحب تلویح نے بیان کیے ہیں ۔ ان پر بحث و ہیں ہوگی۔ ان کے علاوہ ایک احتمال اور بھی ہے کہ یہاں استعارہ تصریحہ پایا جاتا ہے کہ ارادہ ثناء کو تشبیہ دی ہے۔ عنان کے ساتھ کہ جس طرح عنان اور لگام سے گھوڑے کو جس طرف چاہیں موڑ سکتے ہیں اسی طرح ثناء کے ارادہ کو جس ممدوح کی طرف چاہیں موڑ سکتے ہیں خلاصہ یہ کہ ذکر مشبہ بہ کا ہے مراد مشبہ ہے یہ استعارہ مصرحہ ہے۔
Third matter: the intended meaning. Regarding the intended meaning of 'first' and 'second', there are four probabilities. Probability one: by 'first' is meant the praise at the beginning of the book, and by 'second' is meant the praise at the end of the book. And probability two: by 'first' is meant the praise made in Tanqih, and by 'second' is meant the praise made in Tawdih. Probability three: by 'first' is meant the praise of the beginning of life, and by 'second' is meant the praise of the end of life. Probability four: by 'first' is meant 'I praise Allah, the Exalted, for His first creation (creation of souls)', and by 'second' is meant 'I praise Him for the second creation (creation of bodies)'. Additional probabilities are mentioned in Talwih. Fourth matter: metaphors. In the phrase 'and to Him the reins of praise are turned second', some metaphors have been explained by the author of Talwih, and there will be discussion on them. Besides them, there is another probability that here a manifest metaphor is found: the intention of praise has been likened to a rein. Just as a rein and bridle can turn a horse in any direction, similarly the intention of praise can be directed to any praised one. In summary, the mention of the thing compared to is present, and the thing compared is intended; this is a manifest metaphor.
Source pages p. 85

Commentary
This passage from the commentary (sharh) discusses the author's opening praise of God. It begins by noting that there are four possible meanings for the phrases 'first' and 'second' in the author's words. This is a typical usul type of analysis: distinguishing multiple interpretations (iḥtimālāt). The first interpretation refers to the praise at the beginning and end of the book; the second to the praises in Tanqih and Tawdih; the third to the beginning and end of one's life; and the fourth to the first creation (souls) and second creation (bodies). The author then moves to metaphors, explaining how the phrase 'reins of praise' is a manifest metaphor (istiʿārah taṣrīḥiyyah): the intention of praise is likened to a rein that can be directed. This shows the rhetorical depth of the text. The commentary follows the order of the matn, clarifying each element.

Key Terms
احتمال (ihtimal): A possible interpretation or meaning of a word or phrase
استعارہ تصریحہ (isti'arah tasrihiyyah): A manifest metaphor where the thing compared to (the rein) is mentioned, and the thing compared (the intention) is intended

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
How many probabilities are mentioned for the meaning of 'first' and 'second' in the author's praise?
A) Two
B) Three
C) Four
D) Five

Key Takeaway
In usul, a single phrase can support multiple valid interpretations; the scholar's task is to identify and weigh them, not to assume a single meaning.

The Author's Use of 'Hamidan' as a Hal: Reconciling Two Hadiths on Beginning Acts
Textual analysis of author's grammatical choice for hamd

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain why the author chose to express hamd as a circumstantial clause (hal) rather than a nominal or verbal sentence, and how this choice resolves the apparent conflict between the hadiths on beginning with basmala and hamd.

Core Idea
The author uses 'hamidan' as a hal to equalize basmala and hamd while prioritizing basmala via Quran and ijma.

In this textual analysis, we examine the author's deliberate grammatical choice to render 'hamid' as a circumstantial clause (hal) instead of the more common nominal or verbal forms. This seemingly minor shift serves a major legal-hermeneutical function: it harmonizes two Prophetic traditions that both demand to be the opening of any important matter. By understanding this choice, you will see how Hanafi usul scholars use grammatical analysis to resolve textual conflicts (ta'arud) and preserve the full import of each dalil.

Guided Path
1
Identify the grammatical issue
The author could have written 'al-hamdu lillah' (nominal) or 'ahmadu Allah' (verbal) to express praise. Instead he wrote 'hāmida[n]' as a circumstantial clause. Determine what grammatical structure 'hal' represents and how it differs from a full sentence.
A hal describes the state of the subject/object at the time of the action, often indicating a condition or concurrent circumstance.
2
Locate the two hadiths
The commentator cites two hadiths: one requiring 'Bismillah' at the start of important matters, another requiring 'Al-hamdu lillah'. Recognize that these two traditions, if taken at face value, appear to conflict because beginning with one necessarily omits beginning with the other.
The principle of combining dalils (jama') is preferred over discarding one.
3
Understand the author's reconciling technique
The author makes both basmala and hamd into circumstantial clauses attached to an implicit 'I begin' (ana abtadi'). This way, both are conditions of the beginning without being the explicit first word. The basmala takes priority in order because of Quranic practice and ijma.
The basmala is placed first textually, and the hamd follows as a hal, signalling equality in importance but difference in order.
4
Analyse the omission of the conjunction (waw)
The author deliberately omits the conjunction 'wa' (and) before 'hāmida[n]'. If he had used 'wa', it would imply subordination. Without it, the hal is coordinate, indicating that hamd is not subordinate to basmala but equal in status.
This shows how a single particle (or its absence) can alter legal implication.
5
Evaluate the two manuscript versions
The commentator notes a difference between the 'established copy' and the 'old copy' regarding whether 'hāmida[n]' is a hal from the agent of 'yaqulu' or from the implicit 'I begin'. Both readings support the core function of hamd as a circumstantial clause.
This illustrates how manuscript variants can affect grammatical analysis without undermining the overall legal import.

وَالإجماع المُنعَقِدِ عَلَيْهِ وَتَرَكَ العَاطِفَ لِئَلَّا يُشعِرَ بِالتَّبَعِيَّةِ فَيُحِلُّ بِالتَّسْوِيَةِ وَلَا يَجُوزُ أَن يَكُونَ حَامِدًا جَالًا مِن فَاعِل يَقُولُ ؛ لأنَّ قَولَهُ وَبَعدُ فَإِنَّ العَبدَ عَلَى مَا فِي النُّسخَةِ المُقَرَّرَةِ عِندَ المُصَنِّفِ صَارِفٌ عَن ذَلِكَ . وَأَمَّا عَلَى النُسخَةِ القَدِيمَةِ الخَالِيَةِ عَن هَذَا الصَّارِفِ فَالظَّاهِرُ أَنَّهُ حَالٌ عَنهُ .

تشریح فائدہ (۱):۔ عام طور پر علامہ تفتازانی اپنی شرح میں سوال مقدر کا جواب دیتے ہیں (۲) کبھی کبھی خود سوال صراحتاً ذکر کر تے ہیں اور اس کا جواب بھی تحریر کرتے ہیں۔ (۳) مرادی تحقیق یعنی عبارت سے ماتن کی مراد کو واضح کرتے ہیں (۴) تعیین مرجع یعنی متن میں اگر ضمائر کا ذکر ہو تو شاریخ ان کا مرجع متعین کر دیتے ہیں (۵) علامہ تفتازانی کثرت سے ماتن پر رد بھی کرتے ہیں (۶) کبھی کبھی مسئلہ اختلافیہ میں ماھوالمختار عندہ کو بھی بیان کرتے ہیں (۷) کبھی علامہ تفتازانی ماتن کی خوبی بھی بیان کرتے ہیں مثلاً باتن نے اگر صنعت فصاحت و بلاغت وغیرہ استعمال کی ہے تو اس کی تشریح کر دیتے ہیں۔ (۸) ترکیبی تحقیق یعنی کبھی شاریخ متن کے کسی جملہ کی ترکیب کی طرف اشارہ کر دیتے ہیں (۹) لغوی تحقیق بھی بیان کرتے ہیں (۱۰) دوسرے اصولیین پر بھی کبھی رد کرتے ہیں ۔ تلک عشرہ کاملہ ۔
And the consensus that is concluded upon it, and he left out the conjunction particle lest it indicate subordination, so it becomes in equality. And it is not permissible for 'hamid' to be a circumstantial clause from the agent of 'yaqulu' because his saying 'and after, then the slave' according to the established copy of the author is a diverting factor from that. And as for the old copy that lacks this diverting factor, the apparent is that it is a circumstantial clause from it. Translation: His saying 'Bismillah al-Rahman al-Rahim'. 'Hamidan Allah' is a circumstantial clause from the hidden pronoun that is attached to the preposition 'ba', meaning 'Bismillah ajidu fi al-kitabi hamida'. The author preferred the method of making it a circumstantial clause over the method that is famous among authors, i.e., using a nominal sentence like 'al-hamdu lillah' or a verbal sentence like 'ahmadu Allah', etc. This is to create equality between hamd and tasmiyah, and due to observing the appropriateness between them. So it has been verified in hadith that any important matter not begun with 'Bismillah' is bereft of blessing, and any important matter not begun with 'Al-hamdu lillah' is also bereft of blessing. So the author intended to make hamd a condition for beginning by making it a circumstantial clause, just as tasmiyah is also a circumstantial clause from it. But he (the author) gave priority to tasmiyah because the two hadiths apparently conflict. Because beginning with one of these two causes the loss of beginning with the other, while combining them is possible by prioritizing one over the other, so the beginning is actually with one, and the beginning with the other is added to the rest. So the author acted upon the Book of Allah which mentions giving priority to tasmiyah, and upon the consensus that has been formed on giving priority to tasmiyah. And he left out the conjunction particle so that it does not indicate hamd being subordinate, so it becomes equal. And it is not permissible for 'hamid' to be a circumstantial clause from the agent of 'yaqulu' because his saying 'wa ba'du fa'inna al-'abda' according to the established copy of the author is a diverting factor from that. But according to the old copy that lacks this diverting factor, the apparent is that it is a circumstantial clause from it. Lexical investigation: 'mustakin' meaning hidden; 'aathara' from bab mufa'ala meaning to prefer; 'abtar' meaning cut tail, i.e., deficient; 'ajzam' meaning cut hand, i.e., bereft of blessing; 'fahawala' meaning he intended, desired; 'bafawwata' from taf'il meaning to cause to miss. Explanation of the commentator's intentions: Benefit (1): Generally, Allamah Taftazani in his commentary answers implicit questions. (2) Sometimes he explicitly mentions the question and writes its answer. (3) Intent investigation: he clarifies the author's intent from the expression. (4) Determining the referent: if pronouns are mentioned in the text, the commentator determines their referent. (5) Allamah Taftazani frequently refutes the author. (6) Sometimes in a disputed issue he states what is chosen according to him. (7) Sometimes Allamah Taftazani mentions the author's merit, e.g., if the author used a rhetorical device, he explains it. (8) Syntactic investigation: sometimes the commentator points to the grammatical structure of a sentence in the text. (9) He also provides lexical investigation. (10) Sometimes he refutes other usul scholars. That is a complete ten.
Source pages p. 90

Commentary
This passage is a textual analysis of the author's opening lines. The commentator explains why the author used 'hamidan' (praising) as a circumstantial clause (hal) rather than the common nominal or verbal forms like 'al-hamdu lillah' or 'ahmadu Allah'. The key reason is to achieve equality between the basmala and the hamd, both of which are introduced by the author as circumstantial clauses linked to the implicit 'ana abtadi' (I begin). The commentator cites two hadiths: one about the importance of beginning with basmala, another about beginning with hamd. These appear contradictory because one must prioritize one beginning over the other. The author resolves this by acting on the Quranic practice (basmala first) and the consensus (ijma) on giving precedence to basmala. He then makes hamd a circumstantial clause rather than an independent statement to show it is a condition of the beginning but subordinate in order. The commentator also addresses a grammatical issue: whether 'hamid' is a hal from the agent of 'yaqulu' (he says) in a subsequent phrase; he clarifies that according to the established copy it is not, but according to an older copy it could be. The Urdu section lists ten methodological characteristics of Imam Taftazani's commentary style, such as answering implicit questions, clarifying intent, determining pronoun referents, refuting the author, pointing out rhetorical merits, and linguistic analysis.

Key Terms
حال (hal): A circumstantial clause that describes the state of the subject or object at the time of the action.
ابتر (abtar): Literally 'cut-tailed', metaphorically deficient or bereft of blessing.
تعارض (ta'arud): Apparent conflict between two pieces of evidence (dalils).
تسوية (taswiya): Equality; the state of being equal in rank or status.

Key Takeaway
The author's grammatical choice of 'hamidan' as a hal, without the conjunction, resolves the apparent conflict between the hadiths requiring basmala and hamd at the start of important matters.

Grammatical Analysis of Basmala and Equality in Hamd
Analyzing basmala grammar and reason for deviating from common hamd

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to analyze the grammatical structure of the basmala as a specific adverbial (zarf mustaqarr) and explain the author's reason for making both basmala and hamd circumstantial clauses (hal) to achieve equality.

Core Idea
Basmala is a specific adverbial modifying the seeker of blessing, and both basmala and hamd are made equal by being circumstantial clauses.

In the previous lesson, we saw how the author introduced the double hadith to honor both tasmiyah and tahmid. But why did he not use the common forms like 'al-hamdu lillah' or 'ahmadu Allah'? This passage delves into the exact grammatical relationships within the basmala and the hamd phrase. The commentator clarifies that the basmala is not a vague adverbial (zarf laghw) attached to 'abtadi', but a specific adverbial (zarf mustaqarr) describing the state of the one who begins. Then he reveals the author's elegant reasoning: by making both basmala and 'hamid' circumstantial clauses from the same hidden pronoun, the author creates perfect grammatical equality between them.

Guided Path
1
Identify the components of basmala
Break down 'Bismillah al-Rahman al-Rahim' into its parts: the preposition 'ba', the noun 'ism', and the attributes of Allah. Determine the grammatical function of the entire phrase.
The commentator treats the whole phrase as a prepositional phrase that becomes a circumstantial adverbial.
2
Distinguish zarf mustaqarr from zarf laghw
Understand the difference: zarf mustaqarr specifies a location or state and is essential to the meaning, while zarf laghw is vague and can be omitted without changing the core sense. The commentator argues that basmala here is mustaqarr, not laghw.
Evidence: if it were laghw, 'kitab' would not be the object of 'abtadi', but here the commentator made 'kitab' the object, showing basmala is a hal.
3
Relate basmala to the hidden verb
The basmala is related to 'abtadi' (I begin) via its hidden pronoun 'ana'. The phrase functions as a hal (circumstantial clause) describing the state of the one who begins.
The translation: 'I begin in the state that I am one who seeks blessing with the name of Allah...'
4
Analyze the hamd phrase similarly
The author used 'hamid' (praising) as a second circumstantial clause from the same hidden pronoun 'ana', creating parallel structure with basmala.
Both tasmiyah and tahmid become conditions (qayd) for the beginning.
5
Understand the wisdom of equality
The author deliberately deviated from the common hamd forms (nominal or verbal sentences) to make both basmala and hamd grammatically identical – both are circumstantial clauses. This honors both hadiths equally while placing basmala first.
Equality in grammatical form reflects the author's intention to give no precedence to one over the other except by order.

قوله بسم الرحمن الرحيم :۔ یہ شرح کی عبارت کا پہلا حصہ ہے اس عبارت سے غرض شارع ترکیبی تحقیق کو بیان کرنا ہے۔ جس کا حاصل یہ ہے کہ بسم اللہ میں سب حرف جار ۔ یہ اپنے مجرور سے مل کر ظرف مستقر ہو کر متبر کا کے متعلق ہے اور متبر کا حال ہے ابہا امی کی انا ضمیر سے اور حامد ابدی کی انا ضمیر سے حال ثانی ہے ترجمہ ہوگا میں ابتداء کرتا ہوں اس حال میں کہ میں برکت حاصل کرنے والا ہوں اللہ کے نام کے ساتھ جو بڑا مہربان نہایت رحم کرنے والا ہے ( اور ابتداء کرتا ہوں ) اس حال میں کہ حمد بیان کرنے والا ہوں اللہ کی پہلی مرتبہ اور دوسری مرتبہ۔ فائدہ (۲):۔ بظاہر شاریخ کی کلام سے معلوم ہوتا ہے کہ بسم اللہ یہ ظرف لغو ہے اور ابتدگی کے متعلق ہے حالانکہ حقیقت میں ایسے نہیں ہے بلکہ جار مجرور مل کر یہ متبر کا یا مٹیمنا کے متعلق ہو کر ظرف مستقر ہے اور اس پر قرینہ شاریخ کی کلام ہے کہ انہوں نے کتاب کو ابدی کا مفعول بنایا ہے حالانکہ ظرف لغو کی صورت میں تسمیہ مفعول کے قائم مقام ہوگا ۔ معلوم ہوا کہ یہ متبر کا سے متعلق ہے اور وہ حال ہے ابدی کی انا ضمیر سے اور اس کا مفعول کتاب ہے۔
حمد میں مشہور طریقہ سے عدول کی حکمت
قولہ آثر :۔ یہ شرح کی عبارت کا دوسرا حصہ ہے اس عبارت سے شاریخ کی غرض سوال مقدر کا جواب دینا ہے۔ سوال:۔ یہ ہے کہ مائن نے حمد کے مشہور طریقہ یعنی جملہ اسمیہ اور جملہ فعلیہ سے عدول کیوں کیا؟
جواب: ماتن در اصل حمد اور تسمیہ میں برابری کرنا چاہتے ہیں اور ماتن نے حمد اور تسمیہ میں برابری دو طرح سے کی ہے۔ نمبرا ۔ جس طرح بسم اللہ کو ابدی کی انا ضمیر سے حال بنایا ہے۔ حامد کو بھی انا ضمیر سے حال بنایا ہے۔ تاکہ یہ دونوں ابتداء کی قید بن جائیں کیونکہ حال ذوالحال کے لئے قید ہوتا ہے اور تسمیہ وتحمید میں قید اور حال ہونے کے اعتبار سے تسویہ و برابری پائی
His saying 'Bismillah al-Rahman al-Rahim': This is the first part of the commentary's expression. The purpose of this expression is to explain the grammatical analysis. The conclusion is that in 'Bismillah', 'Ba' is a preposition. It, along with its object, becomes a circumstantial adverbial (zarf mustaqarr) related to 'mutabarrik' (seeking blessing), and 'mutabarrik' is a circumstantial clause from the pronoun 'ana' of 'abtadi' (I begin), and 'hamid' is a second circumstantial clause from the pronoun 'ana' of 'abtadi'. The translation would be: I begin in the state that I am one who seeks blessing with the name of Allah, the Most Gracious, the Most Merciful, and I begin in the state that I am one who praises Allah in the first and second instances. Benefit (2): Apparently from the commentator's speech, it seems that 'Bismillah' is a vague adverbial (zarf laghw) and is related to 'abtada' (I began), but in reality it is not so. Rather, the preposition and its object together become a specific adverbial (zarf mustaqarr) related to 'mutabarrik' or 'mutayamman' (seeking blessing), and evidence for this is the commentator's statement that he made 'kitab' the object of 'abtadi', whereas if it were a vague adverbial, the tasmiyah would stand in place of the object. So it became clear that it is related to 'mutabarrik' and it is a circumstantial clause from the pronoun 'ana' of 'abtadi', and its object is 'kitab'.
The wisdom of deviating from the common method in hamd:
His saying 'Aathar' (he preferred): This is the second part of the commentary. The purpose of this expression is to answer an implicit question. The question is: Why did the author deviate from the common method of hamd, i.e., nominal sentence or verbal sentence? Answer: The author originally wanted to create equality between hamd and tasmiyah. And the author created equality in two ways. Number 1: Just as he made 'Bismillah' a circumstantial clause from the pronoun 'ana' of 'abtadi', he also made 'hamid' a circumstantial clause from the pronoun 'ana' so that both become conditions for the beginning, because a circumstantial clause is a condition for its owner. And in tasmiyah and tahmid, from the perspective of being a condition and a circumstantial clause, equality is found.
Source pages p. 91

Commentary
This passage continues the grammatical analysis of the author's preface. The commentator clarifies that the basmala is not a vague adverbial (zarf laghw) but a specific adverbial (zarf mustaqarr) related to 'mutabarrik' (seeking blessing), which itself is a hal from the hidden pronoun 'ana' of 'abtadi'. This is evidenced by the commentator making 'kitab' the direct object of 'abtadi', which would not be possible if the basmala were a vague adverbial. Then the commentator addresses why the author avoided the common method of expressing hamd (e.g., 'al-hamdu lillah' or 'ahmadu Allah'). The answer is that the author wanted to achieve equality between basmala and hamd by making both circumstantial clauses (hal) from the same pronoun 'ana'. This way, both tasmiyah and tahmid become conditions (qayd) for the beginning, and they are equal in grammatical status. This is a sophisticated linguistic choice to honor both hadiths while prioritizing basmala in order.

Key Terms
ظرف مستقر (zarf mustaqarr): A circumstantial adverbial that specifies a location or state and is not vague; it has a specific relation to a verb or verbal noun, and cannot be omitted without changing meaning.
ظرف لغو (zarf laghw): A vague or redundant adverbial that can be omitted without affecting the core meaning, often simply related to the verb.
حال (hal): A circumstantial clause describing the state of the subject or object at the time of the action.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the commentator, why did the author make 'hamid' a circumstantial clause rather than using a common form like 'al-hamdu lillah'?
A) To make hamd subordinate to basmala.
B) To achieve equality between hamd and tasmiyah by making both circumstantial clauses.
C) Because Arabic grammar does not allow nominal sentences in the preface.
D) To follow the hadith literally without interpretation.

Key Takeaway
The basmala is a specific circumstantial adverbial (zarf mustaqarr) describing the state of the one who begins, and the author deliberately crafted both basmala and hamd as circumstantial clauses to achieve grammatical equality, honoring both aspects of the double hadith.

The Grammatical Status of Basmalah in Hanafi Legal Commentaries
Grammatical analysis of basmalah in Sharh al-Taozeeh

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to distinguish between zarf mustaqirr and zarf laghw and explain the correct grammatical analysis of the basmalah in the commentary's opening.

Core Idea
Basmalah is not a dispensable adverb; it is an integral zarf mustaqirr functioning as a hal.

This lesson examines the grammatical analysis of the basmalah as presented in a Hanafi legal commentary. Understanding whether the prepositional phrase 'bismillah' is a mere introductory dispensation (zarf laghw) or an integral part of the sentence (zarf mustaqirr) is crucial for grasping the commentator's method of textual analysis and its implications for legal interpretation.

Guided Path
1
Identify the two competing analyses
Recognize that the apparent reading suggests 'bismillah' is a zarf laghw related to 'ibtida'' (beginning), while the correct reading posits it as a zarf mustaqirr related to 'mutabarak' (the one seeking blessing).
Zarf laghw is syntactically dispensable; zarf mustaqirr is integral.
2
Examine the evidence against zarf laghw
The commentator made 'al-kitab' the object of 'abtadi'u'. If 'bismillah' were zarf laghw, it would substitute for the object, making 'al-kitab' redundant. Thus, 'bismillah' cannot be zarf laghw.
The object position is filled, so 'bismillah' must have another role.
3
Confirm the correct analysis
Since 'bismillah' is not zarf laghw, it must be zarf mustaqirr related to 'mutabarak', which itself is a hal (circumstantial accusative) describing the state of the speaker when they say 'I begin'.
This yields the translation: 'I begin in a state of seeking blessing with the name of Allah...'
4
Appreciate the implication for textual analysis
The basmalah becomes an integral part of the sentence structure, not a mere introductory phrase. This affects how the phrase is interpreted in legal contexts, such as the requirement of basmalah in certain acts.
In usul al-fiqh, grammatical precision shapes legal derivation (istinbat).

قوله بسم الرحمن الرحیم :۔ یہ شرح کی عبارت کا پہلا حصہ ہے اس عبارت سے غرض شارع ترکیبی تحقیق کو بیان کرنا ہے۔ جس کا حاصل یہ ہے کہ بسم اللہ میں سب حرف جار ۔ یہ اپنے مجرور سے مل کر ظرف مستقر ہو کر متبر کا کے متعلق ہے اور متبر کا حال ہے ابہا امی کی انا ضمیر سے اور حامد ابدی کی انا ضمیر سے حال ثانی ہے ترجمہ ہوگا میں ابتداء کرتا ہوں اس حال میں کہ میں برکت حاصل کرنے والا ہوں اللہ کے نام کے ساتھ جو بڑا مہربان نہایت رحم کرنے والا ہے ( اور ابتداء کرتا ہوں ) اس حال میں کہ حمد بیان کرنے والا ہوں اللہ کی پہلی مرتبہ اور دوسری مرتبہ۔ فائدہ (۲):۔ بظاہر شاریخ کی کلام سے معلوم ہوتا ہے کہ بسم اللہ یہ ظرف لغو ہے اور ابتدگی کے متعلق ہے حالانکہ حقیقت میں ایسے نہیں ہے بلکہ جار مجرور مل کر یہ متبر کا یا مٹیمنا کے متعلق ہو کر ظرف مستقر ہے اور اس پر قرینہ شاریخ کی کلام ہے کہ انہوں نے کتاب کو ابدی کا مفعول بنایا ہے حالانکہ ظرف لغو کی صورت میں تسمیہ مفعول کے قائم مقام ہوگا ۔ معلوم ہوا کہ یہ متبر کا سے متعلق ہے اور وہ حال ہے ابدی کی انا ضمیر سے اور اس کا مفعول کتاب ہے۔
His statement: 'In the name of Allah, the Most Gracious, the Most Merciful': This is the first part of the commentary’s expression. The commentator’s purpose from this expression is to explain the syntactic analysis. The outcome is that in 'bismillah', the letter 'ba' is a preposition. It, together with its governed genitive, becomes a 'zarf mustaqirr' and is related to 'mutabarak' (the one seeking blessing), and 'mutabarak' is a 'hal' (circumstantial accusative) from the pronoun 'ana' of 'abtadi'u', and 'hamid' (praising) is a second 'hal' from the pronoun 'ana' of 'abtadi'u'. The translation: 'I begin in a state of seeking blessing with the name of Allah, who is Most Gracious, Most Merciful, (and I begin) in a state of praising Allah the first time and the second time.' Benefit (2): Apparently from the commentator’s words it seems that 'bismillah' is a 'zarf laghw' (adverb of void) related to 'ibtida'' (beginning), but in reality it is not so; rather, the preposition and its governed noun together become related to 'mutabarak' or 'mutayamman' as a 'zarf mustaqirr'. The evidence for this is the commentator’s own words: he made 'al-kitab' the object of 'abtadi'u', whereas in the case of 'zarf laghw', the 'tasmiyah' (mentioning Allah's name) would stand in place of the object. It is thus understood that it is related to 'mutabarak', and that is a 'hal' from the pronoun 'ana' of 'abtadi'u', and its object is 'al-kitab'.
Source pages p. 91

Commentary
This passage is a grammatical analysis of the basmalah phrase in the commentary's opening. The commentator explains that the preposition 'ba' together with its governed noun forms a 'zarf mustaqirr' (a locative adverb meaning 'in/with') that is connected to the implied word 'mutabarak' (one who seeks blessing). This 'zarf mustaqirr' functions as a 'hal' (circumstantial accusative) describing the state of the speaker when they say 'I begin'. The benefit clarifies that this is not a 'zarf laghw' (an adverb that is syntactically dispensable) as might be wrongly inferred from the commentator's wording. The evidence is that the commentator made 'al-kitab' the object of 'abtadi'u', which would be incorrect if 'bismillah' were a 'zarf laghw' because then 'bismillah' itself would take the object position. Therefore, the correct analysis shows the basmalah is an integral part of the sentence structure, not a mere introductory phrase.

Key Terms
ظرف مستقر (zarf mustaqirr): A locative adverb that is an integral part of the sentence, requiring a related noun (here, 'mutabarak').
ظرف لغو (zarf laghw): A dispensable adverb that does not fundamentally affect the sentence structure; often an introductory phrase.
حال (hal): A circumstantial accusative describing the state of the subject or object at the time of the action.
متبارک (mutabarak): One who seeks blessing; the implied noun to which the zarf mustaqirr 'bismillah' is related.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
In the grammatical analysis of 'bismillah' in this passage, what is the role of the prepositional phrase 'bismillah'?
A) It is a 'zarf laghw' related to 'ibtida'', acting as a substitute for the object.
B) It is a 'zarf mustaqirr' related to 'mutabarak', functioning as a 'hal'.
C) It is the direct object of 'abtadi'u'.
D) It is a separated adverb of time.

Key Takeaway
Basmalah in legal commentaries serves as an integral zarf mustaqirr (hal) related to the seeker of blessing, not a dispensable adverb.
