Textual Analysis of 'Hamida' as Hal in Usul Sharh
Grammatical and textual analysis of 'hamida' as hal

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify the grammatical issue of 'hal' in a usul text and evaluate arguments for different manuscript readings.

Core Idea
A single grammatical analysis can determine the meaning and integrity of a legal text.

This passage from a sharh on al-Tawdih examines whether the word 'hamida' (praising) is a circumstantial accusative (hal) referring to the subject of 'yaqulu' or to an implied 'ibtida''. The resolution affects the interpretation of the phrase and the internal consistency of the matn. We will walk through the arguments and see how manuscript variants and authorial intent interact.

Guided Path
1
Identify the grammatical issue
Pinpoint the word 'hamida' and the two possible references for its hal: the pronoun of 'yaqulu' (he says) or the pronoun of an implied 'ibtida'' (beginning).
The hal describes the state of the agent.
2
Understand the objection
Some scholars claim that making 'hamida' a hal from 'yaqulu' leads to repetition of praising. Analyze why this objection is incorrect by reinterpreting the genitive of 'ba'da'.
If the genitive is 'al-ibtida' bi al-tasmiyah', the meaning is: after beginning with basmalah, he says while praising.
3
Analyze the preference for the old manuscript
The author states that in the old version, the hal from 'yaqulu' is apparent because no defect arises. Note the reasoning: the hal from 'yaqulu' is 'from inside the book' since basmalah is not part of the book per al-Tanqih.
Inside the book = referring to the text after the basmalah; outside = referring to the basmalah itself.
4
Evaluate the counterargument about equality
A question suggests that equality between tasmiyah and hamd is lost if hal is from 'yaqulu'. The response argues that even if basmalah were part of the book, connecting post-basmalah text to it is not customary among authors.
This shows that authorial custom (urf al-muallifin) is a consideration in textual analysis.
5
Reflect on the benefit and version change
The passage ends with a benefit: perhaps the old version was intentionally changed to avoid the hal from 'yaqulu' and to achieve the intended equality. This illustrates how manuscript variants can be motivated by interpretive goals.
Such textual criticism is a key skill in usul al-fiqh.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
فائدہ : ۔ بعض حضرات نے فرمایا ہے کہ ایک تیسری خرابی بھی لازم آتی ہے کہ اگر حامدا کو ضمیر یقول سے حال بنا ئیں تو معنی خلاف مقصود ہو جائے گا کیونکہ اس وقت معنی ہوگا۔ بعد الحمد والصلوة يقول خامد ا حمد وصلوٰۃ کے بعد بندہ کہتا ہے اس حال میں کہ حمد بیان کرنے والا ہے اور یہ تکرار محض ہے لیکن یہ درست نہیں ہے۔ کیونکہ اس صورت میں بعد کا مضاف الیہ حمد وصلوٰۃ نہیں ہوگی ۔ بلکہ ابتداء بالتسمیہ ہوگا۔ تقدیر عبارت ہوگی۔ بعد الابتداء بالتسمیہ یقول حامدا ۔ یعنی ابتداء بالتسمیہ کے بعد کہتا ہے بندہ اس حال میں کہ وہ تعریف کرنے والا ہے۔ تو اس صورت میں معنی درست ہے اور تکرار لازم نہیں آتا ۔ ہاں اگر نسخہ قدیمہ ہو تو اس وقت ظاہر یہی ہے کہ حامدا؟ ضمیر یقول سے حال ہے کیونکہ اس وقت کوئی خرابی لازم نہیں آتی ۔
سوال: نسخہ قدیمہ میں اگر خامد ا کو یقول کی ضمیر سے حال بنائیں تو تسمیہ و حمید میں برابری باقی نہیں رہتی حالانکہ مقصودان دونوں میں تسویہ اور برابری پیدا کرنا ہے تو شاریخ نے یہ کیسے کہ دیا کہ ظاہر یہی ہے کہ یقول کی ضمیر سے حال ہے۔ جواب: - حامد کو اگر ضمیر یقول سے حال بنائیں تو یہ حال ہو گا۔ داخل کتاب سے اور اگر ابتدئی کی ضمیر سے حال بنائیں تو یہ حال ہو گا خارج کتاب سے کیونکہ خود مصنف نے تنقیح میں تصریح کی ہے۔ کہ بسم اللہ کتاب کا جز نہیں ہے ۔ لہذا داخل کتاب سے حال بنانا خارج کتاب سے حال سے بنانے سے زیادہ بہتر ہے۔ سوال :۔ یہ تو کوئی ضروری نہیں کہ مصنف نے تنقیح میں اگر تسمیہ کو کتاب کا جز نہیں بنایا تو توضیح میں بھی تسمیہ کو جزء کتاب نہ بنایا ہو۔ بلکہ تسویہ کے قرینہ سے یہ معلوم ہوتا ہے۔ کہ تسمیہ کتاب کا جزء ہے پھر جب یہ کتاب کا جزء ہے تو ابتدئی سے حال بنانے کی صورت میں بھی داخل کتاب سے حال ہوگا۔
جواب: اگر مان بھی لیں کہ تسمیہ کتاب کا جزء ہے پھر بھی کہتے ہیں کہ حامد ا کو یقول کی ضمیر سے حال بنانا ظاہر ہے کیونکہ بسم اللہ کے مابعد کوبسم اللہ سے متعلق کرنا بین المصنفین معہو دو متعارف نہیں ہے۔
فائدہ:۔ شاید اسی وجہ سے نسخہ قدیمہ تبدیل کیا گیا ہے تاکہ یقول کی ضمیر سے حال نہ بنے اور تسویسی تحقیق ہو جائے۔
Benefit: Some scholars have said that a third defect also arises: if we make 'hamida' a hal from the pronoun of 'yaqulu', the meaning becomes contrary to the intended purpose, because then the meaning would be: 'After al-hamd and al-salah, the servant says while he is one who praises' — and this is pure repetition. But this is not correct, because in this case the genitive of 'ba'da' would not be 'hamd' and 'salah', but rather it would be 'al-ibtida' bi al-tasmiyah'. The estimation of the phrase would be: 'After the beginning with the basmalah, he says while praising.' So in this case the meaning is correct and no repetition is necessary. Yes, if it is the old version, then the apparent is that 'hamida' is a hal from the pronoun of 'yaqulu', because no defect arises then. Question: In the old version, if we make 'hamida' a hal from the pronoun of 'yaqulu', then equality between tasmiyah and hamd is not maintained, even though the intended purpose is to create equality between the two. So how did the commentators say that the apparent is that it is a hal from the pronoun of 'yaqulu'? Answer: If we make 'hamida' a hal from the pronoun of 'yaqulu', then this hal is from inside the book; if we make it a hal from the pronoun of 'ibtida'', then it is from outside the book, because the author himself has stated in al-Tanqih that the basmalah is not part of the book. Therefore, making it a hal from inside the book is better than making it a hal from outside the book. Question: This is not necessary that if the author did not make the basmalah part of the book in al-Tanqih, then in al-Tawdih he also did not make it part of the book. Rather, from the context of equality it is known that the basmalah is part of the book; then when it is part of the book, making it a hal from 'ibtida'' would also be from inside the book. Answer: Even if we admit that the basmalah is part of the book, still we say that making 'hamida' a hal from the pronoun of 'yaqulu' is apparent, because connecting what comes after the basmalah to the basmalah is not customary among the authors. Benefit: Perhaps for this reason the old version was changed, so that it would not be a hal from 'yaqulu' and the verification of equality would be achieved.
Source pages p. 95

Commentary
This passage is a grammatical and textual analysis from a usul sharh. It discusses the correct interpretation of the phrase 'بعد الحمد والصلوة يقول حامدا' (after praise and prayer, he says, praising). The issue is whether the word 'حامدا' (praising) is a hal (circumstantial accusative) referring to the subject of 'يقول' (he says) or to the implied subject of the implicit verb 'ابتدأ' (begin). The author resolves that in the old manuscript version, making it a hal from 'يقول' is apparent and does not lead to repetition if the genitive of 'بعد' is taken as 'الابتداء بالتسمية' (the beginning with the basmalah) rather than 'الحمد والصلوة'. A question arises that equality between tasmiyah and hamd is lost, but the answer is that making it a hal from 'يقول' is from inside the book (since the basmalah is not part of the book according to the author's Tanqih), and is therefore preferred. A second question suggests that the basmalah might be part of the book, but the reply is that even so, connecting the post-basmalah text to the basmalah is not customary, so the older version's reading is still apparent. The passage concludes with a benefit noting that the version may have been changed intentionally to preserve equality.

Key Terms
حال (hal): A circumstantial accusative describing the state of the agent.
نسخہ قدیمہ (nuskha qadima): The old manuscript version of the text.
تسویہ (taswiyah): Equality; here meaning parity between mentioning the basmalah and praising.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, why is it better to make 'hamida' a hal from the pronoun of 'yaqulu' in the old manuscript?
A) Because it avoids any repetition.
B) Because it keeps the hal inside the book, not outside.
C) Because the basmalah is part of the book.
D) Because the author prefers it.

Key Takeaway
Grammatical analysis in usul al-fiqh must consider internal textual evidence and authorial custom to resolve interpretive disputes.

The Meaning of 'Awwalan' and 'Thaniyan' in the Author's Praise
Commentary on the author's use of 'awwalan' and 'thaniyan'

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify the three interpretations of 'awwalan' and 'thaniyan' in the author's praise and apply the Hanafi usul principle that 'hamd' can be used metaphorically for 'madah' using Quranic evidence.

Core Idea
Praise (hamd) can be metaphorical for eulogy (madah), allowing praise of Allah's essence.

This passage is a commentary (sharh) that unpacks the author's introductory praise of Allah. The commentator explores the meaning of the words 'awwalan' (first) and 'thaniyan' (second), offering three interpretations. Understanding these interpretations reveals how the Hanafi tradition handles metaphorical language in Qur'anic usage and its implications for usul al-fiqh.

Guided Path
1
Identify the three interpretations
Read the passage to list the three possibilities for what 'awwalan' and 'thaniyan' refer to: essential vs. favor praise, first/second creation/preservation, and this world vs. Hereafter.
The commentator presents these as 'three aspects' (wujuh thalathah).
2
Analyze the objection and answer
Focus on the objection that hamd is for voluntary acts, so how can one praise Allah's essence? Note the answer: hamd is used metaphorically (majaz) for madah (eulogy), which applies to voluntary and involuntary acts.
This is the key usul point.
3
Examine the Quranic dalil
Locate the verse Quran 17:79 ('maqaman mahmuda') and understand how it proves that hamd can be used for non-voluntary things.
The verse uses 'mahmuda' for a station not chosen by the Prophet.
4
Map the second interpretation to Qur'anic surahs
The second interpretation links 'awwalan' to first creation/preservation and 'thaniyan' to second creation/preservation. Identify the surahs cited (al-Fatihah, al-An'am, al-Kahf, Saba', Fatir).
The author follows the pattern of these surahs.
5
Synthesize the usul principle
Derive the principle: linguistic usage can extend literal meanings when supported by Qur'anic evidence. This illustrates the Hanafi approach to majaz.

کی طرف۔ پس مصنف اللہ کی حمد بیان کرتا ہے دونوں قسموں پر ان سورتوں کی اقتداء کرتے ہوئے جن کو حمد کے ساتھ شروع کیا گیا ہے۔ اس حیثیت سے کہ سورۃ فاتحہ میں تمام کی طرف اور سورہ انعام میں ایجاد اولی کی طرف اور سورہ الکہف میں ابقاء اولی کی طرف اور سباء میں ایجاد ثانوی کی طرف اور سورہ ملائکہ میں ابقاء ثانوی کی طرف اشارہ ہے۔ تیسرا احتمال رعایت کرنا اللہ تعالیٰ کے قول ولہ الحمد فی الا ولی والآخرہ کی۔ اس معنی پر محمول کرتے ہوئے کہ وہ حمد کا مستحق ہے دنیا میں جیسا کہ دلائل سے اس کا کمال پہچانا گیا ہے۔ اور بندوں تک اس کی عطا پہنچتی ہے اور آخرت میں حمد کا مستحق ہے جیسا کہ اس کی کبریائی کا مشاہدہ کیا جائے گا۔ اور اس کی ایسی نعمتوں کا نظارہ ہوگا ۔ جن کو کسی آنکھ نے نہیں دیکھا اور نہ کسی کان نے سنا ہے اور نہ کسی بشر کے دل پر کھٹکی ہیں اور اسی کی طرف اشارہ ہے۔ اس کے قول وآخر دعواهم ان الحمد لله رب العلمین (جنت میں ان کی باہم گفتگو یہی ہوگی کہ تمام تعریفیں اللہ کے لئے ہیں جو تمام جہانوں کے پروردگار ہیں ) پس اگر تو کہے کہ تحقیق تعرض واقع ہو چکا ہے اللہ تعالی کی عظیم ذات پر اور دنیا اور آخرت کی نعمتوں پر پھر اس کے قول والعنان الثناء الیہ ثانیا ( اس کا عطف حامد اپر ڈالتے ہوئے ) کا کیا معنی ہے؟ میں کہتا ہوں کہ اس کا معنی و مطلب اللہ کی عظمت بیان کرنے کا قصد کرنا ہے اور اس کے قریب ہونے کی نیت کرنا ہے ہر اس چیز میں جو اس کی صلاحیت رکھتی ہے۔ اقوال سے افعال سے اموال خرچ کرنے سے عبادات کی مختلف انواع کی طرف اشارہ کرتے ہوئے۔ پس اللہ تعالیٰ کی نعمتیں واجب کرتی ہیں تشکر کو دل سے زبان سے اور اعضاء سے اور حمد نہیں ہو سکتی مگر زبان سے۔ اور اس میں اشارہ ہے کہ علوم اسلامیہ کو شروع کرنے والے کے لیے مناسب ہے کہ منہ موڑے مخلوق کی طرف سے اور پھیرے تعریف کی لگاموں کو تمام اطراف سے حق تعالیٰ کی طرف جو بلند و برتر اور پاک ذات ہے اس بات کو جانتے ہوئے کہ ثناء کی مستحق صرف وہی ایک ذات ہے۔ لغوی تحقیق: الملا حظہ۔ باب مفاعلہ کا مصدر ہے بمعنی ایک دوسرے کو دیکھنا غور وفکر کرنا۔ تاسیا۔ باب تفعیل سے اصل معنی ہے تسلی دینا۔ صبر کرنا۔ لیکن اس کا صلہ (ب) آ جائے تو اس کا معنی ہوتا ہے۔ پیروی کرنا۔ اقتداء کرنا اور یہاں یہی معنی مراد ہے۔ نوال بخشش ۔ حصہ درستی؟ یہاں بخشش و عطاء والا معنی مراد ہے۔ خطرت باب ضرب اور نصر سے اس کا معنی ہے سوجھنا۔ خیال آنا ۔ اولا و ثانیا کی مرادی تحقیق تشریح : واما تفصیل الحمد ۔ یہ شرح کی عبارت کا ساتواں حصہ ہے۔ اور غرض شارح متن میں آنے والے اولا و ثانیا کے الفاظ کی مرادی تحقیق کو بیان کرنا ہے کہ اس کی مراد میں تین وجوہ و احتمال ہیں اور یہاں وجوہ ثلاثہ میں سے وجہ اول کو بیان کرتے ہیں ۔ جس کا حاصل یہ ہے کہ اللہ کی حمد کبھی نعمت پر کی جاتی ہے کبھی بغیر نعمت کے ۔ گویا کہ اللہ رب العزت مستحق حمد ہیں ذات کی وجہ سے بھی اور انعامات کی وجہ سے بھی تو ماتن نے اولا میں استحقاق ذاتی کی طرف اشارہ کیا اور ثانیا سے استحقاق انعامی کی طرف اشارہ کیا۔ یعنی میں پہلی مرتبہ اللہ کی ذات کی وجہ سے تعریف کرتا ہوں اور دوسری مرتبہ اس کے انعامات پر تعریف کرتا ہوں اور ان میں سے ایک انعام یہ ہے کہ مجھے اتنی بڑی کتاب لکھنے کی توفیق عطاء فرمائی۔ سوال :۔ حد تو محمود کے فعل اختیاری پر ہوتی ہے اور اللہ تعالیٰ کی ذات وصفات اللہ کے لیے غیر اختیاری ہیں ورنہ ان کا حادث ہونا لازم آئے گا۔ تو اللہ کی حمد اس کی ذات وصفات پر کیسے ہو سکتی ہے؟ جواب:۔ یہاں حمد مجاز امدح کے معنی میں مستعمل ہے اور مدح فعل اختیاری و غیر اختیاری سب پر ہوتی ہے جیسے ارشاد باری تعالیٰ ہے عیسی ان یبعث ربک مقام محمودا کہ مقام محمود آپ صلى الله عليه وسلمے کے اختیار میں نہیں لیکن اس پر حمد کا اطلاق کیا گیا ہے کیونکہ یبعثگ محمود مدوح کے معنی میں ہے۔ الثانی:۔ یہاں سے وجہ ثانی کا بیان ہے جس کا حاصل یہ ہے کہ تمام انعامات چار چیزوں کی طرف لوٹتے ہیں۔ (۱) ایجاد اولی کی طرف یعنی دنیا کو پیدا کرنا (۲) ابقاء اولی کی طرف یعنی دنیا کو باقی رکھنا (۳) ایجاد ثانوی کی طرف یعنی آخرت کو پیدا کرنا ( ۴) ابقاء ثانوی کی طرف یعنی آخرت کو باقی رکھنا۔ اللہ رب العزت نے ان چار چیزوں کا قرآن میں ذکر کیا ہے۔ جیسا کہ سورۃ الفاتحہ میں رب العلمین میں ایجاد اولی کی طرف اشارہ ہے کیونکہ تربیت ایجاد کے بعد ہو سکتی ہے اور الرحمن الرحیم میں ابقاء اولی کی طرف اشارہ ہے کیونکہ دنیا اللہ کی رحمت سے باقی ہے ملک یوم الدین ایجاد ثانوی کی طرف اشارہ ہے اور ایاک نعبد میں ابقاء ثانوی کی طرف اشارہ ہے کیونکہ عبادت کی وجہ سے انسان ہمیشہ جنت میں رہے گا ۔ اور عدم عبادت کی وجہ سے جہنم میں رہنا ہوگا ۔ اور سورہ انعام میں هُوَ الَّذِي خَلَقَكُمْ مِنْ طِيْنِ الآية میں ایجاد اولی کی طرف اشارہ ہے اور سورۃ الکہف میں الْحَمْدُ لِلَّهِ الَّذِي أَنْزَلَ عَلَى عَبْدِهِ الْكِتَاب الآية میں ابقاء اولی کی طرف اشارہ ہے کیونکہ کتاب اللہ کی وجہ سے دنیا میں نوع انسانی باقی ہے اور سورہ سباء میں وَقَالَ الَّذِينَ كَفَرُوا لَا تَأْتِينَا السَّاعَةُ قُلْ بَلَى وَرَبِّي لَتَأْتِيَنَّكُمُ الآية میں ایجاد ثانوی کی طرف اشارہ ہے اور سورہ فاطر میں جَاعِلِ الْمَلائِكَةِ رُسُلاً میں ابقاء ثانوی کی طرف اشارہ ہے کیونکہ رسلا سے مراد اہل جنت کے ساتھ فرشتوں کی ملاقات اور استقبال مراد ہے تو مصنف نے ان سورتوں کی اتباع کرتے ہوئے اولا کہہ کر ایجاد اولی اور ابقاء اولی کی طرف اشارہ کیا یعنی اللہ کی تعریف کرتا ہوں ایجاد اولی اور ابقاء اولی کی وجہ سے اور ثانیاً کہہ کر اشارہ کیا ایجاد ثانوی اور ابقاء ثانوی کی طرف یعنی میں اللہ تعالیٰ کی تعریف کرتا ہوں ایجاد ثانوی اور ابقاء ثانوی کی وجہ سے۔
Towards. So the author expresses praise of Allah, following both types by following those surahs which begin with praise. In the sense that in Surah Fatihah it refers to all, in Surah An'am it refers to the first creation, in Surah al-Kahf to the first preservation, in Surah Saba' to the second creation, and in Surah Mala'ikah to the second preservation. The third possibility is to regard the saying of Allah 'and to Him belongs praise in the first and the last', interpreting it to mean that He is deserving of praise in the world as His perfection is recognized through proofs, and His gifts reach the servants; and in the Hereafter He is deserving of praise as His greatness will be witnessed, and such blessings will be seen which no eye has seen, no ear has heard, nor have they occurred to any human heart. And to this points His saying 'and their last call is that all praise is for Allah, the Lord of the worlds'. So if you say: indeed the subject has been addressed concerning the great essence of Allah and the blessings of the world and the Hereafter, then what is the meaning of His saying 'and the reins of praise are directed to Him secondly'? I say: its meaning and intent is to intend to express Allah's greatness and to intend to draw near to Him in every thing that has capacity, indicating from words, actions, spending wealth, and various types of worship. So the blessings of Allah oblige gratitude from heart, tongue, and limbs, and praise can only be from the tongue. And in this is an indication that for one who begins Islamic sciences, it is appropriate to turn away from creation and turn the reins of praise from all directions to the Exalted and Pure Truth, knowing that only He is deserving of praise. Lexical investigation: 'al-mulahazah': it is a masdar from bab mufa'alah, meaning looking at each other, contemplation. 'ta'asiyan': from bab taf'il, original meaning is consolation, patience, but if it is connected with the preposition 'bi', its meaning becomes following, imitating, and that is the intended meaning here. 'nawal': gift, portion; here the meaning of gift and donation is intended. 'khatarah': from bab darb and nasr, its meaning is to occur to the mind, to come to mind. Investigation of the meaning of 'awwalan and thaniyan': Commentary: 'wa amma tafsir al-hamd' – this is the seventh part of the commentary's text. And the purpose of the commentator is to explain the meanings of the words 'awwalan and thaniyan' appearing in the text, that there are three aspects and possibilities in their meaning, and here he states the first of the three aspects. Its summary is that praise of Allah is sometimes upon a blessing and sometimes without a blessing. That is, Allah, the Lord of Might, is deserving of praise both by virtue of His essence and by virtue of His favors. So the author indicated in 'awwalan' the essential deserving, and in 'thaniyan' the deserving due to favors. That is: I praise Allah firstly because of His essence, and secondly because of His favors, and among those favors is that He granted me the ability to write this great book. Question: Praise is only for voluntary acts of the praised one, and the essence and attributes of Allah are not voluntary for Him, otherwise it would necessitate their being contingent. So how can praise be upon His essence and attributes? Answer: Here 'hamd' is used metaphorically in the meaning of 'madah' (eulogy), and 'madah' applies to both voluntary and involuntary acts, as in Allah's saying: 'that your Lord may raise you to a praiseworthy station' – the 'praiseworthy station' is not in the choice of the Prophet (peace be upon him), but praise is applied to it because 'muhammad' is in the meaning of 'mamduh' (praised). The second: From here is the explanation of the second aspect. Its summary is that all favors return to four things: (1) the first creation, i.e., creating the world; (2) the first preservation, i.e., preserving the world; (3) the second creation, i.e., creating the Hereafter; (4) the second preservation, i.e., preserving the Hereafter. Allah has mentioned these four things in the Qur'an. For example, in Surah al-Fatihah, 'Lord of the worlds' indicates the first creation because tarbiyah can only occur after creation; 'the Most Merciful, the Especially Merciful' indicates the first preservation because the world remains through Allah's mercy; 'Master of the Day of Judgment' indicates the second creation; 'You alone we worship' indicates the second preservation because through worship man will remain forever in Paradise, and due to lack of worship he will remain in Hell. And in Surah al-An'am, 'It is He who created you from clay' indicates the first creation; in Surah al-Kahf, 'All praise is for Allah who sent down upon His servant the Book' indicates the first preservation because the human species remains in the world through the Book of Allah; in Surah Saba', 'Those who disbelieve say: "The Hour will not come to us." Say: "Yes, by my Lord, it will certainly come to you"' indicates the second creation; and in Surah Fatir, 'Maker of the angels as messengers' indicates the second preservation because 'messengers' refers to the meeting and reception of the angels with the people of Paradise. So the author, following these surahs, by saying 'awwalan' indicated the first creation and first preservation – i.e., I praise Allah because of the first creation and first preservation – and by saying 'thaniyan' indicated the second creation and second preservation – i.e., I praise Allah because of the second creation and second preservation.
Source pages p. 97

Commentary
This passage is a commentary (sharh) on the author's introductory praise of Allah, specifically the meaning of the words 'awwalan' (first) and 'thaniyan' (second) as used by the author of the matn. The commentator explains that there are three possible interpretations for these words. The first possibility: 'awwalan' refers to praise for Allah's essence (essential deserving), and 'thaniyan' refers to praise for His blessings (deserving due to favors). A question arises: since hamd (praise) is typically for voluntary actions, how can one praise Allah's essence which is not voluntary? The answer is that 'hamd' here is used metaphorically in the sense of 'madah' (eulogy), which can be for both voluntary and involuntary things, as in the Quranic phrase 'maqaman mahmuda' (a praiseworthy station) which is not voluntary for the Prophet. The second possibility: all blessings reduce to four categories: first creation (creating the world), first preservation (keeping the world in existence), second creation (creating the Hereafter), and second preservation (keeping the Hereafter eternal). The commentator then maps these four categories to specific verses in the Quran: Surah al-Fatihah, al-An'am, al-Kahf, Saba', and Fatir. The author's 'awwalan' indicates the first two categories, and 'thaniyan' indicates the last two. The third possibility is mentioned briefly: referring to Allah's statement 'and to Him belongs praise in the first and the last', meaning He is deserving of praise in this world and the Hereafter. The commentary is based strictly on the matn and does not introduce outside rulings.

Key Terms
اولا (awwalan): The first part of the author's praise; according to one interpretation, it refers to praise for Allah's essence.
ثانیا (thaniyan): The second part of the author's praise; according to one interpretation, it refers to praise for Allah's blessings or for the second creation and preservation.
حمد (hamd): Praise; in this context, it is used metaphorically to mean eulogy (madah) which can apply to both voluntary and involuntary acts.
مدح (madah): Eulogy; it applies to both voluntary and involuntary actions, as opposed to hamd which is typically for voluntary acts.
ایجاد اولی (ijād ulā): The first creation, i.e., the creation of the world.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the first interpretation, what does the author's use of 'awwalan' (first) indicate?
A) Praise for the creation of the world
B) Praise for Allah's essence
C) Praise for the blessings of the Hereafter
D) Praise for the preservation of the world

Key Takeaway
The author's use of 'awwalan' and 'thaniyan' can be interpreted in three ways, with the key usul point that 'hamd' can be metaphorical for 'madah', enabling praise of Allah's essence.

The Condition of Hal and Customary Extension (Urf) in Hanafi Usul
Objection and answer regarding the condition of the state (hal) being concurrent with its factor.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain how Hanafi usul extends the condition of concurrency for the state (hal) through customary ('urfi) time frames and apply this principle to resolve grammatical objections.

Core Idea
Customary extension makes a state concurrent even if not instantaneous.

This lesson examines a classic grammatical objection regarding the basmalah: the state (hal) must be concurrent with its factor, but the states mentioned in the basmalah do not occur at the exact moment of starting. The commentator resolves this by reinterpreting the grammar and invoking customary extension—a key Hanafi usul tool. Understanding this principle helps you appreciate how Hanafi scholars use 'urf (custom) to maintain textual coherence.

Guided Path
1
Identify the objection
The condition for a state (hal) is concurrency with its factor. The objector claims that the states 'praising' etc. are not concurrent with the beginning of the basmalah.
The factor here is the verb 'abtadi' (I begin).
2
Analyze the grammatical reanalysis
The commentator states that the ba' is not a part of the verb; rather, the prepositional phrase 'bismillah' is an adverbial (zarf) functioning as a state (hal). Thus the meaning becomes 'Seeking blessing with the name of Allah, I begin the book.'
This changes the grammatical function, making the state explicit.
3
Apply customary extension
'Beginning' is not an instantaneous moment but a customary process extending from the initial intent of composition to the start of research. During this period, the state of seeking blessing persists, fulfilling concurrency.
Hanafi usul accepts 'urfi (customary) time frames for such conditions.
4
Note the Hanafi usul significance
This principle extends beyond grammar: in legal reasoning, continuity and concurrency can be established through customary understanding, as seen in acts of worship requiring continuity.
This is a standard tool in Hanafi usul to resolve apparent temporal conflicts.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
فَإِن قُلتَ : مِن شَرطِ الحَالِ المُقَارَنَةُ لِلعَامِلِ وَالْاحَوَالُ المَذْكُورَةُ أَعْنِي حَامِدًا وَغَيرَهُ لا تُقَارِنُ الابْتِدَاءَ بِالتّسْمِيَةِ قُلتُ : لَيسَ البَاءُ صِلَةٌ لَّا بَتَدِى بَل الظرف حَالٌ وَالمَعنى مُتَبَرِّكًا بِسمِ اللَّهِ أَبتَدِى الكِتَابَ وَالابْتِدَاءُ أَمرٌ عُرفِيٌّ يُعتَبَرُ مُمتَدًّا مِن حِينِ الأَحَدِ فِى التّصنِيفِ إِلَى الشُّرُوعَ فِي البَحثِ وَيُقَارِنُهُ التَّبَرُّك
For if you say: Among the conditions of the state (hal) is that it be concurrent with its factor, and the mentioned states, i.e., 'praising' and others, are not concurrent with the beginning of the basmalah. I say: The ba' is not a part of the word 'I begin' (abtadi), rather the adverbial (zarf) is a state (hal), and the meaning is: 'Seeking blessing with the name of Allah, I begin the book.' And 'beginning' is a customary matter that is considered extended from the time of the beginning in composition until starting the research, and seeking blessing is concurrent with it.
Source pages p. 100

Commentary
This passage addresses a grammatical objection regarding the basmalah. The objection states that the state (hal) must be concurrent with its factor (the verb 'starting'), but the states mentioned (like 'praising') are not occurring at the exact moment of starting the basmalah. The commentator answers by reinterpreting the grammar: the prepositional phrase 'with the name of Allah' is not an object of the verb 'I begin' but rather an adverbial (zarf) functioning as a state (hal). Thus the meaning is 'Seeking blessing with the name of Allah, I begin the book.' Moreover, 'beginning' is a customary process that extends from the initial intent of composition to the actual start of research. During this extended period, the state of 'seeking blessing' persists and is therefore concurrent. This is a standard Hanafi usul approach: considering customary (urfi) time frames for legal and grammatical analysis.

Key Terms
حال (hal): A grammatical state that describes the condition of the subject/object during the action; must be concurrent with the factor.
عامل ('amil): The grammatical factor (typically a verb or verbal noun) that governs the case and temporal relation of the state.
عرفي ('urfi): Customary; based on common practice rather than literal definition.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
How does the commentator resolve the objection that the state (hal) is not concurrent with its factor in the basmalah?
A) By reinterpreting the state as an adjective
B) By arguing that the factor is not the verb but a nominal sentence
C) By explaining that 'beginning' is a customary extended process from intention to start of research
D) By denying that concurrency is a condition for the state

Key Takeaway
Hanafi usul employs customary extension ('urf) to satisfy the condition of concurrency between a state and its factor, allowing for legal and linguistic validity.

Reason for Salawat After Hamd and Omission of Prophet's Name
Commentary on why the author mentions salawat after hamd

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain why Hanafi authors structure their prefaces with tahmid followed by tasliyah, and evaluate the reasons for omitting explicit mention of the Prophet's name.

Core Idea
The Prophet is the greatest benefactor; salawat after hamd is obligatory gratitude.

This passage from the commentary on al-Tawdīḥ wa al-Talwīḥ addresses a subtle but important aspect of scholarly writing: why the author begins with praise of Allah followed by blessings upon the Prophet, and why in some versions the Prophet's name is not explicitly stated. Understanding this reveals deeper principles of gratitude (shukr) and reverence (taẓīm) that govern Hanafi textual practice.

Guided Path
1
Identify the two questions
The commentator addresses two implicit questions: (1) Why is salawat placed after hamd? (2) Why is the Prophet's name omitted in one manuscript tradition? Recognize that these are separate issues, both relating to the matn's structure.
2
Analyze the first answer: gratitude for the greatest blessing
The commentator argues that Islam is the greatest blessing, conveyed through the Prophet, who is the benefactor (muḥsin). Thanking a benefactor is intellectually and legally (ʿaqlan wa sharʿan) obligatory. Therefore, salawat follows hamd as an act of gratitude.
The term 'wājib' here indicates a moral-legal obligation, not necessarily a fiqh ruling.
3
Analyze the second answer: omission of the name
The commentator gives two reasons: (1) Arab custom: when exalting someone's greatness, one describes attributes rather than naming; (2) Clarity: the name is omitted only when there is no risk of confusion—here, 'the best of messengers' clearly refers to the Prophet.
This reflects the principle of adab (etiquette) in writing.
4
Synthesize the underlying principles
The passage demonstrates how textual choices are grounded in broader principles: shukr (gratitude), taẓīm (reverence), and wuḍūḥ (clarity). These principles guide the author's structure and wording.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
سوال:۔ ماتن نے تحمید کے بعد تصلیہ علی النبی صلی اللہ علیہ وسلم کو کیوں ذکر کیا؟
جواب:۔ جواب کا حاصل یہ ہے کہ تمام نعمتوں میں سے بڑی نعمت دین اسلام ہے کیونکہ اسی اسلام کی وجہ سے انسان جنت کی نعمتوں کو حاصل کرے گا۔ اور یہ نعمت ہم تک نبی کریم صلی اللہ علیہ وسلم کے واسطہ سے پہنچی ہے تو آپ صلی اللہ علیہ وسلم محسن ہوئے اور محسن کے احسان کا شکریہ ادا کرنا عقلاً اور شرعاً واجب ہے۔ اس لیے ماتن نے تحمید کے بعد تصلیہ علی النبی صلی اللہ علیہ وسلم کو ذکر کیا تا کہ آپ صلی اللہ علیہ وسلم کے احسان کا شکر یہ ادا ہو سکے۔
قولہ وفی ترک التصریح:- یہ عبارت کا دوسرا حصہ ہے۔ اس میں شاریخ نے ایک سوال کا جواب دیا ہے ۔ سوال سمجھنے سے پہلے یہ ذہن میں رکھنا ضروری ہے کہ توضیح و تلویح کے دو نسخے ہیں ایک نسخہ میں لفظ محمدصلی اللہ علیہ وسلم کا ذکر ہے اور دوسرے میں نہیں ہے۔ جس نسخہ میں آپ صلی اللہ علیہ وسلم کے نام کا ذکر نہیں ہے تو اس پر یہ اعتراض ہوتا ہے کہ حضور صلی اللہ علیہ وسلم کے نام نامی کو صراحتا ذ کر کیوں نہیں فرمایا ؟
جواب:۔ دووجہ سے آپ صلى الله عليه وسلم کا نام نامی صراحۃ ذکر نہیں کیا نمبر (۱) جب اہل عرب کسی کی عظمت بیان کرتے ہیں تو اس کا نام ذکر نہیں کرتے بلکہ وصف ذکر کرتے ہیں۔ اس لیے ماتن نے بھی آپ صلی اللہ علیہ وسلم کی عظمت کو مد نظر رکھتے ہوئے نام نامی اسم گرامی ذکر نہیں کیا نمبر (۲) دوسری وجہ یہ ہے کہ نام وہاں ذکر کیا جاتا ہے جہاں التباس کا خطرہ ہو اور افضل الرسل سے بدلہہ آپ صلی اللہ علیہ وسلم ہی مراد ہیں اس لیے نام ذکر کرنے کی ضرورت نہیں۔
Question: Why did the author (matn) mention salawat upon the Prophet after hamd? Answer: The conclusion is that the greatest blessing is the religion of Islam, because through this Islam a person will attain the blessings of Paradise. And this blessing reached us through the mediation of the Noble Prophet (peace be upon him), so he is the benefactor, and thanking the benefactor for his favor is intellectually and legally obligatory. Therefore, the author mentioned salawat upon the Prophet after hamd in order to express gratitude for his favor. His statement: 'And regarding the omission of explicit mention' - this is the second part of the passage. In it, the commentator answered a question. Before understanding the question, it is necessary to keep in mind that there are two versions of al-Tawdih and al-Talwih: in one version the word 'Muhammad' is mentioned, and in the other it is not. In the version where the Prophet's name is not mentioned, an objection arises: why did he not explicitly mention the noble name of the Prophet? Answer: He did not explicitly mention the noble name for two reasons: (1) When the Arabs exalt someone's greatness, they do not mention his name but rather his attribute. Therefore, the author, considering the Prophet's greatness, did not mention his name. (2) The second reason is that a name is mentioned where there is a risk of confusion, and here it is clear that the best of messengers is meant, so there is no need to mention the name.
Source pages p. 104

Commentary
This passage is a commentary explaining why the author of the matn mentioned salawat (blessings) upon the Prophet after praising Allah (hamd), and why in some versions the Prophet's name is not explicitly stated. The commentator first addresses the relationship between hamd and salawat: the greatest blessing is Islam, which came through the Prophet, so thanking the Prophet is obligatory. Thus, salawat follows hamd as a form of gratitude. Then, regarding the omission of the name, the commentator gives two reasons based on Arabic custom and clarity: Arabs avoid naming the exalted, and there is no ambiguity here.

Key Terms
تحمید (tahmid): Praising Allah, specifically saying 'Alhamdulillah'.
تصلیہ (tasliyah): Sending blessings (salawat) upon the Prophet.
محسن (muhsin): Benefactor, one who does a favor.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What is the primary reason the author mentions salawat after hamd according to the commentary?
A) To follow the practice of the Arabs.
B) Because the Prophet is the greatest benefactor and thanking him is obligatory.
C) Because it is a mandatory part of the text.
D) To avoid confusion about which messenger is meant.

Key Takeaway
The placement of salawat after hamd and the omission of the Prophet's name are intentional, reflecting principles of gratitude and reverence that shape Hanafi textual style.

Lexical Investigation of Halbah, Mujtaba, and Musalla
Lexical analysis of horse-racing terms in a usul commentary.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to distinguish between the literal and metaphorical meanings of key horse-racing terms used in Hanafi legal texts and identify their etymological derivations.

Core Idea
A word's metaphorical usage can extend its legal scope, as 'halbah' shifts from a group of horses to the racecourse itself.

In this passage, the commentator pauses to investigate the lexical meanings of terms that appear in the matn. Understanding these terms precisely is essential for correctly interpreting legal rulings related to horse racing (sabq). We will explore how 'al-halbah', 'al-mujtaba', 'al-musalla', and 'al-midmar' are defined and derived.

Guided Path
1
Identify the literal meaning of each term
Look at the commentary: for each term, the commentator gives a literal definition. Note the root and literal sense.
Literal meanings are the foundation for metaphorical extensions.
2
Trace the metaphorical extension
See how the literal meaning is applied to a related concept, e.g., 'halbah' from a group of horses to the racecourse.
Metaphor (majaz) is common in legal terminology.
3
Analyze the etymology (ishqaq)
For 'musalla', the commentator derives it from 'shalwayn' (flanks). Understand the derivational process.
Etymology clarifies the semantic connection.
4
Connect to legal application
Explain how these terms would be used in fiqh of horse racing, e.g., to define the starting point or winners.
Precise terminology prevents legal ambiguity.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قولہ والحلبہ :۔ یہ شرح کی عبارت کا تیسرا حصہ ہے۔ غرض شارح لغوی تحقیق کرنا ہے۔ طلبہ اس کا حقیقی معنی ہے گھوڑوں کی وہ جماعت جن کو دوڑانے کے لیے جمع کیا جائے لیکن مجاز اطلبہ اس میدان کو کہتے ہیں جس میں گھوڑ دوڑ ہو۔
فائدہ : ۔ گھوڑ دوڑ کے میدان کو مضمار سے اس لیے تعبیر کیا کہ اس میدان میں گھوڑنے کی تضمیر ہوتی ہے ۔ اور وہ یہ ہے کہ گھوڑے کو خوب کھلایا جاتا ہے اور میدان میں خوب دوڑایا جاتا ہے اس سے وہ دبلا ہوکر سبک رفتار ہو جاتا ہے۔ مجتبی اس گھوڑے کو کہتے ہیں جو دوڑ میں پہلے نمبر پر آئے۔ مصلی اس گھوڑے کو کہتے ہیں جو بجلی کے پیچھے ہو اور دوسرے نمبر پر آئے۔ اس کی وجہ تسمیہ یہ ہے کہ مصلی مشتق ہے تحریک الصلوین سے اور دوسرے گھوڑے کا سر بھی پہلے گھوڑے کی صلوین کے پیچھے ہوتا ہے۔ اس لیے اس کو مصلی کہتے ہیں۔
His statement: 'and al-Halbah' - this is the third part of the commentary's passage. The commentator intends lexical investigation. Its literal meaning is 'a group of horses gathered for racing', but metaphorically it denotes the field where horse racing takes place. Benefit: The racing field is called 'midmar' because in that field the horse is conditioned (tadmir), meaning the horse is fed well and raced thoroughly, becoming lean and swift. 'Mujtaba' is the horse that comes first in the race. 'Musalla' is the horse that follows behind the first and comes second. The reason for naming is that 'musalla' is derived from 'tahrik al-shalwayn' (movement of the two flanks), and the second horse's head is behind the flanks of the first horse. Therefore it is called 'musalla'.
Source pages p. 104

Commentary
This passage provides lexical analysis of the word 'Halbah' and related technical terms used in horse racing, which appear in the matn. The commentator explains that 'Halbah' literally refers to a group of horses gathered for a race, but metaphorically it comes to mean the racecourse itself. The term 'midmar' (race track) is derived from 'tadmir', the process of conditioning a horse by feeding and training it to become light and fast. The winners are 'mujtaba' (first place) and 'musalla' (second place). The etymology of 'musalla' is interesting: it comes from 'shalwayn' (two hipbones), because the second horse's head aligns with the first horse's flanks. These terms illustrate the precise language used in classical texts.

Key Terms
الحلبہ (al-halbah): Literal: a group of horses gathered for racing. Metaphorical: the racecourse.
المجتبی (al-mujtaba): The horse that comes first in the race.
المصلی (al-musalla): The horse that comes second, derived from 'shalwayn' meaning flanks.
المضمار (al-midmar): The race track, from 'tadmir' (conditioning the horse).

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What is the literal meaning of 'al-Halbah'?
A) The race track.
B) A group of horses gathered for racing.
C) The first-place horse.
D) The second-place horse.

Key Takeaway
Understanding the literal and etymological meanings of legal terms is essential for accurate interpretation of Hanafi texts.

Resolving Apparent Contradictions Through Kinayah and Aspect Distinction
Commentary reconciling two descriptions of the one sending salawat

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify when an apparent textual contradiction can be resolved by interpreting terms as kinayah or by distinguishing between different aspects of reference, and apply this method to similar cases.

Core Idea
Apparent contradictions dissolve when we recognize figurative language or shift the aspect of reference.

A careful reader of the matn might notice that the author calls himself both 'mujli' (first) and 'musalli' (second) in sending salawat. This seems contradictory. In this lesson, we analyze how the commentator resolves this tension by offering two distinct explanations. The first treats both terms as kinayah for repetition, eliminating any ranking. The second differentiates the object of salawat: the Prophet (primary) versus his family (secondary). Understanding such resolution techniques is essential for usul al-fiqh, where apparent contradictions in evidence must be harmonized.

Guided Path
1
Identify the Apparent Contradiction
First, recognize what creates the tension: the same person is described as both 'mujli' (one who comes first) and 'musalli' (one who comes second) in the context of sending salawat. If he is first, he cannot be second, and vice versa. Pinpoint the precise source of inconsistency.
The contradiction arises from taking both terms in their literal sense of rank.
2
Analyze the First Answer: Kinayah for Repetition
The first answer reinterprets both 'mujliyan' and 'musalliyan' as kinayah (metonymy) for repeatedly sending salawat. In this interpretation, the speaker is simply emphasizing the abundance of his salawat, with no implication of ranking. Understand how kinayah removes the conflict by shifting meaning from literal ranking to iterative action.
Kinayah is a common tool in usul to resolve literal contradictions.
3
Analyze the Second Answer: Aspect Distinction
The second answer distinguishes the object of salawat: 'mujliyan' refers to salawat upon the Prophet (the primary object), while 'musalliyan' refers to salawat upon his family (the secondary object). Since the family is subordinate, the term 'musalli' (indicating second place) is appropriate. Recognize that a different aspect (al-i'tibar) yields a different description without contradiction.
This is a classic example of resolving a conflict by pointing to different aspects (jihaat) of the same act.
4
Apply to Similar Cases
Now consider a similar apparent contradiction in another text, e.g., a hadith that says 'The best of you is the one who learns the Qur'an and teaches it' and another that says 'The best of you is the one who is best to his family.' How would you resolve this using the techniques above? Identify potential kinayah or aspect distinctions.
Practice trains the mind to see resolution pathways.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قولہ و معنی ذلک: یہ شرح کی عبارت کا چوتھا حصہ ہے۔ غرض اس عبارت سے یہ ہے کہ اس میں شارع نے ایک سوال کے دو جواب دیے ہیں۔ سوال : متن کی عبارت میں تضاد ہے کیونکہ مجلیا سے معلوم ہوتا ہے کہ وہ درود بھیجنے کے میدان میں پہلے نمبر پر آنے والا ہے۔ اور مصلیا سے معلوم ہوتا ہے کہ وہ دوسرے نمبر پر آنے والا ہے۔ اگر پہلے نمبر پر ہے تو دوسرے نمبر پر کیسے؟ اور اگر دوسرے نمبر پر ہے تو پہلے نمبر پر نہیں ہوسکتا۔
جواب (۱): مجلیا ومصلیا یہ دونوں کنا یہ ہیں ۔ تکرار صلوۃ اور تکثیر صلوۃ سے یعنی میں بار بار درود بھیجنے والا ہوں نہ جواب (۲): ملیا نبی صلی اللہ علیہ وسلم پر درود بھیجنے کے اعتبار سے ہے۔ کیونکہ آپ صلی اللہ علیہ وسلم تصلیہ میں مقصود اصلی ہیں۔ اور مصلیا آپ صلی اللہ علیہ وسلم کی آل پر درود بھیجنے کے اعتبار سے ہے کیونکہ آل تصلیہ میں تابع ہے مقصود اصلی نہیں ہے۔ اور تابع ہمیشہ دوسرے نمبر پر ہوتا ہے۔ تو اختلاف حیثیت کی وجہ سے تضاد لازم نہیں آئے گا۔
His statement: 'and the meaning of that' - this is the fourth part of the commentary's passage. The purpose is that the commentator gave two answers to a question. Question: There is a contradiction in the text of the matn, because 'mujliyan' indicates that he is the one who comes first in the field of sending salawat, and 'musalliyan' indicates that he is the one who comes second. If he is first, how can he be second? And if he is second, he cannot be first. Answer (1): 'Mujliyan' and 'musalliyan' are both kinayah (metonymy) for repetition and multiplicity of salawat, i.e., 'I am one who sends salawat repeatedly'. Answer (2): 'Mujliyan' is with regard to sending salawat upon the Prophet himself, because he is the primary object of salawat. And 'musalliyan' is with regard to sending salawat upon his family, because the family is secondary in salawat, not the primary object. The secondary is always in second place. Thus, due to the difference in aspect, no contradiction arises.
Source pages p. 105

Commentary
This passage resolves an apparent contradiction in the matn where the author describes himself as both 'mujli' (first) and 'musalli' (second) in sending salawat. The contradiction is only apparent, and the commentator provides two answers. The first answer interprets both terms as kinayah (metonymy) meaning 'repeatedly sending salawat' — thus no ranking. The second answer distinguishes the object: 'mujliyan' refers to salawat upon the Prophet himself (primary), while 'musalliyan' refers to salawat upon his family (secondary). Since the family is secondary, the term 'musalli' (second place) is appropriate. The point is that different aspects eliminate the contradiction.

Key Terms
مجلیا (mujliyan): Derived from 'ijla' (coming first), here used as kinayah for repeatedly sending salawat or specifically upon the Prophet.
مصلیا (musalliyan): Derived from 'isla' (coming second), here used as kinayah for repeatedly sending salawat or specifically upon the family.
کنایہ (kinayah): Metonymy, a figure of speech where something is referred to indirectly.
تابع (tabi'): Secondary, subordinate; here referring to the family as secondary object.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the commentator's second answer, why does the term 'musalliyan' not contradict 'mujliyan'?
A) Because the Prophet is secondary in salawat.
B) Because 'musalliyan' refers to sending salawat upon the family, which is secondary.
C) Because both terms mean the same thing.
D) Because the matn is unreliable.

Key Takeaway
Apparent contradictions in texts can often be resolved by interpreting terms figuratively (kinayah) or by distinguishing the aspects or objects of the action.

Resolving the Apparent Contradiction in the Matn's Opening
Resolving an apparent contradiction in the matn's wording

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify an apparent textual contradiction in a Hanafi matn and apply the commentator's methodology (ta'wil based on different aspects or metonymy) to resolve it.

Core Idea
An apparent contradiction dissolves when each term is understood within its specific context or as a metonymical expression.

In studying usul al-fiqh, we often analyze the language of foundational texts. The opening passage of Al-Tawdih wa Al-Talwih contains a puzzle: the matn uses 'mujalliyan' (one who comes first) and 'musalliyan' (one who comes second) in the same sentence. How can a person be both first and second? The commentator provides two elegant resolutions, demonstrating how careful attention to context and rhetorical usage eliminates contradiction. This lesson walks through that reasoning, a valuable skill for interpreting legal texts.

Guided Path
1
Identify the apparent contradiction
Locate the two terms 'mujalliyan' and 'musalliyan' in the matn. Note that mujalliyan implies precedence, while musalliyan implies being second in a sequence. The literal reading suggests a conflict.
The contradiction is based on a superficial reading.
2
Analyze the first answer: metonymy (kinaayah)
The commentator suggests that both terms are metonymies, not literal descriptions. 'Mujalliyan' and 'musalliyan' indicate repetition and abundance of sending salawat, not ordinal position.
This removes the contradiction because no actual sequence is implied.
3
Analyze the second answer: different aspects (ikhtilaf al-haythiyyat)
Alternatively, 'mujalliyan' refers to sending salawat upon the Prophet (primary object), and 'musalliyan' refers to sending salawat upon his family (secondary object). The subordinate is always second in rank, so no inconsistency.
Different aspects allow both to be true simultaneously.
4
Evaluate the resolutions
Both resolutions preserve the integrity of the matn. The first relies on rhetorical usage, the second on distinguishing the objects of the action. Recognize that contradictory readings can be harmonized.
This method is common in Hanafi usul for reconciling apparently conflicting texts (ta'arud).
5
Apply the methodology to other cases
Consider similar seeming contradictions in legal texts, e.g., two hadiths where one obligates recitation and the other allows silence. The resolution may involve different aspects (imam vs. alone) or figurative interpretation.
This skill is essential for a faqih or usuli.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ويُحُ لِحَلَ التَّوْضِيح وَالتَّلويح
مجلیا و مصلیا کی مرادی تحقیق
104
قولہ و معنی ذلک: یہ شرح کی عبارت کا چوتھا حصہ ہے۔ غرض اس عبارت سے یہ ہے کہ اس میں شارع نے ایک سوال کے دو جواب دیے ہیں۔ سوال : متن کی عبارت میں تضاد ہے کیونکہ مجلیا سے معلوم ہوتا ہے کہ وہ درود بھیجنے کے میدان میں پہلے نمبر پر آنے والا ہے۔ اور مصلیا سے معلوم ہوتا ہے کہ وہ دوسرے نمبر پر آنے والا ہے۔ اگر پہلے نمبر پر ہے تو دوسرے نمبر پر کیسے؟ اور اگر دوسرے نمبر پر ہے تو پہلے نمبر پر نہیں ہوسکتا۔
جواب (۱): مجلیا ومصلیا یہ دونوں کنا یہ ہیں ۔ تکرار صلوۃ اور تکثیر صلوۃ سے یعنی میں بار بار درود بھیجنے والا ہوں نہ جواب (۲): ملیا نبی صلی اللہ علیہ وسلم پر درود بھیجنے کے اعتبار سے ہے۔ کیونکہ آپ صلی اللہ علیہ وسلم تصلیہ میں مقصود اصلی ہیں۔ اور مصلیا آپ صلی اللہ علیہ وسلم کی آل پر درود بھیجنے کے اعتبار سے ہے کیونکہ آل تصلیہ میں تابع ہے مقصود اصلی نہیں ہے۔ اور تابع ہمیشہ دوسرے نمبر پر ہوتا ہے۔ تو اختلاف حیثیت کی وجہ سے تضاد لازم نہیں آئے گا۔
ثُمَّ لَا يخفى حُسنُ مَا فِي قَرَائِنِ الحَمدِ وَالصَّلَاةِ مِن التَّجنِيسِ وَمَا فِي القَرِينَةِ الثَّانِيَةِ مِن الاسْتِعَارَةِ بِالكِنَايَةِ وَالتَّحْيِيلِ وَالتَّرشِيحِ وَمَا فِي الرَّابِعَةِ مِن التَّمْثِيلِ وَإِنَّ تَقدِيمَ المَعمُولاتِ فِى القَرَائِنِ الثَّلَاثِ الْأَخِيرَةِ لِرِعَايَةِ السَّجِعِ
وَالأهتِمَامِ إذ الحَصْرُ لَا يُنَاسِبُ المَقَامَ وَإِنَّ انتِصَابَ أَوَّلًا وَثَانِيَا عَلَى الظَّرْفِيَّةِ . وَأَمَّا التَّنْوِينُ فِي أَوَّلًا مَعَ أَنَّهُ أَفْعَلُ التَّفضِيلِ بِدَلِيلِ الْأُولَى وَالْأَوَائِلِ كَالفُضْلَى وَالأفَاضِل فَلانَّهُ هُنَا ظَرف بمعنى قَبلُ وَهُوَ حِينَيْدٍ مُنصَرِفْ لَا وَصَفِيَّةَ لَهُ أَصلا وَهَذَا مَعنَى مَا قَالَ فِى الصَّحَاحِ إِذَا جَعَلْتَهُ صِفَةٌ لَم تَصرِفهُ تَقُولُ لَقِيتُهُ عَامًا أَوَّلَ وَإِذَا لَم تَجْعَلهُ صِفَةٌ صَرَفتَهُ تَقُولُ لَقِيتُهُ عَامًا أَوَّلًا وَمَعْنَاهُ فِي الْأَوَّلِ أَوَّلُ مِن هَذَا العامِ وَفِي الثَّانِي قَبْلَ هَذَا العَامِ
ترجمہ :۔ پھر مخفی نہیں جو کچھ حد وصلوٰۃ کے جملوں میں حسن و خوبی پائی جاتی ہے۔ تجنیس سے اور جو دوسرے جملہ میں استعارہ

مکیہ ہے اور تخیلیہ ہے اور ترشیجیہ ہے اور جو چوتھے جملے میں تمثیل پائی گئی ہے۔ اور آخری تین جملوں میں معمولات کو مقدم کرنا سمیع بندی کی رعایت کرنے اور اہمیت کوملحوظ رکھنے لئے ہے۔ اس لیے کہ حضر ( اس ) مقام کے مناسب نہیں ہے۔ اور تحقیق لفظ اولا اور ثانیا کو منصوب پڑھنا ظرفیت کی بناء پر ہے اور لیکن اولاً میں تنوین باوجود یکہ یہ افعل التفضیل کا صیغہ ہے اس دلیل کے ساتھ ہے کہ اس کی مونث اولی آتی ہے۔ اور جمع اوائل آتی ہے جس طرح افضل کی مؤنث فصلی اور جمع افاضل آتی ہے۔ پس اس وجہ سے کہ یہاں ظرف ہے اور قبل کے معنی میں ہے اور اس وقت منصرف ہے اس میں وصفیت والا معنی بالکل نہیں پایا جاتا اور یہی مطلب ہے جو صحاح میں کہا ہے کہ جب تو اس (اول) کو صیغہ صفت بنائے تو غیر منصرف پڑھے گا۔ اور تو کہے گا ۔ حقیتہ عاما اول" بغیر تنوین کے ساتھ اور اگر اس کو تو صفت نہ بنائے تو اس کو منصرف پڑھے گا تو کہے گا عاما اون ( تنوین کے ساتھ ) اور پہلی صورت میں معنی ہوگا ملا میں اس کو اس سے پہلے سال اور دوسری صورت میں معنی ہو گا اس سے پہلے (خواہ پچھلا سال ہو یا اس
سے پچھلا )۔
لغوی تحقیق:۔ قرائن جمع ہے قرینہ کی۔ قرینہ وہ شے ہے جو کلام کے مقصود و مراد پر دلالت کرے لیکن یہاں قرینہ سے مجاز اجملہ مراد ہے۔
صنعات بلاغت یعنی تجنیس تمثیل ، استعارات کا بیان
تشریح قولہ تم لاکی :۔ یہ شرح کا عبارت کا پانچواں حصہ ہے اس عبارت میں شارع نے متن کی خوبی بیان فرمائی ہے۔
جس کا حاصل یہ ہے کہ مائن نے اپنی عبارت میں علم بلاغت کی اصطلاحات تجنیس ، استعارہ اور تمثیل کو ذکر کیا ہے۔ تجنیس:۔ کہتے ہیں کہ دو لفظوں کا شکل وصورت میں ایک جیسا ہونا لیکن معنی میں مختلف ہونا۔ جیسے یہاں ثانیا کو دو مرتبہ ذکر فرمایا ہے۔ پہلے ثانیا سے مراد دوسرا ہے۔ اور دوسرے ثانیا سے مراد پھیرنے والا ہے۔ اسی طرح مصلیا کو دو مرتبہ ذکر فرمایا۔ پہلے مصلیا کا معنیٰ ہے درود بھیجنے والا اور دوسرے مصلیا کا معنی ہے دوسرے نمبر پر آنے والا تو یہ تجنیس ہے۔
استعارہ:۔ اس طرح ہے کہ ماتن نے ثناء کو تشبیہ دی ہے گھوڑے کے ساتھ تو ذکر مشبہ کا مراد بھی مشبہ ہے لیکن وجہ تشبیہ مضمر فی النفس ہے تو یہ استعارہ مکیہ ہے اور گھوڑے کے لوازمات میں سے ہے کہ اس کی لگام ہو تو عنان میں استعارہ تخیلیہ اور گھوڑے کے مناسبات میں سے ہے کہ اس کو موڑا اور پھر ا جائے تو لفظ ثانیا میں استعار و ترشیجیہ ہے۔
تمثیل :۔ کے دو معنی ہیں۔ نمبر1۔ تشبیہ المرکب بالمرکب یعنی ایک مرکب چیز کو دوسری مرکب چیز کے ساتھ تشبیہ دینا تو اس
And the explanation of solving the clarification and the brightening. Investigation of the meaning of mujalliyan and musalliyan. 104. His statement and the meaning of that: This is the fourth part of the commentary's phrase. In summary, this phrase means that the commentator gave two answers to one question. Question: There is contradiction in the matn's phrase because 'mujalliyan' indicates that he is the one who comes first in the field of sending salawat, and 'musalliyan' indicates that he is the one who comes second. If he is first, how can he be second? And if he is second, he cannot be first. Answer (1): 'Mujalliyan' and 'musalliyan' are both metonymies. They mean repetition of salat and abundance of salat, i.e., I am one who sends salawat repeatedly. Answer (2): 'Mujalliyan' is with respect to sending salawat upon the Prophet (peace be upon him), because he is the primary object in salat. And 'musalliyan' is with respect to sending salawat upon his family, because the family is subordinate in salat, not the primary object. And the subordinate is always in second place. So due to difference in aspect, contradiction does not necessarily arise. Then, the beauty in the phrases of the praise and salutation—from tajnis in them, and in the second phrase from isti'ara by way of kinaayah, takhyil, and tarshih, and in the fourth phrase from tamthil—is not hidden. And the advancement of the objects in the last three phrases is to observe rhyme and importance, because restriction (hasr) is not appropriate to the context. And the accusative of 'awwala' and 'thaniya' is on the basis of being adverbs. As for the tanween in 'awwala' despite it being af'al al-tafdil, evidenced by its feminine 'ula' and plural 'awa'il', like 'fudla' and 'afadil', it is because here it is an adverb meaning 'before', and in that case it is fully declinable (munsarif), having no adjectival quality at all. And this is the meaning of what was said in al-Sihah: When you make it an adjective, you do not decline it fully; you say 'laqeetuho 'aamun awwalu' (without tanween). And when you do not make it an adjective, you decline it fully; you say 'laqeetuho 'aamun awwalan' (with tanween). And the meaning in the first case is 'first of this year', and in the second case is 'before this year'. Translation: Then it is not hidden that the beauty found in the phrases of praise and salutation from tajnis, and what is in the second phrase from isti'ara... [Page 106] ...makkiyya, takhyiliyya, and tarshihiyya, and what is in the fourth phrase from tamthil. And the advancement of the objects in the last three phrases is to observe rhyme and importance. Because restriction (hasr) is not appropriate to the context. And investigation of reading the words 'awwala' and 'thaniya' as accusative is on the basis of being adverbs. And the tanween in 'awwala' despite it being the form of af'al al-tafdil, evidenced by its feminine 'ula' and plural 'awa'il', just as afdal has feminine fudla and plural afadil, is because here it is an adverb meaning 'before', and in that case it is fully declinable, having no adjectival quality at all. And this is the meaning of what was said in al-Sihah: When you make it an adjective, you read it as non-declinable, and you say 'laqeetuho 'aamun awwalu' without tanween. And if you do not make it an adjective, you decline it fully, and you say 'laqeetuho 'aamun awwalan' (with tanween). In the first case the meaning is 'I met him in the first of this year', and in the second case the meaning is 'before this year' (whether it is last year or any time before). Lexical investigation: 'Qara'in' is the plural of 'qarina'. A qarina is something that indicates the intended meaning of the speech, but here by qarina is meant the expression conveying the metaphor. The rhetorical arts: tajnis, tamthil, statement of isti'ara. Commentary on his statement 'tumma la yakhfa' (then it is not hidden): This is the fifth part of the commentary's phrase. In this phrase the commentator stated the beauty of the matn. The summary is that the matn author mentioned the terms of balaghah: tajnis, isti'ara, and tamthil. Tajnis: Two words that are similar in form but different in meaning. For example, here 'thaniya' is mentioned twice. The first 'thaniya' means second, and the second 'thaniya' means turner. Similarly, 'musalliyan' is mentioned twice. The first 'musalliyan' means one who sends salawat, and the second 'musalliyan' means the one who comes in second place. This is tajnis. Isti'ara: The matn author compared 'thana' (praise) to a horse, so by mentioning the compared, the compared-to is intended, but the reason for comparison is implicit in the mind. So this is isti'ara makkiyya. And among the accessories of a horse is its rein, so 'inan' is isti'ara takhyiliyya. And among the things related to a horse is that it is turned and made to return, so the word 'thaniya' is isti'ara tarshihiyya. Tamthil: Has two meanings. Number 1. Comparing a compound thing to another compound thing, i.e., comparing one compound entity to another compound entity.
Source pages p. 105

Commentary
This passage is an analysis of the rhetorical and grammatical features of the matn (base text) of Al-Tawdih wa Al-Talwih. The commentator first addresses an apparent contradiction in the matn's use of 'mujalliyan' and 'musalliyan'. Two answers are provided: (1) both are metonymical expressions indicating abundance of sending salawat; (2) the first refers to sending salawat upon the Prophet (primary) and the second upon his family (secondary), thus no contradiction due to different aspects. Next, the commentator highlights the rhetorical beauties (tajnis, isti'ara, tamthil) found in the phrases of hamd and salah. He explains that the advancement of objects in the last three phrases serves rhyme and emphasis, not restriction (hasr). The grammatical point: 'awwala' has tanween though it is af'al al-tafdil; this is because it is used as an adverb meaning 'before', not as an adjective, so it is fully declinable. This is supported by a citation from al-Sihah. Finally, the lexical investigation defines qarina and the rhetorical terms with examples from the matn. Tajnis is illustrated by the double use of 'thaniya' and 'musalliyan'. Isti'ara is explained through the simile of praise to a horse, with takhyiliyya and tarshihiyya subtypes. Tamthil is defined as comparing one compound to another. This commentary follows the author's order and remains strictly within the text.

Key Terms
مجلیا (mujalliyan): One who sends abundant salawat (first answer) or one who sends salawat upon the Prophet (second answer).
مصلیا (musalliyan): One who sends salawat upon the family (second answer) or one who comes second in the tajnis interpretation.
كناية (kinaayah): A rhetorical figure where something is expressed indirectly; here, the terms are not literal but indicate abundance.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What is the primary contradiction that the commentator addresses?
A) The matn uses two different words for the same action.
B) The matn claims the same person is both first and second in sending salawat.
C) The matn has a grammatical error.
D) The matn contradicts a hadith.

Key Takeaway
Apparent contradictions in authoritative texts can often be resolved by recognizing different aspects or figurative language.

Textual and Editorial Notes
advanced
10 min
Rhetorical and Grammatical Nuances in the Matn's Opening
Analyzing the matn's rhetorical and grammatical beauties

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify tajnis, isti'ara, and tamthil in a Hanafi matn and explain the grammatical reason for tanween on 'awwala' when used as an adverb.

Core Idea
The matn's opening employs three rhetorical devices and a grammatical nuance that are essential for accurate interpretation.

After resolving the apparent contradiction, the commentator turns to the aesthetic and linguistic features of the matn. He points out three rhetorical devices: tajnis (paronomasia), isti'ara (metaphor) with subtypes, and tamthil (compound comparison). He also explains a grammatical curiosity: why the word 'awwala' appears with tanween despite being a comparative form (af'al al-tafdil). This lesson unpacks these features, showing how they enhance the text's meaning and are crucial for proper interpretation in usul al-fiqh.

Guided Path
1
Identify the rhetorical devices mentioned
From the passage, identify tajnis, isti'ara, and tamthil. Note that they are found in the phrases of praise and salutation.
These are standard terms in balaghah.
2
Analyze the tajnis (paronomasia)
Tajnis is when two words are similar in form but different in meaning. The matn uses 'thaniya' twice: first meaning 'second', second meaning 'turner'. Similarly, 'musalliyan' is used twice with different meanings.
This adds rhetorical beauty without confusing the intended meaning.
3
Analyze the isti'ara (metaphor)
Praise (thana') is compared to a horse. The commentator identifies three subtypes: makkiyya (the basic metaphor), takhyiliyya (mentioning a horse's equipment like 'inan'), and tarshihiyya (mentioning turning the horse, using 'thaniya').
The metaphor is sustained through related terms.
4
Analyze the tamthil (compound comparison)
Tamthil compares a compound entity to another compound entity. The fourth phrase is given as an example.
This is a higher-level rhetorical device than simple simile.
5
Examine the grammatical point: tanween on 'awwala'
The word 'awwala' is normally af'al al-tafdil (comparative adjective) and would be indeclinable (mamnu' min al-sarf). However, in the matn it has tanween. The commentator explains that here it is used as an adverb (zarf) meaning 'before', not as an adjective, so it is fully declinable. Evidence is cited from al-Sihah.
This shift in grammatical category affects parsing and meaning.

جواب (۱): مجلیا ومصلیا یہ دونوں کنا یہ ہیں ۔ تکرار صلوۃ اور تکثیر صلوۃ سے یعنی میں بار بار درود بھیجنے والا ہوں نہ جواب (۲): ملیا نبی صلی اللہ علیہ وسلم پر درود بھیجنے کے اعتبار سے ہے۔ کیونکہ آپ صلی اللہ علیہ وسلم تصلیہ میں مقصود اصلی ہیں۔ اور مصلیا آپ صلی اللہ علیہ وسلم کی آل پر درود بھیجنے کے اعتبار سے ہے کیونکہ آل تصلیہ میں تابع ہے مقصود اصلی نہیں ہے۔ اور تابع ہمیشہ دوسرے نمبر پر ہوتا ہے۔ تو اختلاف حیثیت کی وجہ سے تضاد لازم نہیں آئے گا۔
ثُمَّ لَا يخفى حُسنُ مَا فِي قَرَائِنِ الحَمدِ وَالصَّلَاةِ مِن التَّجنِيسِ وَمَا فِي القَرِينَةِ الثَّانِيَةِ مِن الاسْتِعَارَةِ بِالكِنَايَةِ وَالتَّحْيِيلِ وَالتَّرشِيحِ وَمَا فِي الرَّابِعَةِ مِن التَّمْثِيلِ وَإِنَّ تَقدِيمَ المَعمُولاتِ فِى القَرَائِنِ الثَّلَاثِ الْأَخِيرَةِ لِرِعَايَةِ السَّجِعِ

مکیہ ہے اور تخیلیہ ہے اور ترشیجیہ ہے اور جو چوتھے جملے میں تمثیل پائی گئی ہے۔ اور آخری تین جملوں میں معمولات کو مقدم کرنا سمیع بندی کی رعایت کرنے اور اہمیت کوملحوظ رکھنے لئے ہے۔ اس لیے کہ حضر ( اس ) مقام کے مناسب نہیں ہے۔ اور تحقیق لفظ اولا اور ثانیا کو منصوب پڑھنا ظرفیت کی بناء پر ہے اور لیکن اولاً میں تنوین باوجود یکہ یہ افعل التفضیل کا صیغہ ہے اس دلیل کے ساتھ ہے کہ اس کی مونث اولی آتی ہے۔ اور جمع اوائل آتی ہے جس طرح افضل کی مؤنث فصلی اور جمع افاضل آتی ہے۔ پس اس وجہ سے کہ یہاں ظرف ہے اور قبل کے معنی میں ہے اور اس وقت منصرف ہے اس میں وصفیت والا معنی بالکل نہیں پایا جاتا اور یہی مطلب ہے جو صحاح میں کہا ہے کہ جب تو اس (اول) کو صیغہ صفت بنائے تو غیر منصرف پڑھے گا۔ اور تو کہے گا ۔ حقیتہ عاما اول" بغیر تنوین کے ساتھ اور اگر اس کو تو صفت نہ بنائے تو اس کو منصرف پڑھے گا تو کہے گا عاما اون ( تنوین کے ساتھ ) اور پہلی صورت میں معنی ہوگا ملا میں اس کو اس سے پہلے سال اور دوسری صورت میں معنی ہو گا اس سے پہلے (خواہ پچھلا سال ہو یا اس
سے پچھلا )۔

تشریح قولہ تم لاکی :۔ یہ شرح کا عبارت کا پانچواں حصہ ہے اس عبارت میں شارع نے متن کی خوبی بیان فرمائی ہے۔
جس کا حاصل یہ ہے کہ مائن نے اپنی عبارت میں علم بلاغت کی اصطلاحات تجنیس ، استعارہ اور تمثیل کو ذکر کیا ہے۔ تجنیس:۔ کہتے ہیں کہ دو لفظوں کا شکل وصورت میں ایک جیسا ہونا لیکن معنی میں مختلف ہونا۔ جیسے یہاں ثانیا کو دو مرتبہ ذکر فرمایا ہے۔ پہلے ثانیا سے مراد دوسرا ہے۔ اور دوسرے ثانیا سے مراد پھیرنے والا ہے۔ اسی طرح مصلیا کو دو مرتبہ ذکر فرمایا۔ پہلے مصلیا کا معنیٰ ہے درود بھیجنے والا اور دوسرے مصلیا کا معنی ہے دوسرے نمبر پر آنے والا تو یہ تجنیس ہے۔
استعارہ:۔ اس طرح ہے کہ ماتن نے ثناء کو تشبیہ دی ہے گھوڑے کے ساتھ تو ذکر مشبہ کا مراد بھی مشبہ ہے لیکن وجہ تشبیہ مضمر فی النفس ہے تو یہ استعارہ مکیہ ہے اور گھوڑے کے لوازمات میں سے ہے کہ اس کی لگام ہو تو عنان میں استعارہ تخیلیہ اور گھوڑے کے مناسبات میں سے ہے کہ اس کو موڑا اور پھر ا جائے تو لفظ ثانیا میں استعار و ترشیجیہ ہے۔
تمثیل :۔ کے دو معنی ہیں۔ نمبر1۔ تشبیہ المرکب بالمرکب یعنی ایک مرکب چیز کو دوسری مرکب چیز کے ساتھ تشبیہ دینا تو اس
And the explanation of solving the clarification and the brightening. Investigation of the meaning of mujalliyan and musalliyan. 104. His statement and the meaning of that: This is the fourth part of the commentary's phrase. In summary, this phrase means that the commentator gave two answers to one question. Question: There is contradiction in the matn's phrase because 'mujalliyan' indicates that he is the one who comes first in the field of sending salawat, and 'musalliyan' indicates that he is the one who comes second. If he is first, how can he be second? And if he is second, he cannot be first. Answer (1): 'Mujalliyan' and 'musalliyan' are both metonymies. They mean repetition of salat and abundance of salat, i.e., I am one who sends salawat repeatedly. Answer (2): 'Mujalliyan' is with respect to sending salawat upon the Prophet (peace be upon him), because he is the primary object in salat. And 'musalliyan' is with respect to sending salawat upon his family, because the family is subordinate in salat, not the primary object. And the subordinate is always in second place. So due to difference in aspect, contradiction does not necessarily arise. Then, the beauty in the phrases of the praise and salutation—from tajnis in them, and in the second phrase from isti'ara by way of kinaayah, takhyil, and tarshih, and in the fourth phrase from tamthil—is not hidden. And the advancement of the objects in the last three phrases is to observe rhyme and importance, because restriction (hasr) is not appropriate to the context. And the accusative of 'awwala' and 'thaniya' is on the basis of being adverbs. As for the tanween in 'awwala' despite it being af'al al-tafdil, evidenced by its feminine 'ula' and plural 'awa'il', like 'fudla' and 'afadil', it is because here it is an adverb meaning 'before', and in that case it is fully declinable (munsarif), having no adjectival quality at all. And this is the meaning of what was said in al-Sihah: When you make it an adjective, you do not decline it fully; you say 'laqeetuho 'aamun awwalu' (without tanween). And when you do not make it an adjective, you decline it fully; you say 'laqeetuho 'aamun awwalan' (with tanween). And the meaning in the first case is 'first of this year', and in the second case is 'before this year'. Translation: Then it is not hidden that the beauty found in the phrases of praise and salutation from tajnis, and what is in the second phrase from isti'ara... [Page 106] ...makkiyya, takhyiliyya, and tarshihiyya, and what is in the fourth phrase from tamthil. And the advancement of the objects in the last three phrases is to observe rhyme and importance. Because restriction (hasr) is not appropriate to the context. And investigation of reading the words 'awwala' and 'thaniya' as accusative is on the basis of being adverbs. And the tanween in 'awwala' despite it being the form of af'al al-tafdil, evidenced by its feminine 'ula' and plural 'awa'il', just as afdal has feminine fudla and plural afadil, is because here it is an adverb meaning 'before', and in that case it is fully declinable, having no adjectival quality at all. And this is the meaning of what was said in al-Sihah: When you make it an adjective, you read it as non-declinable, and you say 'laqeetuho 'aamun awwalu' without tanween. And if you do not make it an adjective, you decline it fully, and you say 'laqeetuho 'aamun awwalan' (with tanween). In the first case the meaning is 'I met him in the first of this year', and in the second case the meaning is 'before this year' (whether it is last year or any time before). Lexical investigation: 'Qara'in' is the plural of 'qarina'. A qarina is something that indicates the intended meaning of the speech, but here by qarina is meant the expression conveying the metaphor. The rhetorical arts: tajnis, tamthil, statement of isti'ara. Commentary on his statement 'tumma la yakhfa' (then it is not hidden): This is the fifth part of the commentary's phrase. In this phrase the commentator stated the beauty of the matn. The summary is that the matn author mentioned the terms of balaghah: tajnis, isti'ara, and tamthil. Tajnis: Two words that are similar in form but different in meaning. For example, here 'thaniya' is mentioned twice. The first 'thaniya' means second, and the second 'thaniya' means turner. Similarly, 'musalliyan' is mentioned twice. The first 'musalliyan' means one who sends salawat, and the second 'musalliyan' means the one who comes in second place. This is tajnis. Isti'ara: The matn author compared 'thana' (praise) to a horse, so by mentioning the compared, the compared-to is intended, but the reason for comparison is implicit in the mind. So this is isti'ara makkiyya. And among the accessories of a horse is its rein, so 'inan' is isti'ara takhyiliyya. And among the things related to a horse is that it is turned and made to return, so the word 'thaniya' is isti'ara tarshihiyya. Tamthil: Has two meanings. Number 1. Comparing a compound thing to another compound thing, i.e., comparing one compound entity to another compound entity.
Source pages p. 105

Commentary
This passage is an analysis of the rhetorical and grammatical features of the matn (base text) of Al-Tawdih wa Al-Talwih. The commentator first addresses an apparent contradiction in the matn's use of 'mujalliyan' and 'musalliyan'. Two answers are provided: (1) both are metonymical expressions indicating abundance of sending salawat; (2) the first refers to sending salawat upon the Prophet (primary) and the second upon his family (secondary), thus no contradiction due to different aspects. Next, the commentator highlights the rhetorical beauties (tajnis, isti'ara, tamthil) found in the phrases of hamd and salah. He explains that the advancement of objects in the last three phrases serves rhyme and emphasis, not restriction (hasr). The grammatical point: 'awwala' has tanween though it is af'al al-tafdil; this is because it is used as an adverb meaning 'before', not as an adjective, so it is fully declinable. This is supported by a citation from al-Sihah. Finally, the lexical investigation defines qarina and the rhetorical terms with examples from the matn. Tajnis is illustrated by the double use of 'thaniya' and 'musalliyan'. Isti'ara is explained through the simile of praise to a horse, with takhyiliyya and tarshihiyya subtypes. Tamthil is defined as comparing one compound to another. This commentary follows the author's order and remains strictly within the text.

Key Terms
تجنیس (tajnīs): Two words similar in form but different in meaning, as in the double use of 'thaniya' or 'musalliyan'.
استعارہ (isti‘ārah): A metaphor where one thing is compared to another and the compared-to is mentioned; here, praise is compared to a horse.
تمثیل (tamthīl): Comparing one compound entity to another compound entity, as in the fourth phrase.
أول (awwal): Used here as an adverb meaning 'before', not as a superlative adjective, hence fully declinable with tanween.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What is the reason for the tanween on 'awwala' in the matn?
A) It is used as an adjective.
B) It is used as an adverb meaning 'before'.
C) It is a proper noun.
D) It is a verbal noun.

Key Takeaway
Rhetorical devices and grammatical nuances are integral to the precise interpretation of legal texts.

Textual and Editorial Notes
advanced
8 min
Rhetorical Devices and Taqdim al-Ma'mulat in Al-Tawdih
Commentary expanding on matn's rhetoric and grammar

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify tajnis, isti'ara, and tamthil in a Hanafi usul text and explain why the ma'mul is fronted, distinguishing between stylistic and logical reasons.

Core Idea
Fronting the object can serve rhyme or emphasis, not just restriction.

This lesson explores how a commentator on Al-Tawdih unpacks the rhetorical richness of the matn. We examine three figures of speech—tajnis, isti'ara, and tamthil—and then delve into a grammatical choice: why the object (ma'mul) is placed before the operator ('amil). The commentary reveals that this fronting serves two purposes: maintaining a rhyming pattern and emphasizing the importance of the object (Allah). A possible third reason, restriction (hasr), is explicitly rejected as contextually inappropriate. Understanding these nuances deepens your appreciation of how Hanafi usul texts use language to convey meaning precisely.

Guided Path
1
Identify the Rhetorical Figures
Read the passage carefully and locate instances of tajnis (two identical words with different meanings), isti'ara (metaphor), and tamthil (allegorical likening of a composite situation). For each, note the specific words or phrases involved.
The commentator explains tajnis through 'thaniya' and 'musalliya', isti'ara through praise likened to a horse, and tamthil through the horse race analogy.
2
Analyze the Isti'ara Subtypes
Break down the isti'ara into its three subtypes: makkiyya (the basic metaphor), takhyiliyya (imaginary accessories), and tarshihiyya (reinforcing associations). Connect each to a specific element in the matn (e.g., 'inan' for takhyiliyya).
Each subtype adds a layer of meaning to the overall metaphor.
3
Understand the Taqdim al-Ma'mulat Issue
Recognize the grammatical question: in several sentences, the object (e.g., a genitive phrase referring to Allah) precedes the operator (verb/preposition). Identify the two reasons given: (1) maintaining rhyme (each sentence ending with 'ya'), and (2) emphasizing the importance of the object.
The commentator answers a presumed question about why the natural order is reversed.
4
Evaluate the Rejection of Hasr
Consider why the third possible reason—restriction (hasr)—is rejected. The commentator specifies that restriction is used to negate sharing (e.g., someone claiming another shares in the act). In this context, no such negation is needed, so hasr is inappropriate.
This shows careful contextual reasoning in usul.
5
Synthesize the Stylistic and Legal Implications
Reflect on how these rhetorical and grammatical choices serve the matn's purpose: to convey the author's humility and precedence in sending blessings, using elegant language. The commentary demonstrates that usul analysis involves not just rules but also literary artistry.
Hanafi usul values precision and beauty in expression.
