Linguistic Precision in Hanafi Usul: Pronoun Omission and Tadmeen
Linguistic defense of the matn's wording

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain and apply the Hanafi usul principles of pronoun omission in adjective clauses and tadmeen for justifying preposition usage.

Core Idea
Tadmeen allows a verb to take a different preposition by implying a synonymous meaning.

This passage from the commentary on Al-Tawzih wa al-Talwih addresses two grammatical objections to the matn. The commentator shows how apparent irregularities are actually permissible in Arabic, demonstrating the precision required in usul al-fiqh texts. Understanding these linguistic devices is essential for correctly interpreting legal texts.

Guided Path
1
Identify the two objections
Read the passage and list the two grammatical issues raised: (1) the adjective clause 'lam tablugh' lacks an explicit pronoun referring to 'tadqeeqat'; (2) the verb 'bulugh' is used with the preposition 'ila', which is not its usual particle.
These are presented as presumed objections by a hypothetical critic.
2
Analyze the first objection: missing pronoun
Recall the rule: an adjective clause must contain a pronoun (daa'ir) referring back to the described noun or a part of it. The commentator offers two solutions: either the pronoun is omitted (the original was 'lam tablughha') or the word 'amad' itself serves as a part of 'tadqeeqat' (since it refers to the limit of tadqeeq).
This shows that the requirement is not that the pronoun be explicit, only that it be understood.
3
Analyze the second objection: preposition 'ila'
Identify that 'bulugh' normally takes a direct object, not 'ila'. The commentator invokes tadmeen: 'bulugh' is used in the meaning of 'wusul' (arrival) and 'intiha' (end), both of which take 'ila'. The implied structure is 'lam yablugh wasilan ila hadha al-amad'.
Tadmeen is a recognized linguistic device in Hanafi usul, allowing a verb to acquire the governance of its implied synonym.
4
Recognize the significance for usul al-fiqh
Understand that such analyses are not mere grammar exercises; they directly affect the interpretation of legal texts. Mistranslating or misinterpreting prepositions can change legal rulings.
The Hanafi school pays meticulous attention to linguistic precision when deriving rulings.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قولہ ولم تبلغ :۔ یہ شرح کی عبارت کا پہلا حصہ ہے۔ غرض شارع ایک سوال مقدر کا جواب ہے۔ سوال :۔ قاعدہ وضابطہ ہے جب جملہ صفت بن رہا ہو تو اس کے اندر عائد (ضمیر ) کا ہونا ضروری ہے جو موصوف کی طرف لوٹے یا اس جملہ کے اندر موصوف کے جز کا پایا جانا ضروری ہے۔ یہاں لم تبلغ تدقیقات کی صفت ہے اور اس کے اندر کوئی ضمیر موجود نہیں جو تدقیقات کی طرف راجع ہو؟
جواب:۔ یہاں ضمیر محذوف ہے کیونکہ ضمیر کا لفظوں میں موجود ہونا کوئی ضروری نہیں ۔ اصل میں تھا لم تبلغھا اس صورت میں میں اصل تھائم لفظ امد سے مراد انتہا ہو گی۔ معنی ہو گا نہیں پہنچا ان تدقیقات تک اس علم کے شاہسواروں میں سے کوئی ایک اس زمانہ کی انتہا تک یا ضمیر تو محذوف نہیں لیکن امد سے مراد تدقیق ہے تو اس صورت میں موصوف کا ایک جز وصفت میں پایا گیا معنیٰ ہوگا نہیں پہنچا اس علم کے شاہسواروں میں سے کوئی ایک اس تدقیق تک ۔
قولہ و تعدیہ المبلوغ :۔ یہ عبارت کا آخری حصہ ہے۔ غرض شاریخ سوال مقدر کا جواب دینا ہے۔ سوال:۔ ماتن نے لم تبلغ الی ھذہ الامد میں بلوغ کوالی کے ساتھ متعدی کیا ہے ۔ حالانکہ بلوغ کا صلہ الی نہیں آتا ۔ جواب:۔ یہاں تضمین ہے بلوغ بمعنی وصول و انتہا کے ہے اور وصول و انتہا کا صلہ الی آسکتا ہے۔ تقدیر عبارت یوں ہوگی۔ لم يبلغ واصلا الى هذا الامد قولہ سمیت لهذا الكتاب :۔ یہ شرح کی عبارت کا پہلا حصہ ہے۔ غرض شاریخ ترکیبی تحقیق کی طرف اشارہ کرتا ہے۔ فرماتے ہیں ۔ سمیت ھذ الکتاب جزاء ہے۔ اور لما تیسر اس کی شرط ہے۔ معنی یہ ہوگا کہ جب اس کتاب کا مکمل ہونا آسان ہو
His statement: 'Lam tablugh'. This is the first part of the commentator's phrase. The purpose is to answer a presumed objection. Objection: The rule is that when a clause becomes an adjective, it must contain a pronoun (referring back) that refers to the described noun, or a part of the described noun must be found in the clause. Here 'lam tablugh' is an adjective of 'tadqeeqat' and it contains no pronoun referring to 'tadqeeqat'?
Answer: Here the pronoun is omitted, because it is not necessary that the pronoun be present in words. Originally it was 'lam tablughha'. In that case, the word 'amad' implies the limit (intiha). The meaning would be: no one among the cavaliers of this knowledge reached those tadqeeqat to the limit of that time. Or, if the pronoun is not omitted and 'amad' means 'tadqeeq', then a part of the described noun is found in the adjective. The meaning would be: no one among the cavaliers of this knowledge reached that tadqeeq.
His statement: 'Wa ta'diyatu al-mablugh'. This is the last part of the phrase. The purpose is to answer a presumed objection. Objection: The matn author made 'bulugh' transitive with 'ila' in 'lam tablugh ila hadha al-amad', while 'bulugh' does not take the preposition 'ila'. Answer: Here there is tadmeen: 'bulugh' is in the meaning of 'wusul' (arrival) and 'intiha' (end), and both 'wusul' and 'intiha' can take the preposition 'ila'. The implied expression would be 'lam yablugh wasilan ila hadha al-amad'. His statement: 'Sammaytu li hadha al-kitab'. This is the first part of the commentator's phrase. The purpose is to indicate a synthetic investigation. He says: 'Sammaytu hadha al-kitab' is the answer, and 'lama tayassara' is its condition. The meaning would be: when the completion of this book became easy...
Source pages p. 116

Commentary
This passage addresses two linguistic issues in the matn. First, the adjective phrase 'lam tablugh' lacks an explicit pronoun, but the commentator explains that the pronoun is understood (omitted) or that the word 'amad' itself serves as part of the described noun. Second, the preposition 'ila' with 'bulugh' is justified by tadmeen, where 'bulugh' takes the meaning of 'wusul' which takes 'ila'. This shows the careful attention to grammatical precision in Hanafi usul texts.

Key Terms
عائد (ضمیر) ('a'id (dameer)): A pronoun in a descriptive clause that refers back to the described noun.
بلوغ (bulugh): To reach or attain, but here used with the meaning of 'arrival' (wusul).
تضمین (tadmeen): Linguistic device where a verb implies the meaning of another verb, thereby taking its grammatical behavior (e.g., preposition).

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What is the justification given in the passage for using 'ila' with 'bulugh'?
A) 'Bulugh' is a transitive verb by nature
B) The pronoun is omitted
C) 'Bulugh' implies the meaning of 'wusul', which takes 'ila'
D) It is a metaphorical usage

Key Takeaway
In Hanafi usul, apparent linguistic irregularities in authoritative texts are often resolved through recognized devices like tadmeen, ensuring the text remains valid for legal derivation.

The Device of Taḍmīn in Hanafi Linguistic Analysis
Linguistic defense via taḍmīn in the commentary

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify instances of taḍmīn in classical texts and apply it to justify prepositional variations.

Core Idea
Taḍmīn: a word borrows another’s syntax by assuming its meaning.

In this lesson, we examine how the commentator uses taḍmīn (inclusion) to defend the author's use of the preposition 'ilā' with 'balagha' and to justify a poet's expression. This rhetorical device is central to Hanafi usul for reconciling linguistic variants in the Qur’an and hadith.

Guided Path
1
Identify the objection
Locate the objection: the verb 'balagha' normally does not take 'ilā', yet the author used it. Also, a poet used 'sabaqa' with 'alā' instead of 'ilā'.
Objections arise from perceived violation of standard transitivity.
2
Define taḍmīn
Taḍmīn is when a word is given the meaning of another word, thereby adopting its grammatical behavior.
Here 'balagha' takes the meaning of 'wasala' (to reach), which allows 'ilā'.
3
Apply taḍmīn to the case
Show how the commentator argues that 'bulūgh' is used in the sense of 'wuṣūl', which legitimately takes 'ilā'.
The implied phrase is 'lam yablugh wāṣilan ilā hādhā al-amad'.
4
Assess the response to the poet objection
The second response: the poet's quote is unreliable (from Ahl al-Najm) and contradicts the Qur’an, which uses 'alā' with 'sabaqa'.
This shows multiple lines of defense: linguistic, textual, and source criticism.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
جواب الجواب:۔ لیکن تاریخ نے بعض حواشی کے اندر اس کا جواب دیا ہے۔ کہ میں نے یہ اعتراض معنی لغوی کے اعتبار سے کیا ہے۔ تضمین کے اعتبار سے نہیں کیا۔ یعنی معنی لغوی کے اعتبار سے صواب اور درست یہ ہے کہ اس کا صلہ الی ذکر کیا جائے نہ کہ معنی مجازی اور تضمین کے اعتبار سے۔ فلا اعتراض علیہ ۔ جواب ثانی :۔ اصل اعتراض کا دوسرا جواب یہ ہے کہ شاریخ کا اس شاعر کے قول سے استدلال درست نہیں کیونکہ یہ اہل نجم میں سے ہے۔ نیز یہ قرآن کے بھی خلاف ہے کیونکہ قرآن میں سبقت کا صلہ علی استعمال ہوا ہے۔ کما قال اللہ تعالیٰ و مانحن بمسبوقین علی ان مبدل امثالکم ۔
قولہ ولم تبلغ :۔ یہ شرح کی عبارت کا پہلا حصہ ہے۔ غرض شارع ایک سوال مقدر کا جواب ہے۔ سوال :۔ قاعدہ وضابطہ ہے جب جملہ صفت بن رہا ہو تو اس کے اندر عائد (ضمیر ) کا ہونا ضروری ہے جو موصوف کی طرف لوٹے یا اس جملہ کے اندر موصوف کے جز کا پایا جانا ضروری ہے۔ یہاں لم تبلغ تدقیقات کی صفت ہے اور اس کے اندر کوئی ضمیر موجود نہیں جو تدقیقات کی طرف راجع ہو؟
جواب:۔ یہاں ضمیر محذوف ہے کیونکہ ضمیر کا لفظوں میں موجود ہونا کوئی ضروری نہیں ۔ اصل میں تھا لم تبلغھا اس صورت میں میں اصل تھائم لفظ امد سے مراد انتہا ہو گی۔ معنی ہو گا نہیں پہنچا ان تدقیقات تک اس علم کے شاہسواروں میں سے کوئی ایک اس زمانہ کی انتہا تک یا ضمیر تو محذوف نہیں لیکن امد سے مراد تدقیق ہے تو اس صورت میں موصوف کا ایک جز وصفت میں پایا گیا معنیٰ ہوگا نہیں پہنچا اس علم کے شاہسواروں میں سے کوئی ایک اس تدقیق تک ۔
قولہ و تعدیہ المبلوغ :۔ یہ عبارت کا آخری حصہ ہے۔ غرض شاریخ سوال مقدر کا جواب دینا ہے۔ سوال:۔ ماتن نے لم تبلغ الی ھذہ الامد میں بلوغ کوالی کے ساتھ متعدی کیا ہے ۔ حالانکہ بلوغ کا صلہ الی نہیں آتا ۔ جواب:۔ یہاں تضمین ہے بلوغ بمعنی وصول و انتہا کے ہے اور وصول و انتہا کا صلہ الی آسکتا ہے۔ تقدیر عبارت یوں ہوگی۔ لم يبلغ واصلا الى هذا الامد 
قولہ سمیت لهذا الكتاب :۔ یہ شرح کی عبارت کا پہلا حصہ ہے۔ غرض شاریخ ترکیبی تحقیق کی طرف اشارہ کرتا ہے۔ فرماتے ہیں ۔ سمیت ھذ الکتاب جزاء ہے۔ اور لما تیسر اس کی شرط ہے۔ معنی یہ ہوگا کہ جب اس کتاب کا مکمل ہونا آسان ہوگیا تو میں نے اس کا نام توضیح فی حل غوامض التنقیح رکھا لیکن یہ تفصیل اس نسخہ کے مطابق ہے جس میں سمیت سے پہلے حرف واؤ نہیں اور بعض نسخوں میں واؤ ہے تو اس نسخہ کے مطابق یہ وسمیت معطوف ہوگا جعلتہ عراضتہ پر اور جعلتہ جواب لما ہوگا اور شرط کی جزا ہوگی۔
وضع اسم الاشارہ :۔ یہ شرح کی عبارت کا دوسرا حصہ ہے غرض شارع دفع دخل مقدر ہے۔
سوال: یہ ہے کہ شاریخ نے سمیت ھذا الکتاب میں اسم اشارہ ذکر کیا۔ ضمیر کو ذکر کیوں نہیں کیا حالانکہ یہ موضع موضع ضمیر ہے کیونکہ عام طور پر اگر ایک مرتبہ اسم ظاہر ذکر کر دیا جائے تو پھر اس کی طرف ضمیر لوٹائی جاتی ہے۔
جواب (۱):۔ اسم اشارہ سے زیادہ امتیاز حاصل ہوتا ہے بنسبت ضمیر کے کیونکہ اسم اشارہ سے معین اور محسوس چیز کی طرف اشارہ ہوتا ہے اور یہ ذات وصفات دونوں پر دلالت کرتا ہے اور ضمیر صرف ذات پر دلالت کرتی ہے تو مصنف نے کتاب کی عظمت کی طرف اشارہ کرنے کے لیے اسم اشارہ ذکر کیا۔ گویا کہ یہ کتاب فن کی تمام کتابوں میں ممتاز ہے۔
قوله فان قلت : فان قلت سے سوال قلت سے جواب ۔ سوال :۔ سوال کا حاصل یہ ہے کہ لما کے بعد ایک شرط اور ایک جزاء ہوتی ہے۔ اور لما جزاء کے ثبوت کے لیے آتا ہے شرط کے ثبوت کی وجہ سے تو اب یہاں لما کی شرط اتمام ہے۔ اور جزاء سمیت ھذا الکتاب معنیٰ ہوگا۔ اس کا پورا ہو ناتسمیہ بالتوضیح کے لیے سبب ہے حالانکہ یہ درست نہیں کیونکہ یہ کوئی ضروری نہیں کہ کتاب کا تمام ہونا تو ضیح نام رکھنے کے لئے سبب بن جائے؟ جواب : کا حاصل یہ ہے کہ اتمامہ میں ضمیر مطلقا کتاب کی طرف نہیں لوٹ رہی ہے بلکہ اس کتاب (شرح) کی طرف ضمیر لوٹ رہی ہے جو مذکورہ صفات کے ساتھ متصف ہے جن میں تنقیح کی مشکلات کو واضح کیا گیا ہے۔ اور ان کو کھول دیا گیا ہے۔ اور ایسی کتاب کا پورا ہونا تسمیہ بالتوضیح کے لیے سبب بن سکتا ہے۔ سوال: ضمیر صرف ذات پر دلالت کرتی ہے اوصاف پر نہیں تو آپ نے اس کتاب کے اوصاف کیسے مراد لے لئے؟ جواب:۔ اوصاف ضمیر کی وجہ سے سمجھ میں نہیں آئے بلکہ قرینہ مقام کی وجہ سے سمجھ میں آئے ہیں ۔ فلا اعتراض علیہ۔ خطبة تنقيح مع التوضيح
Response to the objection: But the historian has responded to it in some margins that I made this objection from the perspective of literal meaning, not from the perspective of inclusion (taḍmīn). That is, from the perspective of literal meaning, it is correct that its preposition should be 'ilā', not from the perspective of metaphorical meaning and taḍmīn. So no objection against him. Second response: The second response to the original objection is that the commentator's inference from this poet's saying is not correct because he is from the people of Najm. Also, it contradicts the Qur'an because in the Qur'an the preposition for 'sabaqa' is 'alā'. As Allah said: 'And we are not to be outstripped (mashūqīn) over ('alā) changing your likenesses.'
His statement 'wa lam tablugh': This is the first part of the commentary's phrase. The objective is the commentator answering an implied question. Question: The rule is that when a clause is descriptive, it must contain a returning pronoun (ḍamīr) that refers back to the described noun, or the clause must contain a part of the described noun. Here 'lam tablugh' is a description of 'tadqīqāt', and it does not contain any pronoun referring back to 'tadqīqāt'? Answer: Here the pronoun is omitted because the pronoun's presence in the words is not necessary. Originally it was 'lam tablughahā'; in that case, 'amad' means 'end'. The meaning would be 'No one among the horsemen of this science reached those tadqīqāt up to the end of this time.' Or the pronoun is not omitted, but 'amad' means 'tadqīq'. In that case, a part of the described noun is found in the description. The meaning would be 'No one among the horsemen of this science reached this tadqīq.'
His statement 'wa ta'diyat al-mablugh': This is the last part of the phrase. The objective is the commentator answering an implied question. Question: The author made 'bulūgh' transitive with 'ilā' in 'lam tablugh ilā hādhā al-amad', whereas 'bulūgh' does not take 'ilā' as its preposition. Answer: Here there is taḍmīn: 'bulūgh' is in the meaning of 'wuṣūl' and 'intihā'', and 'wuṣūl' and 'intihā'' can take 'ilā'. The implied phrase would be: 'lam yablugh wāṣilan ilā hādhā al-amad.'
His statement 'sammaytu li-hādhā al-kitāb': This is the first part of the commentary's phrase. The objective is the commentator pointing to a syntactic investigation. He says: 'sammaytu hādhā al-kitāb' is the consequence, and 'lammā tayassara' is its condition. The meaning would be: When the completion of this book became easy, I named it 'Tawḍīḥ fī Ḥall Ghawāmiḍ al-Tanqīḥ'. But this detail is according to the manuscript in which there is no 'wāw' before 'sammaytu'. And in some manuscripts there is a 'wāw', then according to this manuscript 'wa sammaytu' would be coordinated with 'ja'altuhu 'irāḍatan', and 'ja'altuhu' would be the response of 'lammā' and would be the consequence of the condition.
Placement of the demonstrative pronoun: This is the second part of the commentary's phrase. The objective is the commentator repelling an implied objection. Question: The commentator mentioned the demonstrative pronoun in 'sammaytu hādhā al-kitāb'. Why did he not mention the pronoun, whereas this is the place of the pronoun because generally if a noun is mentioned once, then a pronoun is used to refer back to it? Answer (1): The demonstrative pronoun gives more distinction than the pronoun because the demonstrative pronoun points to a specific and perceptible thing, and it indicates both the essence and attributes, whereas the pronoun indicates only the essence. So the author mentioned the demonstrative pronoun to indicate the greatness of the book. As if this book is distinguished among all books of the field.
His statement 'fa-in qulta': 'fa-in qulta' is the question, 'qultu' is the answer. Question: The gist of the question is that 'lammā' has a condition and a consequence. And 'lammā' comes for the establishment of the consequence due to the establishment of the condition. So here the condition of 'lammā' is 'itmām' (completion), and the consequence is 'sammaytu hādhā al-kitāb'. The meaning would be: Its completion is the cause for naming it 'al-Tawḍīḥ', whereas this is not correct because it is not necessary that the completion of the book be the cause for naming it 'Tawḍīḥ'. Answer: The gist is that in 'itmāmuhu', the pronoun is not absolutely referring to the book, but rather the pronoun refers to this book (the commentary) which is characterized by the mentioned attributes, in which the difficulties of the Tanqīḥ are clarified and opened. And the completion of such a book can be the cause for naming it 'al-Tawḍīḥ'. Question: The pronoun indicates only the essence, not attributes. So how did you take the attributes of this book? Answer: The attributes were not understood because of the pronoun, but rather because of the contextual clue (qarīnat al-maqām). So no objection against him. The sermon of al-Tanqīḥ with al-Tawḍīḥ.
Source pages p. 116

Commentary
This passage is a detailed commentary on the author's introduction, addressing various linguistic and rhetorical objections. The commentator first deals with an objection regarding a poet's quote used by a previous commentator, providing two responses: one based on literal vs. metaphorical meaning (taḍmīn), and another questioning the reliability of the poet and noting that the Qur'an uses a different preposition. Next, the commentator explains a phrase from the sharh 'wa lam tablugh' by addressing the absence of a pronoun in the descriptive clause. He offers two solutions: either the pronoun is omitted but implied, or the word 'amad' itself refers to 'tadqīq', thus containing a part of the described noun. Then, the commentator justifies the transitivity of 'bulūgh' with 'ilā' by invoking taḍmīn, where 'bulūgh' takes the meaning of 'wuṣūl' or 'intihā''. He also analyzes the naming of the book, explaining the syntactic structure of 'sammaytu' as the consequence of 'lammā'. The use of the demonstrative pronoun 'hādhā' instead of a pronoun is justified by the greater distinction it provides, indicating the book's eminence. Finally, a question about 'lammā' and its consequence is resolved by clarifying that the pronoun in 'itmāmuhu' refers specifically to the commentary with its attributes, and that the attributes are understood through contextual clues, not the pronoun itself. This passage exemplifies the careful linguistic analysis typical in Hanafi usul commentaries.

Key Terms
تضمين (taḍmīn): A rhetorical device where a word is given the meaning of another word, thereby affecting its syntactic behavior (e.g., transitivity).
بلوغ (bulūgh): The act of reaching, used here with taḍmīn to mean 'wuṣūl'.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What is the primary function of taḍmīn in the passage?
A) To reject a weak hadith
B) To justify the transitivity of 'balagha' with 'ilā'
C) To criticise the poet
D) To change the meaning of the word completely

Key Takeaway
Taḍmīn allows a word to adopt another’s syntax by assuming its meaning, a crucial tool in Hanafi linguistic analysis.

Pronoun Omission and Demonstrative Emphasis in Hanafi Commentary
Linguistic clarifications on pronouns and demonstratives

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain why an omitted pronoun in a descriptive clause is permissible when context supplies the reference, and why a demonstrative pronoun is used instead of a personal pronoun for emphasis.

Core Idea
Omitted pronouns are valid when context supplies the reference; demonstratives excel pronouns in highlighting both essence and attributes.

This lesson examines two related linguistic points from the commentary: the omission of a pronoun in a descriptive clause (sifa) and the choice of a demonstrative pronoun over a simple pronoun to refer to a previously mentioned object. Both demonstrate the Hanafi preoccupation with precision in language.

Guided Path
1
Identify the first issue: pronoun in sifa clause
The author wrote 'lam tablugh' as a description of 'tadqīqāt', but there is no visible pronoun referring back to 'tadqīqāt'.
The rule: a descriptive clause must contain a returning pronoun (ḍamīr) or a part of the described noun.
2
Analyse the two solutions for the omitted pronoun
Solution 1: the pronoun is omitted (mahdhūf) and implied; the original was 'lam tablughahā'. Solution 2: the word 'amad' itself means 'tadqīq', so the clause contains a part of the described noun.
Ellipsis is allowed when the meaning is clear.
3
Examine the demonstrative pronoun choice
The author uses 'hādhā' instead of a personal pronoun to refer back to 'al-kitāb'. The commentator justifies this by noting that demonstratives give more distinction (imtiyāz) and indicate both essence and attributes.
This emphasizes the book's greatness.
4
Resolve the lammā conditional
The question: how can completion of the book be a cause for naming it? The commentator clarifies that 'itmāmuhu' refers specifically to this commentary with its attributes, not any book. The attributes are understood from context (qarīnat al-maqām).
The pronoun's reference is narrowed by context.

قولہ ولم تبلغ :۔ یہ شرح کی عبارت کا پہلا حصہ ہے۔ غرض شارع ایک سوال مقدر کا جواب ہے۔ سوال :۔ قاعدہ وضابطہ ہے جب جملہ صفت بن رہا ہو تو اس کے اندر عائد (ضمیر ) کا ہونا ضروری ہے جو موصوف کی طرف لوٹے یا اس جملہ کے اندر موصوف کے جز کا پایا جانا ضروری ہے۔ یہاں لم تبلغ تدقیقات کی صفت ہے اور اس کے اندر کوئی ضمیر موجود نہیں جو تدقیقات کی طرف راجع ہو؟
جواب:۔ یہاں ضمیر محذوف ہے کیونکہ ضمیر کا لفظوں میں موجود ہونا کوئی ضروری نہیں ۔ اصل میں تھا لم تبلغھا اس صورت میں میں اصل تھائم لفظ امد سے مراد انتہا ہو گی۔ معنی ہو گا نہیں پہنچا ان تدقیقات تک اس علم کے شاہسواروں میں سے کوئی ایک اس زمانہ کی انتہا تک یا ضمیر تو محذوف نہیں لیکن امد سے مراد تدقیق ہے تو اس صورت میں موصوف کا ایک جز وصفت میں پایا گیا معنیٰ ہوگا نہیں پہنچا اس علم کے شاہسواروں میں سے کوئی ایک اس تدقیق تک ۔
قولہ و تعدیہ المبلوغ :۔ یہ عبارت کا آخری حصہ ہے۔ غرض شاریخ سوال مقدر کا جواب دینا ہے۔ سوال:۔ ماتن نے لم تبلغ الی ھذہ الامد میں بلوغ کوالی کے ساتھ متعدی کیا ہے ۔ حالانکہ بلوغ کا صلہ الی نہیں آتا ۔ جواب:۔ یہاں تضمین ہے بلوغ بمعنی وصول و انتہا کے ہے اور وصول و انتہا کا صلہ الی آسکتا ہے۔ تقدیر عبارت یوں ہوگی۔ لم يبلغ واصلا الى هذا الامد 
قولہ سمیت لهذا الكتاب :۔ یہ شرح کی عبارت کا پہلا حصہ ہے۔ غرض شاریخ ترکیبی تحقیق کی طرف اشارہ کرتا ہے۔ فرماتے ہیں ۔ سمیت ھذ الکتاب جزاء ہے۔ اور لما تیسر اس کی شرط ہے۔ معنی یہ ہوگا کہ جب اس کتاب کا مکمل ہونا آسان ہوگیا تو میں نے اس کا نام توضیح فی حل غوامض التنقیح رکھا لیکن یہ تفصیل اس نسخہ کے مطابق ہے جس میں سمیت سے پہلے حرف واؤ نہیں اور بعض نسخوں میں واؤ ہے تو اس نسخہ کے مطابق یہ وسمیت معطوف ہوگا جعلتہ عراضتہ پر اور جعلتہ جواب لما ہوگا اور شرط کی جزا ہوگی۔
وضع اسم الاشارہ :۔ یہ شرح کی عبارت کا دوسرا حصہ ہے غرض شارع دفع دخل مقدر ہے۔
سوال: یہ ہے کہ شاریخ نے سمیت ھذا الکتاب میں اسم اشارہ ذکر کیا۔ ضمیر کو ذکر کیوں نہیں کیا حالانکہ یہ موضع موضع ضمیر ہے کیونکہ عام طور پر اگر ایک مرتبہ اسم ظاہر ذکر کر دیا جائے تو پھر اس کی طرف ضمیر لوٹائی جاتی ہے۔
جواب (۱):۔ اسم اشارہ سے زیادہ امتیاز حاصل ہوتا ہے بنسبت ضمیر کے کیونکہ اسم اشارہ سے معین اور محسوس چیز کی طرف اشارہ ہوتا ہے اور یہ ذات وصفات دونوں پر دلالت کرتا ہے اور ضمیر صرف ذات پر دلالت کرتی ہے تو مصنف نے کتاب کی عظمت کی طرف اشارہ کرنے کے لیے اسم اشارہ ذکر کیا۔ گویا کہ یہ کتاب فن کی تمام کتابوں میں ممتاز ہے۔
قوله فان قلت : فان قلت سے سوال قلت سے جواب ۔ سوال :۔ سوال کا حاصل یہ ہے کہ لما کے بعد ایک شرط اور ایک جزاء ہوتی ہے۔ اور لما جزاء کے ثبوت کے لیے آتا ہے شرط کے ثبوت کی وجہ سے تو اب یہاں لما کی شرط اتمام ہے۔ اور جزاء سمیت ھذا الکتاب معنیٰ ہوگا۔ اس کا پورا ہو ناتسمیہ بالتوضیح کے لیے سبب ہے حالانکہ یہ درست نہیں کیونکہ یہ کوئی ضروری نہیں کہ کتاب کا تمام ہونا تو ضیح نام رکھنے کے لئے سبب بن جائے؟ جواب : کا حاصل یہ ہے کہ اتمامہ میں ضمیر مطلقا کتاب کی طرف نہیں لوٹ رہی ہے بلکہ اس کتاب (شرح) کی طرف ضمیر لوٹ رہی ہے جو مذکورہ صفات کے ساتھ متصف ہے جن میں تنقیح کی مشکلات کو واضح کیا گیا ہے۔ اور ان کو کھول دیا گیا ہے۔ اور ایسی کتاب کا پورا ہونا تسمیہ بالتوضیح کے لیے سبب بن سکتا ہے۔ سوال: ضمیر صرف ذات پر دلالت کرتی ہے اوصاف پر نہیں تو آپ نے اس کتاب کے اوصاف کیسے مراد لے لئے؟ جواب:۔ اوصاف ضمیر کی وجہ سے سمجھ میں نہیں آئے بلکہ قرینہ مقام کی وجہ سے سمجھ میں آئے ہیں ۔ فلا اعتراض علیہ۔ خطبة تنقيح مع التوضيح
Response to the objection: But the historian has responded to it in some margins that I made this objection from the perspective of literal meaning, not from the perspective of inclusion (taḍmīn). That is, from the perspective of literal meaning, it is correct that its preposition should be 'ilā', not from the perspective of metaphorical meaning and taḍmīn. So no objection against him. Second response: The second response to the original objection is that the commentator's inference from this poet's saying is not correct because he is from the people of Najm. Also, it contradicts the Qur'an because in the Qur'an the preposition for 'sabaqa' is 'alā'. As Allah said: 'And we are not to be outstripped (mashūqīn) over ('alā) changing your likenesses.'
His statement 'wa lam tablugh': This is the first part of the commentary's phrase. The objective is the commentator answering an implied question. Question: The rule is that when a clause is descriptive, it must contain a returning pronoun (ḍamīr) that refers back to the described noun, or the clause must contain a part of the described noun. Here 'lam tablugh' is a description of 'tadqīqāt', and it does not contain any pronoun referring back to 'tadqīqāt'? Answer: Here the pronoun is omitted because the pronoun's presence in the words is not necessary. Originally it was 'lam tablughahā'; in that case, 'amad' means 'end'. The meaning would be 'No one among the horsemen of this science reached those tadqīqāt up to the end of this time.' Or the pronoun is not omitted, but 'amad' means 'tadqīq'. In that case, a part of the described noun is found in the description. The meaning would be 'No one among the horsemen of this science reached this tadqīq.'
His statement 'wa ta'diyat al-mablugh': This is the last part of the phrase. The objective is the commentator answering an implied question. Question: The author made 'bulūgh' transitive with 'ilā' in 'lam tablugh ilā hādhā al-amad', whereas 'bulūgh' does not take 'ilā' as its preposition. Answer: Here there is taḍmīn: 'bulūgh' is in the meaning of 'wuṣūl' and 'intihā'', and 'wuṣūl' and 'intihā'' can take 'ilā'. The implied phrase would be: 'lam yablugh wāṣilan ilā hādhā al-amad.'
His statement 'sammaytu li-hādhā al-kitāb': This is the first part of the commentary's phrase. The objective is the commentator pointing to a syntactic investigation. He says: 'sammaytu hādhā al-kitāb' is the consequence, and 'lammā tayassara' is its condition. The meaning would be: When the completion of this book became easy, I named it 'Tawḍīḥ fī Ḥall Ghawāmiḍ al-Tanqīḥ'. But this detail is according to the manuscript in which there is no 'wāw' before 'sammaytu'. And in some manuscripts there is a 'wāw', then according to this manuscript 'wa sammaytu' would be coordinated with 'ja'altuhu 'irāḍatan', and 'ja'altuhu' would be the response of 'lammā' and would be the consequence of the condition.
Placement of the demonstrative pronoun: This is the second part of the commentary's phrase. The objective is the commentator repelling an implied objection. Question: The commentator mentioned the demonstrative pronoun in 'sammaytu hādhā al-kitāb'. Why did he not mention the pronoun, whereas this is the place of the pronoun because generally if a noun is mentioned once, then a pronoun is used to refer back to it? Answer (1): The demonstrative pronoun gives more distinction than the pronoun because the demonstrative pronoun points to a specific and perceptible thing, and it indicates both the essence and attributes, whereas the pronoun indicates only the essence. So the author mentioned the demonstrative pronoun to indicate the greatness of the book. As if this book is distinguished among all books of the field.
His statement 'fa-in qulta': 'fa-in qulta' is the question, 'qultu' is the answer. Question: The gist of the question is that 'lammā' has a condition and a consequence. And 'lammā' comes for the establishment of the consequence due to the establishment of the condition. So here the condition of 'lammā' is 'itmām' (completion), and the consequence is 'sammaytu hādhā al-kitāb'. The meaning would be: Its completion is the cause for naming it 'al-Tawḍīḥ', whereas this is not correct because it is not necessary that the completion of the book be the cause for naming it 'Tawḍīḥ'. Answer: The gist is that in 'itmāmuhu', the pronoun is not absolutely referring to the book, but rather the pronoun refers to this book (the commentary) which is characterized by the mentioned attributes, in which the difficulties of the Tanqīḥ are clarified and opened. And the completion of such a book can be the cause for naming it 'al-Tawḍīḥ'. Question: The pronoun indicates only the essence, not attributes. So how did you take the attributes of this book? Answer: The attributes were not understood because of the pronoun, but rather because of the contextual clue (qarīnat al-maqām). So no objection against him. The sermon of al-Tanqīḥ with al-Tawḍīḥ.
Source pages p. 116

Commentary
This passage is a detailed commentary on the author's introduction, addressing various linguistic and rhetorical objections. The commentator first deals with an objection regarding a poet's quote used by a previous commentator, providing two responses: one based on literal vs. metaphorical meaning (taḍmīn), and another questioning the reliability of the poet and noting that the Qur'an uses a different preposition. Next, the commentator explains a phrase from the sharh 'wa lam tablugh' by addressing the absence of a pronoun in the descriptive clause. He offers two solutions: either the pronoun is omitted but implied, or the word 'amad' itself refers to 'tadqīq', thus containing a part of the described noun. Then, the commentator justifies the transitivity of 'bulūgh' with 'ilā' by invoking taḍmīn, where 'bulūgh' takes the meaning of 'wuṣūl' or 'intihā''. He also analyzes the naming of the book, explaining the syntactic structure of 'sammaytu' as the consequence of 'lammā'. The use of the demonstrative pronoun 'hādhā' instead of a pronoun is justified by the greater distinction it provides, indicating the book's eminence. Finally, a question about 'lammā' and its consequence is resolved by clarifying that the pronoun in 'itmāmuhu' refers specifically to the commentary with its attributes, and that the attributes are understood through contextual clues, not the pronoun itself. This passage exemplifies the careful linguistic analysis typical in Hanafi usul commentaries.

Key Terms
ضمير محذوف (ḍamīr maḥdhūf): An omitted pronoun implied by context.
اسم الإشارة (ism al-ishāra): Demonstrative pronoun used for emphasis, indicating essence and attributes.
قرينة المقام (qarīnat al-maqām): Contextual clue derived from the situation or surrounding discourse.

Key Terms from Source Passage

A) Because Arabic grammar requires a demonstrative after the verb 'sammā'.

The Legal Significance of Using Ism al-Ishara in Hanafi Texts
Commentary on author's choice of ism al-ishara

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify why a Hanafi author uses a demonstrative pronoun instead of a regular pronoun, and apply the principle that ism al-ishara indicates both essence and attributes.

Core Idea
Ism al-ishara points to both essence and attributes, elevating the referent and providing greater legal specificity.

In Hanafi textual analysis, word choice matters. This passage from al-Tarweeh explains why the author used 'hadha al-kitab' (this book) instead of a simple pronoun. The commentator shows that the demonstrative pronoun carries extra meaning—it indicates not only the book's identity but its distinguished qualities. Understanding such choices is key to proper istinbat.

Guided Path
1
Identify the textual variant
The commentator first clarifies a manuscript difference regarding the word 'sammaytu'. This shows that even a conjunction can affect the syntactical analysis.
Note the importance of manuscript variants in Hanafi textual criticism.
2
Recognize the objection
The objector asks why a demonstrative pronoun was used instead of a regular pronoun, since a pronoun is normally sufficient after a noun is mentioned.
This objection reflects a standard grammatical expectation.
3
Analyze the response
The answer explains that ism al-ishara provides greater distinction (imtiyaz) by pointing to both the essence (dhat) and the attributes (sifat) of the book, thereby honoring it.
The response highlights the hermeneutic weight of ism al-ishara.
4
Examine the second objection
A further objection arises from the 'lamma' construction: how does the completion of the book cause its naming?
This objection targets the causal link between completion and naming.
5
Apply contextual clues (qarina)
The commentator resolves this by noting that the pronoun in 'itmamihi' refers to the specific commentary described with attributes, and that the attributes are understood through qarinat al-maqam, not the pronoun itself.
Contextual clues (qara'in) are essential for interpreting ambiguous references.

التَّرويحُ لِحَلَّ التَّوْضِيح وَالتَّلويج
گیا تو میں نے اس کا نام توضیح فی حل غوامض التنقیح رکھا لیکن یہ تفصیل اس نسخہ کے مطابق ہے جس میں سمیت سے پہلے حرف واؤ نہیں اور بعض نسخوں میں واؤ ہے تو اس نسخہ کے مطابق یہ وسمیت معطوف ہوگا جعلتہ عراضتہ پر اور جعلتہ جواب لما ہوگا اور شرط کی جزا ہوگی۔
اسم اشارہ کو ضمیر کی جگہ ذکر کرنا
وضع اسم الاشارہ :۔ یہ شرح کی عبارت کا دوسرا حصہ ہے غرض شارع دفع دخل مقدر ہے۔
سوال: یہ ہے کہ شارح نے سمیت ھذا الکتاب میں اسم اشارہ ذکر کیا۔ ضمیر کو ذکر کیوں نہیں کیا حالانکہ یہ موضع ضمیر ہے کیونکہ عام طور پر اگر ایک مرتبہ اسم ظاہر ذکر کر دیا جائے تو پھر اس کی طرف ضمیر لوٹائی جاتی ہے۔
جواب (۱):۔ اسم اشارہ سے زیادہ امتیاز حاصل ہوتا ہے بنسبت ضمیر کے کیونکہ اسم اشارہ سے معین اور محسوس چیز کی طرف اشارہ ہوتا ہے اور یہ ذات وصفات دونوں پر دلالت کرتا ہے اور ضمیر صرف ذات پر دلالت کرتی ہے تو مصنف نے کتاب کی عظمت کی طرف اشارہ کرنے کے لیے اسم اشارہ ذکر کیا۔ گویا کہ یہ کتاب فن کی تمام کتابوں میں ممتاز ہے۔
قوله فان قلت : فان قلت سے سوال قلت سے جواب ۔ سوال :۔ سوال کا حاصل یہ ہے کہ لما کے بعد ایک شرط اور ایک جزاء ہوتی ہے۔ اور لما جزاء کے ثبوت کے لیے آتا ہے شرط کے ثبوت کی وجہ سے تو اب یہاں لما کی شرط اتمام ہے۔ اور جزاء سمیت ھذا الکتاب معنیٰ ہوگا۔ اس کا پورا ہونا تسمیہ بالتوضیح کے لیے سبب ہے حالانکہ یہ درست نہیں کیونکہ یہ کوئی ضروری نہیں کہ کتاب کا تمام ہونا توضیح نام رکھنے کے لئے سبب بن جائے؟ جواب : کا حاصل یہ ہے کہ اتمامہ میں ضمیر مطلقا کتاب کی طرف نہیں لوٹ رہی ہے بلکہ اس کتاب (شرح) کی طرف ضمیر لوٹ رہی ہے جو مذکورہ صفات کے ساتھ متصف ہے جن میں تنقیح کی مشکلات کو واضح کیا گیا ہے۔ اور ان کو کھول دیا گیا ہے۔ اور ایسی کتاب کا پورا ہونا تسمیہ بالتوضیح کے لیے سبب بن سکتا ہے۔ سوال: ضمیر صرف ذات پر دلالت کرتی ہے اوصاف پر نہیں تو آپ نے اس کتاب کے اوصاف کیسے مراد لے لئے؟ جواب:۔ اوصاف ضمیر کی وجہ سے سمجھ میں نہیں آئے بلکہ قرینہ مقام کی وجہ سے سمجھ میں آئے ہیں ۔ فلا اعتراض علیہ۔
Then I named it 'Tawdih fi Hall Ghawamid al-Tanqih'. But this detail is according to the manuscript in which there is no letter 'waw' before 'sammaytu', and in some manuscripts there is 'waw', so according to that manuscript, 'wa-sammaytu' will be conjunctive, making 'ja'altuhu' the object of 'aradtuhu', and 'ja'altuhu' will be the answer to 'lamma', and it will be the result of the condition. Placing the demonstrative pronoun in place of a pronoun. 'Wad' Ism al-Ishara': This is the second part of the commentary's statement. The goal of the commentator is to repel a potential objection. Question: It is that the commentator mentioned the demonstrative pronoun in 'sammaytu hadha al-kitab'. Why did he not mention a pronoun, although this is the place for a pronoun, because generally, when a noun is mentioned once, then a pronoun refers back to it? Answer (1): The demonstrative pronoun provides greater distinction compared to a pronoun, because the demonstrative pronoun points to a specific and perceptible thing, and it indicates both essence and attributes, while a pronoun indicates only essence. So the author mentioned the demonstrative pronoun to indicate the greatness of the book, as if this book is distinguished among all books of the discipline. His statement 'fa-in qulta': 'fa-in qulta' for the question, 'qulta' for the answer. Question: The gist of the question is that after 'lamma' there is a condition and a result. And 'lamma' comes for the confirmation of the result due to the confirmation of the condition. So here the condition of 'lamma' is completion, and the result would be 'sammaytu hadha al-kitab' in meaning. Its completion is a cause for naming it 'al-Tawdih', but this is not correct because it is not necessary that the completion of the book becomes the cause for naming it 'al-Tawdih'. Answer: The gist is that the pronoun in 'itmamihi' does not refer absolutely to the book, but rather the pronoun refers to this commentary which is characterized by the mentioned attributes, in which the difficulties of al-Tanqih are clarified and explained. And the completion of such a book can be a cause for naming it 'al-Tawdih'. Question: The pronoun indicates only essence, not attributes, so how did you intend the attributes of this book? Answer: The attributes were not understood from the pronoun, but rather from the contextual clue (qarinat al-maqam). So there is no objection.
Source pages p. 117

Commentary
This passage is a commentary from the sharh explaining why the author used the demonstrative pronoun 'hadha' instead of a regular pronoun. The commentator first clarifies a textual variant regarding the word 'sammaytu' and its conjunction. He then introduces the topic of using ism al-ishara in place of a pronoun. He presents a question: why not use a pronoun (damir) since the book was already mentioned? The answer is that ism al-ishara gives greater specificity, indicating both the essence and attributes, and honors the book. A second question arises from the construction with 'lamma', asking how the completion of the book causes its naming. The commentator explains that the pronoun refers to the specific commentary that has the attributes of clarifying difficulties, and the completion of such a work is indeed a fitting cause for naming it 'al-Tawdih'. Finally, a question about how attributes are understood from a pronoun is answered by invoking the contextual clue (qarina). This is typical usul analysis of textual reasoning.

Key Terms
اسم الإشارة (ism al-ishāra): A word that points to a specific, perceptible thing, indicating both essence and attributes.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the commentator, what does ism al-ishara indicate that a regular pronoun does not?
A) Only the essence
B) Both essence and attributes
C) Only attributes
D) The book's author

Key Takeaway
In Hanafi textual analysis, the choice of ism al-ishara over a pronoun is deliberate and conveys greater distinction and specificity, affecting the legal understanding of the text.

The Principle of Idmar Qabl al-Dhikr in Hanafi Usul
Justifying the use of a pronoun without prior explicit mention when the referent is mentally present.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain the Hanafi principle that a pronoun may refer to a mentally present antecedent (madhkur fi al-dhihn) and apply this to analyze Quranic and textual examples.

Core Idea
Mental presence suffices as an antecedent — what is in the mind has legal weight.

In Hanafi usul al-fiqh, the use of a pronoun before its explicit antecedent (idmar qabl al-dhikr) is generally impermissible. However, when the referent is clearly present in the mind, the principle relaxes. This lesson unpacks the reasoning behind this exception, grounded in Quranic usage and the reality of the believer's heart.

Guided Path
1
Identify the grammatical issue
Notice that in the matn, the pronoun 'ilayhi' refers to Allah, yet Allah's name is not explicitly mentioned in the preceding text. This is a potential instance of idmar qabl al-dhikr.
The pronoun 'ilayhi' is in the phrase 'al-hamdu lillahi lalu alih'.
2
Understand the objection
A skilled questioner would object that idmar qabl al-dhikr is impermissible because a pronoun needs an explicit antecedent. This objection is based on a common linguistic rule.
Idmar qabl al-dhikr is considered a flaw in clear expression.
3
Grasp the Hanafi response
The commentator explains that the objection does not apply because Allah's remembrance is mentally present (madhkur fi al-dhihn) for every believer, especially when beginning a book. This mental presence serves as a legal antecedent.
This is a contextual and pragmatic justification, not a mere grammatical exception.
4
Analyze the Quranic evidence
The passage cites two Quranic verses: 'wa bil-haqqi anzalnahu' (17:105) and 'innahu laqur'anun karim' (56:77). In both, the pronoun refers to the Quran even though 'Quran' is not explicitly mentioned before. The basis is that the Quran is present in the reader's mind.
The pronoun 'nahu' in 'anzalnahu' and 'hu' in 'innahu' refer to the Quran without prior mention.
5
Derive the usul principle
From this, the Hanafi principle is established: what is present in the mind (madhkur fi al-dhihn) can legally serve as the antecedent of a pronoun. This is an exception to the general rule against idmar qabl al-dhikr.
This principle is applied in textual analysis and istinbat when interpreting Quran and hadith.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
تشریح قولہ انتخ۔ اس عبارت میں صاحب توضیح نے سوال مقدر کا جواب دیا ہے۔ سوال :۔ یہ ہے کہ الیہ کی ضمیر کا مرجع لفظ اللہ ہے حالانکہ اس کا ماقبل میں کوئی ذکر نہیں ۔ یہ تو اضمار قبل الذکر ہے ۔ جو کہ نا جائز ہے۔ جواب:۔ یہ ہے کہ یہاں اضار قبل الذکر لازم نہیں آتا کیونکہ اگر چہ ماقبل میں لفظ اللہ کا صراحتا کوئی ذکر نہیں ہے۔ لیکن حکماً ذکر موجود ہے۔ کیونکہ ہر مومن کے دل میں اللہ کا ذکر پایا جاتا ہے۔ خصوصا کتاب کو شروع کرتے ہوئے تو اللہ کا ذکر ضرور پایا جاتا ہے۔ ورنہ ذی بال کام کا افتتاح بے برکت ہو جائے گا۔ اور اس کی تائید و بالحق انزلناہ اور انہ لقرآن الکریم ،، سے ہو رہی ہے کیونکہ انزلناہ اور انہ میں ضمیر کا مرجع قرآن ہے لیکن ما قبل میں اس کا ذکر نہیں ۔ لیکن پڑھنے والے کے ذہن میں قرآن موجود ہوتا ہے۔ تو گویا مذکور فی الذہن کو حکما با ضمیر کا مرجع بنا دیا۔
Explanation of the statement 'Intakh' [or 'انتخ'?]. In this passage, the author of al-Tawdih has answered a presumed question. The question: The antecedent of the pronoun 'ilayhi' is the word Allah, even though there is no prior mention of it. This is idmar qabl al-dhikr (pronoun before antecedent), which is impermissible. The answer: Here idmar qabl al-dhikr is not necessary, because although the word Allah is not explicitly mentioned before, it is existent implicitly (hukman). Because the remembrance of Allah is present in the heart of every believer, especially when beginning a book, the remembrance of Allah is certainly present. Otherwise the opening of a worthwhile work would be without blessing. This is supported by the Quranic verses 'wa bil-haqqi anzalnahu' and 'innahu laqur'anun karim', where the pronoun refers to the Quran even though it is not mentioned before, but the Quran is present in the mind of the reader. So the mentally present referent is made, by legal consideration, the antecedent of the pronoun.
Source pages p. 121

Commentary
This passage addresses the grammatical and rhetorical issue of idmar qabl al-dhikr (using a pronoun before its antecedent is explicitly mentioned). In the context of the matn, the pronoun 'ilayhi' in 'al-hamdu lillahi lalu alih' refers to Allah, but Allah's name is not in the preceding text. The presumed question is that this is impermissible. The commentator responds by explaining that the rule does not apply here because Allah's remembrance is mentally present in the mind of every believer, especially at the start of a book. This is supported by Quranic examples where pronouns refer to the Quran even though 'Quran' is not explicitly mentioned before. The principle is that what is present in the mind (madhkur fi al-dhihn) can serve as the antecedent hukman (legally). This is a nuanced usul al-fiqh discussion about the permissibility of implicit references.

Key Terms
اضمار قبل الذکر (Idmar qabl al-dhikr): Using a pronoun before its antecedent is explicitly mentioned; considered impermissible unless the antecedent is mentally present.
مذکور فی الذھن (Madhkur fi al-dhihn): What is present in the mind; legally considered as an antecedent for a pronoun.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

A) Because the rule of idmar qabl al-dhikr is always invalid
B) Because Allah's name is present in the mind of the reader, especially at the start of a book
C) Because the word 'Allah' appears later in the sentence
D) Because the matn is not a serious work

Key Takeaway
Mental presence (madhkur fi al-dhihn) is a valid antecedent for a pronoun in Hanafi usul, as evidenced by Quranic usage.

Adjective for Non-Human Plural (Jam' Ghayr Dhu al-Uqul)
Resolving an apparent contradiction in the adjective of a non-human plural

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the rule that non-human plurals distinguished from their singulars by a round ta can take masculine or feminine adjectives, and apply it to resolve apparent contradictions in Quranic and fiqh texts.

Core Idea
If a non-human plural is formed by adding a round ta to its singular, both masculine and feminine adjectives are permissible.

This passage addresses a grammatical nuance often encountered in Hanafi fiqh texts: the rule that non-human plurals take feminine singular adjectives seems violated by the phrase 'al-kalim al-tayyib'. The author resolves the issue by highlighting an exception: when the plural is distinguished from its singular by a round ta (ة), the adjective can be either masculine or feminine. Quranic verses confirm this flexibility, so no contradiction exists.

Guided Path
1
Recognize the general rule
Recall that in Arabic, a non-human plural (jam' ghayr dhu al-uqul) is typically described by a feminine singular adjective.
This is a standard grammar rule.
2
Identify the exception
The passage states that if the plural is distinguished from its singular by a round ta (ة), then both masculine and feminine adjectives are allowed.
Example: nakhil (plural) vs. nakhla (singular).
3
Examine the Quranic evidence
The Quran uses both forms: 'nakhil khawiyah' (feminine) in 69:7 and 'nakhil munqa'ir' (masculine) elsewhere.
This demonstrates the permissibility.
4
Apply to the objection
Since 'al-kalim' comes from 'kalimah' (singular with round ta), its adjective can be masculine (al-tayyib) or feminine (al-tayyibah). Thus no contradiction.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قولہ الطیب :۔ اس عبارت میں سوال مقدر کا جواب دیا ہے۔ سوال:۔ ضابطہ ہے کہ جمع غیر ذوی العقول کی صفت ہمیشہ مؤنث آتی ہے۔ اب یہاں الکلم جمع غیر ذوی العقول ہے۔ تو اس کی صفت مؤنث یعنی الطیبہ آنی چاہیے۔ ماتن نے اس کی صفت مذکر یعنی الطیب کیوں ذکر کی ؟ جواب: ہر وہ جمع کہ اس کے اور اس کے واحد کے درمیان گول تا (ہ) سے فرق کیا جاتا ہو تو اس کی صفت مذکر بھی آسکتی ہے۔ اور مونث بھی۔ جیسے نخل خاویہ اس کا واحد مخلتہ ہے۔ اور قرآن میں ایک جگہ نخل خاویہ مذکور ہے اور دوسری جگہ نخل منععر صورت اول میں صفت مونث اور مصورت ثانی میں صفت مذکر ذکر کی گئی ہے۔ الہندا الکلم کی صفت الطیبہ بھی آسکتی ہے اور الطبیب بھی ۔ فلا اعتراض علیہ۔
His statement 'al-tayyib': In this phrase, the author answers a hypothetical question. The question: The rule is that the adjective of a non-human plural is always feminine. Now here 'al-kalim' is a non-human plural, so its adjective should be feminine, i.e., 'al-tayyibah'. Why did the matn author mention its adjective as masculine, i.e., 'al-tayyib'? The answer: Every plural that is distinguished from its singular by a round ta (ة) can take either a masculine or feminine adjective. For example, 'nakhil khawiyah' (hollow palm trees) its singular is 'nakhlah'. In the Quran, in one place 'nakhil khawiyah' is mentioned (with feminine adjective) and in another place 'nakhil munqa'ir' (uprooted palm trees) (with masculine adjective). In the first case the adjective is feminine, in the second masculine. So for 'al-kalim', both 'al-tayyibah' (feminine) and 'al-tayyib' (masculine) are permissible. Thus there is no objection against it.
Source pages p. 121

Commentary
This passage addresses a grammatical rule concerning adjectives for non-human plurals (جمع غیر ذوی العقول). The objection is that 'al-kalim' (the words) is a non-human plural, so its adjective should be feminine (الطیبة), but the text uses the masculine 'الطیب'. The answer explains that when a plural is distinguished from its singular by a round ta (ة) — like 'nakhl' (plural) vs. 'nakhla' (singular) — then the adjective can be either masculine or feminine. Quranic evidence is provided: in Surah Al-Haqqah (69:7) 'nakhil khawiyah' uses feminine, and in another verse 'nakhil munqa'ir' (perhaps 54:20) uses masculine. Therefore, both forms are acceptable, so there is no objection. This shows the flexibility of Arabic grammar and the importance of contextual evidence from the Quran.

Key Terms
جمع غیر ذوی العقول (jam' ghayr dhu al-uqul): A plural of non-rational beings or objects, which normally takes a feminine singular adjective.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
Why is the masculine adjective 'al-tayyib' allowed for 'al-kalim' rather than the feminine 'al-tayyibah'?
A) Because 'al-kalim' is a rational plural.
B) Because 'al-kalim' is a broken plural that does not follow the rule.
C) Because the plural is distinguished from its singular by a round ta, allowing both masculine and feminine adjectives.
D) Because the author made a grammatical error.

Key Takeaway
The adjective of a non-human plural can be masculine or feminine when the plural is formed by adding a round ta to its singular, as demonstrated by Quranic usage.

Lexical Clarification: The Meaning of 'Minsat' (منصۃ العروس)
Lexical note defining 'minsat'

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the lexical meaning of 'minsat' and explain why such clarifications are necessary in usul al-fiqh commentary.

Core Idea
Even a single unfamiliar term must be clarified for precise legal understanding.

This passage is a brief lexical note within a commentary on a usul al-fiqh text. The commentator defines the word 'minsat' (or 'minsah') which appears in the base matn. Such clarifications are essential because the precise meaning of each word affects the legal derivation. Without an accurate understanding of terms, the entire chain of reasoning can be compromised.

Guided Path
1
Identify the term being explained
Locate the word 'minsat' (منصۃ) in the passage. Notice it is part of the phrase 'minsat al-'arus'.
The term appears in the commentary, not in the matn itself.
2
State the lexical definition given
The commentator defines 'minsah' as 'the place where the bride is seated for display'. Understand this as a physical location, not an object or action.
The Arabic root n-s-w relates to women, but here it denotes a specific place.
3
Recognize the commentator's purpose
The commentator provides this definition to prevent misunderstanding. In usul al-fiqh, every word must be understood correctly before deriving rulings.
This is a typical expansion-probe: clarifying a term that might be obscure to readers.
4
Connect to the broader commentary context
Consider that this lexical note enables later legal discussions that depend on the accurate meaning of 'minsat'. Without this, the reader might misinterpret the base text.
The note is simple but serves as a foundation for subsequent analysis.

Source Text

His statement 'minsat al-'arus': In this phrase, the author presents the lexical investigation of 'minsah'. 'Minsah' refers to the place where the bride is seated for display.

It is the place where a bride is seated for people to see her. This is a simple linguistic note to aid understanding of the text being commented upon.

Gender Flexibility in Quranic Adjectives: Refuting a Linguistic Objection
Linguistic refutation of gender mismatch objection

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain why the gender of adjectives for inanimate nouns in the Quran is not a valid objection in usul al-fiqh.

Core Idea
For non-rational nouns, adjective gender is not fixed; both forms are attested.

In the study of usul al-fiqh, understanding Arabic linguistic flexibility is crucial. This passage addresses a potential objection that might be raised against the Quran's consistency: how can the same noun appear with both feminine and masculine adjectives? By examining two examples—'nakhla' (palm tree) and 'jahannam' (hell)—the author demonstrates that for inanimate objects, such variation is perfectly acceptable. This insight prevents us from mistakenly dismissing valid Quranic usages as errors.

Guided Path
1
Identify the objection
First, understand what objection is being refuted. The passage begins with 'And feminine too...' indicating someone claimed that the gender should always match.
The objection likely stems from a strict grammatical rule for animate nouns.
2
Examine the Quranic examples
Look at the two instances of 'nakhla' in the Quran: one with a feminine adjective ('khawiya') and another with a masculine adjective ('mun'afir'). Note that the Quran itself uses both.
The word 'nakhla' is grammatically feminine, yet both forms appear.
3
Extend to other nouns
The author then applies the same principle to 'jahannam' (hell), stating that both 'tayyiba' (feminine) and 'tayyib' (masculine) are acceptable.
This shows the rule applies generally to inanimate nouns.
4
Derive the usul implication
Realize that in usul, a grammatical disagreement cannot be used as an argument against the authenticity or consistency of a text. The flexibility is a feature of Arabic.
Therefore, objections based on gender mismatch are invalid.

Parsing 'Fasl al-Khitab': Resolving Grammatical Objections
Grammatical analysis and refutation of objections

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify the grammatical roles of 'fasl' and 'khitab' in the construct 'fasl al-khitab' and explain why the two objections against its validity are resolved by interpreting 'fasl' as an active participle.

Core Idea
Understanding 'fasl' as an active participle rather than a verbal noun resolves the grammatical tension in the phrase 'fasl al-khitab'.

In this passage, the author of the commentary addresses two grammatical objections to the phrase 'fasl al-khitab'. Both objections arise from misidentifying the morphological form of 'fasl' – one treats it as a masdar (verbal noun) and the other as a pure attribute. By showing that 'fasl' is an ism fa'il (active participle) meaning 'separator', the author demonstrates that the predication is grammatically sound. This lesson walks through the reasoning step by step, sharpening your ability to analyze Arabic grammatical structures in legal texts.

Guided Path
1
Identify the two objections
The passage presents two distinct grammatical critiques of 'fasl al-khitab'. The first argues that it forces an attribute (masdar) to be predicated on a substance. The second argues that both terms are masdars and their meanings are not identical externally, making attribute predication invalid.
Both objections rely on a misreading of 'fasl' as a masdar.
2
Analyze the author's response to the first objection
The author clarifies that 'fasl' is built on the pattern of tafa'ul, which is an ism fa'il (active participle). An ism fa'il denotes a substance together with an attribute. Predicating a substance-with-attribute on a substance (khitab) is grammatically correct.
The key is the morphological form: 'fasl' is not a masdar but an active participle.
3
Analyze the author's response to the second objection
Even if both words were masdars, the objection would only hold if 'fasl' were used in its masdar sense. Here, it is used as an ism fa'il, so the problem of non-identical meanings does not arise.
The author emphasizes that the usage determines the grammatical category.
4
Synthesize the conclusion
The phrase 'fasl al-khitab' is valid because 'fasl' is an active participle meaning 'separator', making the construct a straightforward noun-adjective idafa. Neither objection stands.
This analysis highlights the importance of accurate morphological parsing in understanding legal terminology.

Source Text

We say that here 'fasl' is ism fa'il and means 'separator between truth and falsehood'. In summary, this is not of the category of predication of attribute on attribute, requiring identity of meaning externally.
Source pages p. 122

Commentary
This passage is a grammatical analysis of the construct 'fasl al-khitab' found in the text. The author addresses two potential objections. The first objection: if 'fasl' is an adjective (masdar) and 'khitab' is the described noun (musnad ilayh), then predicating an attribute on a substance is problematic. The answer: 'fasl' is actually an ism fa'il (active participle), which denotes a substance with an attribute, so predication on a substance works. The second objection: if both are masdars, then attribute predication requires identity of meaning. The answer: 'fasl' here is used as ism fa'il, not masdar, so the objection doesn't apply.

Key Terms
فصل الخطاب (fasl al-khitab): the decisive speech; here parsed as 'al-khitab al-fasil' (the separating speech)
مصدر (masdar): verbal noun denoting an action or attribute
اسم فاعل (ism fa'il): active participle denoting the doer of an action
حمل الصفت علی الصفت (haml al-sifah 'ala al-sifah): predicating an attribute on another attribute

D) Because the pattern tafa'ul always indicates an active participle.

Correct morphological analysis of 'fasl' as an ism fa'il resolves grammatical objections and validates the phrase 'fasl al-khitab'.

The Art of Iqtibas in Hanafi Scholarly Openings
Commentary on the matn's unique opening with subtle Quranic quotation

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to define iqtibas (subtle quotation) in the Hanafi tradition and explain its rhetorical and pedagogical purpose as demonstrated by the commentator.

Core Idea
Iqtibas is the artful embedding of Quranic text into one's own speech to convey layered meaning and invoke authority.

In this brief passage, the commentator praises the matn author's unique opening by noting that it contains a 'subtle quotation' (iqtibas latif) of Quran 35:10. This technique is not mere decoration; it carries deep signals about intention, divine remembrance, and the orientation of the scholar. Let us unpack how the commentator reads this opening and what iqtibas means in the Hanafi scholarly tradition.

Guided Path
1
Identify the matn's opening
Recognize that the matn begins with the phrase 'ila yas'adu al-kalim al-tayyib', which alludes to Quran 35:10. Note it as an iqtibas.
2
Understand the commentator's praise
The commentator calls the opening 'gharib' (strange/unprecedented) and highlights the iqtibas as 'latif' (subtle), pointing to its layered meanings.
The commentator is pointing out a rhetorical excellence, not a defect.
3
Define iqtibas from the passage
Iqtibas is defined as incorporating a Quranic verse, hadith, or poetry into one's own speech so seamlessly that the audience thinks it is the author's own words.
This is a permissible and valued rhetorical device in Islamic scholarship.
4
Analyze the subtle meanings (latafah)
The commentator extracts three subtle indications: divine remembrance in every heart, Allah as sole object of praise, and the scholar's intention must be solely for Allah's pleasure.
The iqtibas is not arbitrary; it carries pedagogical and spiritual messages.

Resolving the Pronoun Antecedent Problem: Dhikr fi al-Dhihn
Commentator's response to pronoun-antecedent issue

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to apply the Hanafi usul principle of 'dhikr fi al-dhihn' to resolve apparent pronoun-antecedent violations in legal texts and explain its basis.

Core Idea
A pronoun before its antecedent is valid when the referent is mentally present — dhikr fi al-dhihn.

In this passage, the commentator tackles a subtle grammatical challenge: the opening phrase 'ila hi' uses a pronoun whose referent ('Allah') has not been explicitly stated. How can this be acceptable? The answer lies in a key usul principle: that which is firmly in the mind (madhkur fi al-dhihn) can serve as a referent. This lesson unpacks the three justifications and their common foundation in a principle that bridges language, theology, and legal reasoning.

Guided Path
1
Identify the grammatical rule
Recognize that Arabic grammar generally forbids using a pronoun before its antecedent (idmar qabl adh-dhikr). Understand why this is considered problematic.
The rule exists to avoid ambiguity.
2
Spot the apparent violation
In the text 'ila hi yas'adu al-kalim al-tayyib', the pronoun 'hi' appears without a previously mentioned noun like 'Allah'. This triggers the issue.
The pronoun is part of a Qur'anic quote, but the textual context omits the explicit antecedent.
3
Understand the proposed solution
The commentator introduces the concept of 'mental presence' (dhikr fi al-dhihn): if the referent is firmly established in the mind, the prohibition does not apply.
This is a recognized exception in Hanafi usul.
4
Analyze the three justifications
Each justification rephrases the same idea: (1) Allah's remembrance is always in a believer's heart, (2) Allah's essence is determined for praise, (3) the author's intention is solely Allah. All point to mental presence.
The outcome of each is identical: the pronoun is valid.
5
Synthesize the principle
Conclude that the common basis is 'madhkur fi al-dhihn'. This shows how linguistic rules in usul accommodate theological and contextual clarity.
This principle appears in other chapters of usul, e.g., interpreting vague expressions.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
اضمار قبل الذکر کے لزوم کی توجیہات قولہ اتی با تضمیر : یہ شرح کی عبارت کا دوسرا حصہ ہے۔ غرض شاریخ ایک سوال مقدر کا جواب دینا ہے۔ سوال: الیہ کی ضمیر کا مرجع لفظ اللہ ہے۔ اور یہ ماقبل میں نہ صر احسان کور ہے اور نہ ضمنا اس میں اضمار قبل الذکر لازم آتا ہے۔ جو کہ نا جائز ہے۔ جواب (۱):۔ ہر مومن کے دل میں اللہ کا ذکر موجود ہوتا ہے۔ خصوصاً کتاب کو شروع کرتے وقت تا کہ کتاب کی ابتداء شرعیت کی نگاہ میں اجزم اور بے برکت نہ ہو جائے تو گویا مذکور فی الذہن کو حکما ضمیر کا مرجع بنادیا گیا۔ لہذا اضمار قبل الذکر لازم نہیں آتا۔ جواب (۲):۔ الیہ يصعد الكلم الطبیب سے ماتن اللہ کی حمد بیان کرتے ہیں۔ اور جمیع محامد کا متوجہ الیہ بننے کے لیے اللہ کی ذات متعین ہے۔ جب اللہ کی ذات ذہنوں میں متعین ہے۔ تو اس کو ضمیر کا مرجع بنا دیا۔ جواب (۳) علوم اسلامیہ کو شروع کرنے والے کا طمح نظر اللہ کی رضا ہوتی ہے۔ اور اللہ کے سواوہ کسی کی طرف متوجہ نہیں ہوتا۔ جب خدا کی ذات شارع فی العلوم کے ذہن میں متعین ہے۔ تو الیہ کی ضمیر ک مرجع اس کو بنایا دیا گیا۔ ان جوابوں کا مآل ایک ہی ہے۔
Explanations for the necessity of pronoun before antecedent. His statement 'ati bi tadmir': This is the second part of the commentary's expression. Purpose: The commentator is answering a hypothetical question. Question: The antecedent of the pronoun 'ila' is the word 'Allah'. And this is neither explicitly nor implicitly mentioned before. So it necessitates 'idmar qabl adh-dhikr' (using a pronoun before mentioning its referent), which is not permissible. Answer 1: The remembrance of Allah is present in every believer's heart, especially when beginning a book, so that the beginning of the book is not devoid of blessing in the view of Shariah. Thus, what is mentally present is regarded as the referent of the pronoun. Hence, there is no impermissible pronoun-before-antecedent. Answer 2: By 'ila yas'adu al-kalim al-tayyib' the author is praising Allah, and for directing all praises to Him, Allah's essence is determined. When Allah's essence is determined in minds, He is made the referent of the pronoun. Answer 3: The one who begins Islamic sciences has his sight set on Allah's pleasure, and he does not turn to anyone other than Allah. When Allah's essence is determined in the mind of the book's author, the pronoun's referent is made Him. The outcome of these answers is the same.

Commentary
This is a discussion about a grammatical and rhetorical issue: the pronoun 'hi' in 'ila hi' appears before the explicit mention of 'Allah' (since the book begins with 'ila yas'adu...' without previous mention of 'Allah'). Classical Arabic grammar generally forbids using a pronoun before its antecedent is mentioned. The commentator offers three justifications, all based on the principle of 'dhikr fi al-dhihn' (mental presence): Since Allah is firmly established in the believer's mind, especially at the start of a religious work, the pronoun is valid. The three answers converge on the same idea: the intended referent is mentally present, so the prohibition does not apply. This reflects the usul principle that linguistic rules can account for context and shared knowledge.

Key Terms
اضمار قبل الذكر (idmar qabl adh-dhikr): Using a pronoun before mentioning its actual referent, considered impermissible in normal Arabic usage
مذکور فی الذہن (madhkur fi al-dhihn): Something that is already firmly present in the mind, so it can serve as a referent for a pronoun without explicit mention

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi usul principle of mental presence (dhikr fi al-dhihn) justifies the use of a pronoun before its explicit antecedent when the referent is firmly established in the mind, bridging language and context.

Clarifying the Opening Word 'Ati'
Addressing an objection about starting with a pronoun

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain how the commentator resolves the objection that the book starts with a pronoun by identifying the role of 'ati' as indicating the pronoun is brought later.

Core Idea
The word 'ati' shows the pronoun is brought later, resolving the grammatical objection.

This lesson addresses a grammatical objection raised against the opening of a classical text. The author appears to start with a preposition, not a pronoun, yet the phrase 'bi al-damir' suggests a pronoun is present. The commentator uses the word 'ati' to clarify the intended construction, demonstrating a key skill in interpreting legal texts: supplying missing elements to resolve apparent inconsistencies.

Guided Path
1
Identify the objection
The objection claims that the book begins with a pronoun because the phrase 'bi al-damir' (with the pronoun) appears early, but pronouns must have a clear antecedent before them.
The objection is that the author violated the rule that a pronoun cannot come before its referent.
2
Understand the commentator's response
The commentator states that the objection only arises if the prepositional phrase is directly attached to the opening verb. He says it is actually related to a hidden word 'ityan' (bringing).
The full phrase is reconstructed as 'iftaH al-kitaba ityanan bi al-damir' (I opened the book, bringing the pronoun).
3
See how 'ati' functions
The word 'ati' (having come with) signals that the pronoun is brought later, not before its antecedent. This resolves the objection because the pronoun's referent (the book) is already mentioned in the opening word 'iftaH'.
'Ati' serves as a cue for the reader to supply the missing word 'ityan'.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قولہ اتی:- شارع نے لفظ اتی کہہ کر ایک سوال کے جواب کی طرف اشارہ کیا ہے۔ سوال:۔ ماتن نے افتح کا لفظ ذکر کیا ہے۔ اس سے یہ سمجھ میں آتا ہے کہ کتاب کو ضمیر کے ساتھ شروع کیا ہے۔ حالانکہ ضمیر سے شروع نہیں کیا۔ بلکہ حرف جار سے شروع کیا ہے۔ جواب :۔ تو شاریخ نے اس کے جواب کی طرف اشارہ کیا کہ یہ اعتراض تو تب لازم آئے گا۔ کہ لفظ بالضمیر میں جار مجرور افتح سے متعلق ہو ۔ ہم کہتے ہیں کہ اس کا متعلق امتیان ہے۔ اصل عبارت یوں ہے۔ افتح الكتاب اتیا نا بالضمیر ۔ اب معنی ہوگا مصنف نے کتاب کو شروع کیا۔ ضمیر کو مرجع سے پہلے لاتے ہوئے لہذا اس صورت میں کوئی اعتراض وارد نہیں ہو گا۔
His statement 'ati': The commentator indicated by the word 'ati' an answer to a question. Question: The author mentioned the word 'iftaH'. This gives the impression that he started the book with a pronoun, although he did not start with a pronoun but with a preposition. Answer: The commentator indicated its answer by saying that this objection would arise if the prepositional phrase 'bi al-damir' (with the pronoun) were related to 'iftaH'. We say that its relationship is to 'imtiyan' (or 'ityan'? coming). The original expression is: 'iftaH al-kitaba ityanan bi al-damir' (I opened the book, bringing the pronoun). Now the meaning becomes: The author started the book while bringing the pronoun before its antecedent. Thus, in this case no objection arises.
Source pages p. 127

Commentary
This segment clarifies a potential grammatical objection. The author's phrase 'la yuqal' (page 127) discusses a question: the author began with a preposition, not a pronoun, so why assume pronoun before antecedent? The commentator explains that the word 'ati' (having come with) indicates that the phrase should be understood as 'iftaH al-kitaba ityanan bi al-damir' (I open the book bringing the pronoun). Thus, the pronoun 'hi' is actually part of a later phrase, not attached to the opening verb. The objection disappears because the pronoun is not truly before its antecedent; the word 'ati' shows it is brought later in the intended structure. This shows careful attention to linguistic details in legal texts.

Key Terms
اتی (ati): An Arabic word meaning 'bring' or 'come with', used here as a verbal noun (ityan) indicating the manner of opening

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

Key Takeaway

Core Idea
Mahamid is a plural of mahmada, a verbal noun meaning praise — its linguistic form confirms its suitability for legal usage.

In the study of usul al-fiqh, precise lexical definitions are the bedrock of sound legal interpretation. This lesson unpacks the term 'mahamid' as used in Hanafi texts, showing its singular form, morphological pattern, and how this nuance matters for understanding legal language.

2

Mahamid is a plural. Determine its singular: mahmada.
3
Determine the morphological pattern
Mahmada is a masdar mimi (verbal noun beginning with mīm), equivalent in meaning to hamd.
4
Relate to the root meaning
The root ḥ-m-d gives the core meaning of praise. The masdar mimi emphasizes the action's occurrence.

Distinguishing Hamd and Shukr
Distinguishing hamd from shukr in scope and medium

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to distinguish between ḥamd and shukr by analyzing their scope in medium and occasion, and explain why the author chose ḥamd in the matn.

Core Idea
Ḥamd is verbal praise for any good; shukr is gratitude for a favor, expressed by heart, tongue, and limbs.

In the opening of the matn, the author begins with 'al-ḥamd'. The commentator now explains why he did not use 'al-shukr', by defining and contrasting both terms. Understanding this distinction is crucial for grasping the precise legal connotation of praise in Islamic texts.

Guided Path
1
Identify the two terms being compared
The passage explicitly compares ḥamd and shukr. Locate these terms in the Arabic text.
2
Extract the definition of ḥamd
Find what the commentator says about ḥamd: its medium (only tongue) and its occasion (any quality, favor or not).
Hint: look for 'حمد: کہتے ہیں کسی خوبی پر زبان سے تعریف'
3
Extract the definition of shukr
Find what the commentator says about shukr: its medium (tongue, heart, limbs) and its occasion (only for a favor).
Look for 'شکر کہتے ہیں احسان کے بدلہ میں تعریف کرنا'
4
Compare the two definitions on two axes: medium and occasion
Notice the inverse relationship: ḥamd is specific in medium, general in occasion; shukr is general in medium, specific in occasion.
Use the summary statement: 'محمد مورد کے اعتبار سے خاص ہے زبان کے ساتھ اور متعلق کے اعتبار سے عام ہے'
5
Explain the author's choice of ḥamd
The matn praises Allah unconditionally; ḥamd is more suitable because it does not require a prior favor, unlike shukr.
This connects the distinction to the author's intent.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وهو مقابلہ :۔ یہ عبارت کا پانچواں حصہ ہے۔ اس عبارت میں شاریخ نے حمد و شکر میں فرق بیان کیا ہے۔ حمد : کہتے ہیں کسی خوبی پر زبان سے تعریف و عظمت بیان کرنا چاہے احسان کے بدلہ میں ہو یا نہ ہواور شکر کہتے ہیں احسان کے بدلہ میں تعریف کرنا آگے عام ہے کہ زبان سے ہو یا دل تہ سے ہو یا اعضاء سے ہو ۔ خلاصہ یہ ہے کہ محمد مورد کے اعتبار سے خاص ہے زبان کے ساتھ اور متعلق کے اعتبار سے عام ہے احسان کے بدلہ میں ہو یا نہ ہو۔ اور شکر اس کے برعکس ہے یعنی مورد کے اعتبار سے عام ہے کہ زبان سے ہو بادل سے ہو یا اعضاء سے ہو۔ اور متعلق کے اعتبار سے خاص ہے کہ احسان کے بدلہ میں ہو۔
And he is muqābala: This is the fifth part of the expression. In this expression, the commentator explains the difference between hamd and shukr. Hamd: it is said that it is expressing praise and glorification with the tongue for a quality, whether in return for a favor or not. And shukr: it is said that it is praising in return for a favor, and it is general whether with the tongue, the heart, or the limbs. The summary is that mahmada [hamd] is specific in locus (with the tongue) and general in relation (whether for favor or not). And shukr is the opposite: general in locus (tongue, heart, limbs) and specific in relation (only for favor).
Source pages p. 135

Commentary
This passage clarifies the distinction between hamd and shukr. Hamd is praise for intrinsic goodness, expressed verbally, regardless of whether a favor prompted it. Shukr is gratitude expressed in return for a favor, and it can be done by tongue, heart, or limbs. Therefore, hamd is narrower in medium (only tongue) but broader in reason (any good). Shukr is broader in medium but narrower in reason (only favors). This distinction is important for understanding why the author used hamd in the matn.

Key Terms
حمد (ḥamd): Praise for a quality regardless of favor, expressed with the tongue.
شکر (shukr): Gratitude for a favor, expressed by tongue, heart, or limbs.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

A) Hamd is general in medium; shukr is specific
B) Hamd is only for favors; shukr for any good
C) Hamd is specific to tongue; shukr includes heart and limbs
D) Hamd includes limbs; shukr only tongue

Key Takeaway
The distinction between ḥamd and shukr lies in their scope: ḥamd is restricted to the tongue but general in occasion, while shukr is general in medium but restricted to favors.

Learning Objective

Core Idea
Shari'a literally means a path to water; Islamic law is the path to spiritual and moral life.

This brief passage examines the literal meaning of the word 'mashari'', which is key to understanding the term 'shari'a'. In usul al-fiqh, knowing the lexical origin of technical terms helps uncover the wisdom behind legal concepts. The commentator here highlights that mashari' are watering places where the thirsty gather—a vivid image that shapes the metaphor of Islamic law as a life-giving path.

Guided Path
1

The technical meaning in usul is a divinely revealed law, but the lexical root conveys guidance to salvation.
3
Understand the usul significance
Reflect on why usul scholars discuss lexical meanings. They ground technical terms in their linguistic origins to ensure precision and to derive rulings from the broadest possible understanding of Quranic and hadith terms.
This lexical investigation appears in commentaries on al-Tawdih wa al-Talwih.
